Divine Decree

The Debate with al-Jubba'i on Predestination
Al-Ash'ari refutes Mu'tazili qadar via a logical dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari's logical argument refutes the Mu'tazili doctrine of divine justice (qadar) by exposing its inconsistency.

Core Idea
God's absolute sovereignty cannot be limited by human notions of justice.

This lesson presents a famous debate between al-Ash'ari and his Mu'tazili teacher al-Jubba'i. Through a simple scenario of three brothers with different fates, al-Ash'ari exposes a fatal flaw in the Mu'tazili claim that God must always act in a certain way. Read on to see how logic itself defends Ash'ari orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Read the debate scenario
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the setup: three brothers with different lives and deaths.
Pay attention to al-Jubba'i's initial classification of their fates.
2
Follow the dialectical exchange
Trace al-Ash'ari's three questions and al-Jubba'i's responses. Identify how each question pushes al-Jubba'i into a corner.
The final question is the decisive blow.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider Ibn al-'Imad's commentary: the debate proves God's absolute sovereignty. Ask yourself why al-Jubba'i could not answer the final question.
This connects to the core idea of the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سأل أبو الحسن الأشعري أستاذه أبا علي الجبائي على ثلاثة أخوة ، كان أحدهم مؤمناً براً تقياً . والثاني كان كافراً فاسقاً شقياً ، والثالث كان صغيراً ، فماتوا فكيف حالهم ؟ فقال الجبائي : أما الزاهد ففي الدرجات ، وأما الكافر ففي الدركات ، وأما الصغير فمن أهل السلامة . فقال الأشعري : إن أراد الصغير أن يذهب إلى درجات الزاهد هل يؤذن له ؟ فقال الجبائي : لا !! لأنه يقال له : أخوك إنما وصل إلى هذه الدرجات بطاعاته الكثيرة وليس لك تلك الطاعات ، فقال الأشعري : فإن قال ذلك التقصير ليس مني ، فإنك ما أبقيتني ما أقدرتني على الطاعة ، الجبائي : يقول الباري جل وعلا : كنت أعلم لو بقيت لعصيت وصرت مستحقاً للعذاب الأليم فراعيت مصلحتك ، فقال الأشعري : فلو قال الأخ الأكبر يا إله العالمين كما علمت حاله فقد علمت حالي، فلم راعيت مصلحته دوني فانقطع الجبائي . وقال ابن العماد : « وفي هذه المناظرة دلالة على أن الله تعالى خص من شاء برحمته واختص آخر بعذابه » . اهـ .
Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari asked his teacher Abu 'Ali al-Jubba'i about three brothers: one of them was a believing, pious, God-fearing man; the second was a disbelieving, immoral, wretched man; and the third was a child. They died: what are their states? Al-Jubba'i said: 'As for the ascetic, he is in the highest ranks; as for the disbeliever, he is in the lowest ranks; and as for the child, he is among the people of safety.' Al-Ash'ari said: 'If the child wants to go to the ranks of the ascetic, will he be allowed?' Al-Jubba'i said: 'No! Because it will be said to him: Your brother only reached these ranks through his many acts of obedience, and you do not have those acts of obedience.' Al-Ash'ari said: 'If he says: That deficiency is not from me—You, (O Lord) did not keep me alive and enable me to obey?' Al-Jubba'i said: 'The Exalted and Glorious Creator says: I knew that if you had remained (alive) you would have disobeyed and become deserving of painful punishment, so I looked after your welfare.' Al-Ash'ari said: 'Then what if the elder brother says: O God of the worlds, just as You knew his state, You knew my state—so why did You look after his welfare and not mine?' So al-Jubba'i was silenced. And Ibn al-'Imad said: 'In this debate is an indication that Allah the Exalted selects whom He wills for His mercy and singles out another for His punishment.' End.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is a famous debate between al-Ash'ari and his Mu'tazili teacher al-Jubba'i, demonstrating the flaw in the Mu'tazili doctrine of divine justice (qadar). The debate proceeds in steps: First, al-Ash'ari presents the scenario of three brothers with different fates—a pious believer in paradise, a disbeliever in hell, and a child in a safe state. Al-Jubba'i's Mu'tazili answer assigns each accordingly. Second, al-Ash'ari asks if the child can aspire to the believer's rank; al-Jubba'i says no, because the believer earned his rank through obedience. Third, al-Ash'ari points out that the child did not have the chance to obey because God did not keep him alive—so it is not the child's fault. Al-Jubba'i replies that God knew that if the child had lived, he would have disobeyed and deserved punishment, so God mercifully took him early. Fourth, al-Ash'ari turns the argument: if God knew the believer would obey and the child would disobey, then God also knew the believer's fate; why then did God not let the believer die early as well to spare him from potential sin? Al-Jubba'i is silenced, unable to reconcile God's selective mercy. Ibn al-'Imad concludes that the debate proves God's absolute sovereignty: He grants mercy to whom He wills and punishes whom He wills.

Key Terms
الدرجات
الدركات
الجبائي
الاعتزال
المناظرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The debate questions God's justice or suggests He is unfair.
Correction: The debate actually refutes the Mu'tazili claim that God must act in a certain way; it affirms God's absolute sovereignty and wisdom.

Checkpoint
Why did al-Jubba'i say the child cannot reach the ascetic's ranks?
A) Because the child was sinful.
B) Because the child did not perform any acts of obedience.
C) Because God predestined him for hell.
D) Because the child was too young to understand.

Key Takeaway
This debate demonstrates that God's mercy and justice are not bound by human reasoning; He does as He wills, and His wisdom is beyond our comprehension.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were the believing brother in this debate, how would you respond to God's choice to spare the child but not you? Are you truly content with God's decree, even when His wisdom is hidden from you?
?
This debate shows that God's mercy is not earned but given by His will. How does this truth humble you? Do you live as if your good deeds guarantee paradise, or do you rely solely on God's mercy?
?
Al-Ash'ari's questioning exposed a contradiction in al-Jubba'i's logic. In your own life, when has your understanding of God's justice been challenged? Are you willing to submit to God's wisdom even when it doesn't align with your sense of fairness?

Divine Decree

Allah's Will in Guidance and Misguidance
Al-Ash'ari affirms Allah's will in guidance and misguidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah guides whom He wills and leads astray whom He wills, and that His ability to guide all is not constrained, but His will determines destiny.

Core Idea
Allah's will is sovereign over guidance and misguidance; He is able but wills otherwise.

This passage from Imam al-Ash'ari's *Al-Ibanah* addresses one of the most profound questions of faith: why does Allah guide some and not others? Al-Ash'ari refutes the claim that Allah would have guided everyone if He had been kind, affirming that Allah wills both guidance and misguidance according to His eternal knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the repeated emphasis on Allah's ability and will.
2
Identify the two groups and Allah's actions
The passage contrasts believers and disbelievers. Note what Allah does for each group: guidance, success, kindness for believers; abandonment and sealing of hearts for disbelievers.
The claim of deviant sects is mentioned, so identify it.
3
Understand the refutation
Al-Ash'ari refutes the idea that Allah would have guided all if He had been kind. He states that Allah is fully able but willed otherwise. This is the core theological point.
This guards against the misconception that Allah is powerless.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا في كتاب الله كثير ، وأن الله وفق المؤمنين لطاعته ولطف بهم ونظر لهم وأصلحهم وهداهم وأضل الكافرين ولم يهدهم ولم يلطف بهم بالآيات كزعم أهل الزيغ والطغيان ولو لطف بهم وأصلحهم لكانوا مهتدين وأن الله يقدر أن يصلح الكافرين ويلطف بهم حتى يكونوا مؤمنين ولكنه أراد أن يكونوا كافرين كما علم ، وخذلهم وطبع على قلوبهم . وأن الخير والشر بقضاء الله وقدره ، وإنا نؤمن بقضاء الله وقدره خيره وشره حلوه ومره ، ونعلم أن ما أخطأنا لم يكن ليصيبنا ، وأن ما أصابنا لم يكن ليخطئنا . ونلجئ في أمورنا إلى الله ونثبت الحاجة والفقر في كل وقت إليه .
And this is plentiful in the Book of Allah: that Allah granted success to the believers for His obedience, and was kind to them, and looked upon them, and set them right, and guided them; and He led astray the disbelievers and did not guide them, and was not kind to them through the signs, as the people of deviation and transgression claim; and if He had been kind to them and set them right, they would have been guided; and that Allah is able to set the disbelievers right and be kind to them so that they would be believers, but He willed that they be disbelievers, as He knew; and He abandoned them and sealed their hearts. And that good and evil are by Allah's decree and predestination; and we believe in Allah's decree and predestination, its good and its evil, its sweet and its bitter; and we know that what missed us was not to hit us, and what hit us was not to miss us. And we entrust our affairs to Allah and affirm need and poverty to Him at every time.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a creedal statement on divine will and predestination (qadr). It begins by affirming that the following beliefs are abundant in the Quran: that Allah granted success and guidance to believers, and led astray the disbelievers—not because He was incapable, but because He willed it. The author refutes the claims of deviant sects that say Allah would have guided everyone if He had been kind. Ash'ari states that Allah is fully able to guide the disbelievers, but He willed them to be disbelievers, as He knew eternally. Then the passage affirms that all good and evil occur by Allah's decree and predestination (qadā' and qadar). The believer accepts both the pleasant and unpleasant aspects of destiny. Next, it echoes the hadith: 'What missed you was not to hit you, and what hit you was not to miss you,' emphasizing that everything happens by Allah's precise measure. Finally, the passage concludes by stating that believers entrust their affairs to Allah and constantly acknowledge their need and poverty before Him, which is the proper response to belief in qadr—not fatalism, but reliance on Allah.

Key Terms
هدى
أضل
خذلان
طبع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Allah is unable to guide disbelievers or that He would have guided everyone if He had been kind.
Correction: The passage affirms that Allah is fully able to guide the disbelievers, but He wills them to be disbelievers as He knew.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why are disbelievers not guided?
A) Allah cannot guide them.
B) Allah wills them to be disbelievers.
C) They rejected guidance on their own.
D) Allah is unable to be kind to them.

Key Takeaway
Allah's will is decisive; He guides and leads astray according to His eternal knowledge and will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah could have guided you to a stronger faith but may have willed your current state, how will you humble yourself today and beg Him for steadfastness?
?
When you see a disbeliever, do you recognize that Allah is able to guide them yet wills otherwise, and how does that deepen your awe of His sovereignty?
?
Knowing that Allah abandons and seals hearts, what sin in your life might be hardening your heart, and what immediate step will you take to repent before it is sealed?

Belief in Qadr and Reliance on Allah
Al-Ash'ari affirms the comprehensive nature of qadr and the believer's response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all good and evil occur by Allah's decree, and that true belief in qadr leads to entrusting one's affairs to Allah.

Core Idea
Faith in qadr means accepting both good and bad as from Allah, and responding with trust and reliance.

Having addressed divine will in guidance and misguidance, al-Ash'ari now turns to the broader principle of qadr (divine decree). He affirms that everything—good and evil, sweet and bitter—is by Allah's decree. This belief does not lead to fatalism; rather, it drives the believer to entrust all matters to Allah and to acknowledge constant need of Him.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the clear statement that all good and evil are from Allah's decree.
The wording includes both 'qada' and 'qadar'.
2
Understand the comprehensive nature of qadr
The passage affirms belief in both good and evil, sweet and bitter aspects of destiny. This covers all life events.
This is a key article of Sunni creed.
3
Identify the practical response
The passage concludes with entrusting affairs to Allah and affirming need and poverty to Him at all times. This is the proper response to belief in qadr.
Contrast with fatalism: reliance, not passivity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا في كتاب الله كثير ، وأن الله وفق المؤمنين لطاعته ولطف بهم ونظر لهم وأصلحهم وهداهم وأضل الكافرين ولم يهدهم ولم يلطف بهم بالآيات كزعم أهل الزيغ والطغيان ولو لطف بهم وأصلحهم لكانوا مهتدين وأن الله يقدر أن يصلح الكافرين ويلطف بهم حتى يكونوا مؤمنين ولكنه أراد أن يكونوا كافرين كما علم ، وخذلهم وطبع على قلوبهم . وأن الخير والشر بقضاء الله وقدره ، وإنا نؤمن بقضاء الله وقدره خيره وشره حلوه ومره ، ونعلم أن ما أخطأنا لم يكن ليصيبنا ، وأن ما أصابنا لم يكن ليخطئنا . ونلجئ في أمورنا إلى الله ونثبت الحاجة والفقر في كل وقت إليه .
And this is plentiful in the Book of Allah: that Allah granted success to the believers for His obedience, and was kind to them, and looked upon them, and set them right, and guided them; and He led astray the disbelievers and did not guide them, and was not kind to them through the signs, as the people of deviation and transgression claim; and if He had been kind to them and set them right, they would have been guided; and that Allah is able to set the disbelievers right and be kind to them so that they would be believers, but He willed that they be disbelievers, as He knew; and He abandoned them and sealed their hearts. And that good and evil are by Allah's decree and predestination; and we believe in Allah's decree and predestination, its good and its evil, its sweet and its bitter; and we know that what missed us was not to hit us, and what hit us was not to miss us. And we entrust our affairs to Allah and affirm need and poverty to Him at every time.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a creedal statement on divine will and predestination (qadr). It begins by affirming that the following beliefs are abundant in the Quran: that Allah granted success and guidance to believers, and led astray the disbelievers—not because He was incapable, but because He willed it. The author refutes the claims of deviant sects that say Allah would have guided everyone if He had been kind. Ash'ari states that Allah is fully able to guide the disbelievers, but He willed them to be disbelievers, as He knew eternally. Then the passage affirms that all good and evil occur by Allah's decree and predestination (qadā' and qadar). The believer accepts both the pleasant and unpleasant aspects of destiny. Next, it echoes the hadith: 'What missed you was not to hit you, and what hit you was not to miss you,' emphasizing that everything happens by Allah's precise measure. Finally, the passage concludes by stating that believers entrust their affairs to Allah and constantly acknowledge their need and poverty before Him, which is the proper response to belief in qadr—not fatalism, but reliance on Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think belief in qadr leads to fatalism and passivity.
Correction: The passage shows that belief in qadr leads to reliance on Allah and constant acknowledgment of need, not inaction.

Checkpoint
What is the believer's response to belief in qadr according to this passage?
A) Fatalism and resignation.
B) Entrusting affairs to Allah and acknowledging need.
C) Despair and hopelessness.
D) Inaction and passivity.

Key Takeaway
Believing that everything is by Allah's decree leads to reliance on Him and acknowledgment of our constant need.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When something bitter happens to you—a loss, a disappointment, a trial—do you truly believe it is from Allah's decree with the same certainty you have for blessings? What would it take to train your heart to accept both sweet and bitter as equally from Him starting today?
?
The hadith says: 'What missed you was not to hit you, and what hit you was not to miss you.' Is there a past regret or a 'what if' that you still carry? Will you deliberately release it to Allah's decree right now, and trust that His measure was exact?
?
You say you rely on Allah, but do you live as if your own plans, efforts, and resources are sufficient? How would your actions change if you constantly affirmed your absolute need and poverty before Allah every hour? Write one concrete change you will make today to embody that reliance.

The Qadariyya Accused of Dualism
Al-Ash'ari accuses the Qadariyya of dualistic belief in creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's accusation that the Qadariyya's belief in human creation of evil mirrors Zoroastrian dualism and why this is a grave theological error.

Core Idea
The Qadariyya's belief in human creation of evil mirrors Zoroastrian dualism.

Al-Ash'ari levels a severe charge against the Qadariyya: by affirming that servants create evil, they inadvertently adopt a dualistic framework akin to the Magians (Zoroastrians), who believed in two independent creators—one of good and one of evil. This introduction sets up the comparison and its doctrinal stakes.

Guided Path
1
Read the accusation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation carefully. Notice the terms 'يخلقون الشر' (they create evil) and 'المجوس' (the Magians).
The passage is short but packed with a strong comparison.
2
Identify the comparison
Identify the analogy al-Ash'ari draws between the Qadariyya and the Magians. The Magians believed in two creators: one for good, one for evil. The Qadariyya claim Allah creates good but servants and Satan create evil.
3
Understand the theological problem
Reflect on why this comparison is so damning. If the Qadariyya assign the creation of evil to beings other than Allah, they limit Allah's exclusive sovereignty and introduce a rival to His power—a form of shirk.
Al-Ash'ari is attacking the core of Qadariyya belief.
4
Consider the implication for human responsibility
Think about how the Qadariyya might defend themselves: they want to preserve human moral responsibility. But al-Ash'ari argues that their solution leads to a dualistic universe, which is unacceptable in Islamic monotheism.
5
Take the checkpoint
Answer the multiple-choice question to test your understanding of the passage's main point.
The question asks who al-Ash'ari compares the Qadariyya to.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأثبتوا وأيقنوا أن العباد يخلقون الشر، نظيراً لقول المجوس الذين أثبتوا خالقين: أحدهما يخلق الخير، والآخر يخلق الشر. وزعمت القدرية أن الله عز وجل يَخْلُقُ الخير، وأن الشيطان يخلق الشر.
And they affirmed and were certain that the servants create evil, analogous to the statement of the Magians who affirmed two creators: one creates good and the other creates evil. And the Qadariyya claimed that Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, creates good, and that Satan creates evil.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This accusation targets the Qadariyya (and by extension the Mu'tazila) who believe that human beings have independent power to create their own actions, including evil. Al-Ash'ari draws a parallel with the dualistic Magians (Zoroastrians) who believed in two ultimate principles: one of good and one of evil. The Qadariyya effectively assign the creation of evil to the devil (and to human will), thus limiting Allah's exclusive creative power. This is presented as a serious theological error.

Key Terms
خلق الشر
المجوس
خالقين
الشيطان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the Qadariyya are simply affirming human free will and responsibility, which is a good thing.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari argues that in doing so, they fall into a dualistic error akin to Zoroastrianism, because they effectively posit two sources of creation: Allah for good, and Satan/humans for evil.

Checkpoint
To what group does al-Ash'ari compare the Qadariyya's belief in two creators?
A) The Christians
B) The Jews
C) The Magians (Majus)
D) The ancient Greeks

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's accusation equates the Qadariyya belief in human creation of evil with Zoroastrian dualism, a grave violation of tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you blame Satan for your sins or shortcomings, do you realize that you are implicitly attributing to him a power of creation that belongs only to Allah? How can you take full responsibility for your actions without excusing them?
?
Al-Ash'ari equates the Qadariyya with Zoroastrians. Is there any area of your belief where you subtly assign creative power to something other than Allah—your own effort, society, or circumstance?
?
This passage reminds us that even well-intentioned views (like defending human responsibility) can lead to shirk if not anchored in tawhid. In your daily life, where might you be tempted to compromise Allah's absolute control for the sake of feeling in control?

Refuting the Denial of Allah's Universal Will
Al-Ash'ari refutes Qadari denial of Allah's universal will with consensus and Qur'anic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari uses Qur'anic verses and consensus to refute the Qadari claim that Allah's will is not all-encompassing.

Core Idea
Allah's will is absolute; nothing happens outside His will.

Al-Ash'ari confronts a serious doctrinal error: the claim that Allah wills what does not happen and that what happens is not willed by Him. This lesson examines his refutation based on the Muslim consensus and five clear Qur'anic verses, showing that human will is entirely dependent on Allah's will.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice that al-Ash'ari presents the Qadari claim, then responds with consensus and verses.
The passage is dense with scriptural references.
2
Identify the consensus statement
Find the phrase 'ma sha' Allahu kana wa ma lam yasha' lam yakun' – this is the foundational principle that underlies the whole argument.
This consensus is the first line of refutation.
3
Examine each Qur'anic verse
There are five verses quoted. For each, note how it demonstrates that Allah's will is universal and human will is contingent upon His.
The verses cover different aspects: human action, conflict, guidance, divine power, and prophetic obedience.
4
Understand the prophetic condemnation
The Prophet called them 'Majus al-ummah' (Magians). Reflect on why this is a serious label equating their belief to dualism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعموا أن الله عز وجل يشاء ما لا يكون، ويكون ما لا يشاء، خلافاً لما أجمع عليه المسلمون من أن ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن، ورداً لقول الله عز وجل: { وَمَا تَشَاءُونَ إِلَّا أَن يَشَاءَ اللَّهُ } [الإنسان : 30] فأخبر تعالى أنا لا نشاء شيئاً إلا وقد شاء الله أن نشاءه، ولقوله تعالى: { وَلَوْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ مَا اقْتَتَلُوا } [البقرة : 253]، ولقوله تعالى: { وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَآتَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَاهَا } [السجدة : 13]، ولقوله تعالى: { فَعَّالٌ لِّمَا يُرِيدُ } [البروج : 16]، ولقوله تعالى مخبراً عن نبيه شعيب أنه قال: { وَمَا يَكُونُ لَنَا أَن نَّعُودَ فِيهَا إِلَّا أَن يَشَاءَ اللَّهُ رَبُّنَا وَسِعَ رَبُّنَا كُلَّ شَيْءٍ عِلْمًا } [الأعراف : 89] ولهذا سماهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مجوس هذه الأمة.
And they claimed that Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, wills what does not happen, and that happens what He does not will, contrary to what the Muslims have agreed upon: that whatever Allah wills happens, and whatever He does not will does not happen, and in rejection of the saying of Allah, the Mighty and Majestic: 'And you do not will except that Allah wills' (Qur'an 76:30). So He, exalted, informed us that we do not will anything except that Allah has willed that we will it. And for His saying: 'And if Allah had willed, they would not have fought' (Qur'an 2:253), and His saying: 'And if We had willed, We would have given every soul its guidance' (Qur'an 32:13), and His saying: 'Doer of whatever He wills' (Qur'an 85:16), and His saying, informing about His prophet Shu'ayb that he said: 'And it is not for us to return to it unless Allah, our Lord, wills. Our Lord encompasses everything in knowledge' (Qur'an 7:89). And for this reason the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, called them the Magians of this nation.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This is the final and most extensive accusation. Al-Ash'ari refutes the Qadariyya belief that human will is independent of Allah's will. They claimed that Allah wills something that does not occur, and that what occurs is not willed by Allah. Al-Ash'ari counters first by citing the consensus (ijma‘) of the Muslims that whatever Allah wills happens and whatever He does not will does not happen. Then he quotes five Qur'anic verses that demonstrate the scope of Allah's will: from Surat al-Insan (76:30) teaching that human will is contingent on Allah's will; from Surat al-Baqara (2:253) showing that even human conflict is subject to Allah's will; from Surat al-Sajda (32:13) indicating that guidance is granted only if Allah wills; from Surat al-Buruj (85:16) affirming that Allah does whatever He wills; and from Surat al-A'raf (7:89) quoting Prophet Shu'ayb that his return to a community would only be by Allah's will. Al-Ash'ari concludes by citing a hadith in which the Prophet called the Qadariyya 'the Magians of this nation', equating their belief in independent human will with the Magian dualism.

Key Terms
المشيئة
الإجماع
مجوس هذه الأمة
الآيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming human free will independently of Allah's will preserves divine justice.
Correction: The Qur'an and consensus affirm that Allah's will is absolute; human will is contingent. Denying this leads to a dualistic belief akin to Magianism.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ash'ari, what is the Muslim consensus regarding Allah's will?
A) Allah wills some things and not others
B) Whatever Allah wills happens and what He does not will does not happen
C) Human will is independent of Allah's will
D) Allah wills evil but does not create it

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari demonstrates that the Qur'an and Muslim consensus affirm that Allah's will is all-encompassing and that human will is contingent on His.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you plan your day, how often do you consciously say 'if Allah wills' (insha’Allah) and truly mean it? Think of one specific decision you made today without that acknowledgment. Would you have made it differently if you had remembered that your will is dependent on His?
?
Recall a time when something you desperately wanted did not happen, and you felt resentment or questioned Allah's wisdom. Did you, even momentarily, fall into the Qadari mindset that Allah wills what does not happen? How can you guard your heart against that feeling of injustice when His will contradicts your desires?
?
The Prophet called those who deny Allah's universal will 'the Magians of this nation.' Examine your heart: Do you ever act as if your success, your provision, or your guidance comes from your own efforts independent of Allah's will? What is one practical step you can take today to root out that subtle shirk and surrender your actions entirely to His will?

All Things Occur by Allah's Will
Al-Ash'ari affirms that all good and evil occur by Allah's will and that human action depends on Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that in Ash'ari theology, all events—both good and evil—occur solely by Allah's will, and that human actions are dependent on Allah's prior creation.

Core Idea
Everything that happens—good or evil—is by Allah's will.

This passage from al-Ash'ari establishes a foundational Sunni doctrine: nothing happens in the universe except by Allah's will. It directly counters the Qadariyya who claimed that evil events occur without Allah's will. Here, al-Ash'ari also clarifies that no one can act independently before Allah creates the action.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once. Notice the structure: two main affirmations are presented.
2
Identify the two key claims
The passage makes two points: (a) everything good and evil is by Allah's will, and (b) no one acts before Allah does.
3
Understand the theological context
The Qadariyya denied that evil is willed by Allah; al-Ash'ari asserts the contrary.
4
Reflect on the implications
This establishes complete divine sovereignty over all events without implying moral approval of evil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣٦ - وأنه لا يكون في الأرض شيء من خير وشر إلا ما شاء الله، وأن الأشياء تكون بمشيئة الله عزّ وجلّ، وأن أحداً لا يستطيع أن يفعل شيئاً قبل أن يفعله الله
36. And that nothing occurs in the earth of good or evil except what Allah has willed, and that all things occur by the will of Allah, Mighty and Majestic, and that no one is able to do anything before Allah does it.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage affirms the comprehensive nature of divine will (mashi'ah). Al-Ash'ari states that everything—both good (khayr) and evil (sharr)—occurs only by Allah's will. This is the Sunni position against the Qadariyya who argued that evil is not willed by Allah. Additionally, he asserts that human actions are dependent on Allah's prior act; no one can act independently before Allah's creation of the action. This aligns with the Ash'ari doctrine of kasb (acquisition), where humans acquire actions that are created by Allah.

Key Terms

خير وشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah does not will evil events.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari affirms that even evil occurs by Allah's will, which does not imply approval but complete sovereignty.

Key Takeaway
All events, good and bad, occur only by Allah's will, and no one acts independently of His creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

Everything Occurs by God's Will
Ashari asserts all good and evil happen only by God's will and power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Imam Ashari teaches all events, both good and evil, happen only by God's will and power, and that human actions are entirely dependent on Him.

Core Idea
Good and evil alike flow only from God's will.

This passage from Imam Ashari's Al-Ibanah tackles a fundamental question of Islamic theology: what is the scope of God's will? Does it cover only good, or also evil? Ashari gives a clear, uncompromising answer that has shaped Sunni belief for centuries. As you read, notice how he ties divine will, human inability, and absolute dependence together.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic text and the English translation. Notice the tone: Ashari states these as a series of affirmations, each building on the last.
The passage is dense; read it twice if needed.
2
Identify the key claims
List the four claims: (1) nothing on earth occurs except by God's will, (2) all things come to be by His will, (3) no one can do anything before God does it, (4) we are dependent and cannot escape His knowledge.
3
Reflect on the theological target
Consider that Ashari is refuting the Qadariyya, who believed humans create their own actions independently. How does each claim undermine that view?
The passage is a concentrated refutation.
4
Apply the common misunderstanding check
Review the common misunderstanding: that God willing evil implies moral approval. Think about why that is a misreading of Ashari's intent.
The lesson's core idea helps clarify this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣٦ - وأنه لا يكون في الأرض شيء من خير وشر إلا ما شاء الله، وأن الأشياء تكون بمشيئة الله عزّ وجلّ، وأن أحداً لا يستطيع أن يفعل شيئاً قبل أن يفعله الله، ولا نستغني عن الله، ولا نقدر على الخروج من علم الله عزَّ وجل(۱).
36- And that nothing occurs on earth of good or evil except what God wills, and that things come to be by the will of God, Mighty and Majestic, and that no one can do anything before God does it, and we are not independent of God, nor can we escape from the knowledge of God, Mighty and Majestic.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive statement on divine will and predestination. Ashari teaches that every event, whether good or evil, occurs only by God's will (mashi'a). There is no exception; everything in creation is subject to His decree. He then clarifies that human actions are dependent on God's prior act: no one can do anything before God does it, meaning that the power to act is given by God and the action itself is created by God. Finally, he emphasizes human dependence on God and the impossibility of escaping divine knowledge. This refutes the Qadariyya who claimed that humans independently create their actions.

Key Terms
مشيئة الله
لا يستطيع أن يفعل شيئاً قبل أن يفعله الله
علم الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God wills evil, He approves of evil morally.
Correction: Ashari's statement is about the scope of God's creative will, not His moral approval. Evil is willed by God as a created event, but it is not something He loves or commands.

Checkpoint

A) Only good things
B) Only bad things
C) All things, good and evil
D) Only major events

Key Takeaway
All events, good and evil, occur only by God's will, and humans are utterly dependent on Him in every action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you cannot do anything without God's prior will, then what is the real source of your pride in accomplishments? Are you living as though you are independent of God? Today, identify one area where you have acted independently and repent.
?
Since you cannot escape God's knowledge even for a moment, what secret thought or intention are you hiding from others but not from Him? Will you bring it to Him in sincere repentance and align your inner life with His will?

Only God Creates Human Actions
Ashari proves with multiple Quranic verses that only God creates human actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ashari doctrine that only Allah creates human actions, supported by multiple Quranic verses.

Core Idea
Only God creates all actions, including human ones.

Imam al-Ash'ari begins by affirming the foundational principle of tawhid in creation: no creator but Allah. He then cites several Quranic verses to demonstrate that human actions are created by Allah, refuting the Mu'tazili claim that humans create their own deeds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without focusing on analysis. Then read the English translation to grasp the flow.
The passage begins with a statement and then lists verses as evidence.
2
Identify the main claim
Notice that the first line states the core doctrine: no creator except God and actions are created by God.
This is the central thesis.
3
Examine the Quranic verses
Look at each verse cited and understand how it supports the claim. The first verse directly links God's creation to human actions.
The verses are from al-Saffat, Fatir, an-Nahl, and at-Tur.
4
Understand the refutation
Recognize that these verses are used to refute the idea that humans can create their own actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۷- وأنه لا خالق إلا الله وأن أعمال العباد مخلوقة لله مقدورة له، كما قال سبحانه: ﴿ وَاللهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الصافات: ٩٦ ] (٢). وأن العباد لا يقدرون أن يخلقوا شيئاً وهم يخلقون، كما قال: ﴿هَلْ مِنْ خَلِقٍ غير الله ) [فاطر: ٣]، وكما قال: ﴿ لَا يَخْلُقُونَ شَيْئًا وَهُمْ يُخْلَقُونَ ﴾ [النحل: ٢٠] ، وكما قال سبحانه: ﴿ أَفَمَن يَخْلُقُ كَمَن لا يَخْلُقُ ﴾ [النحل: ١٧]، وكما قال: أمّ خُلِقُوا مِنْ غَيْرِ شَيْءٍ أَمْ هُمُ الْخَلِقُونَ ﴾ [الطور : (٣٥) . وهذا في كتاب الله كثير (۳).
37- And that there is no creator except God, and that the actions of servants are created by God, decreed by Him, as He said: 'And God created you and what you do' [37:96]. And that the servants are not able to create anything while they themselves are created, as He said: 'Is there any creator other than God?' [35:3], and as He said: 'They do not create anything while they are created' [16:20], and as He said: 'Is He who creates like one who does not create?' [16:17], and as He said: 'Or were they created from nothing, or are they the creators?' [52:35]. And this is abundant in the Book of God.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a scriptural proof that only God is the creator, and that human actions are created by Him. Ashari begins with the foundational statement: no creator except God. Then he quotes the famous verse from Surah al-Saffat (37:96): 'And God created you and what you do,' which directly attributes the creation of human actions to God. He then provides four additional verses that refute the idea that humans can create. The first (35:3) asks rhetorically if there is any creator other than God. The second (16:20) states that idols do not create anything while they themselves are created, implying humans similarly do not create. The third (16:17) contrasts the Creator with those who do not create. The fourth (52:35) challenges whether humans were created from nothing or are themselves creators. Ashari concludes by noting the abundance of such verses in the Quran. This argument firmly establishes the Ashari position against the Mu'tazila who claimed humans create their own actions.

Key Terms
لا خالق إلا الله
أعمال العباد مخلوقة لله
خلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage denies that humans have any freedom or choice in their actions.
Correction: The passage only denies that humans create (bring into existence) their actions; the Ashari school affirms human kasb (acquisition), which involves choice and responsibility, but the act of creation is solely Allah's.

Checkpoint

C) ﴿لَا يَخْلُقُونَ شَيْئًا﴾
D) ﴿أَفَمَن يَخْلُقُ كَمَن لا يَخْلُقُ﴾

Key Takeaway
This lesson establishes that the Quran repeatedly affirms that only Allah is the creator, and human actions are part of His creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you genuinely feel that it was Allah who created that action in you, or do you subtly claim ownership of it? How would your humility change if you truly affirmed this verse in your heart right now?
?
Think of a sin you committed today. If Allah created that action, does that make you less responsible? Or does it drive you to repent more sincerely, knowing that only He can change your heart? What will you do after this lesson to align your belief with action?
?
If all your actions—both obedient and disobedient—are created by Allah alone, then what is your role? Are you merely a passive vessel, or does this truth compel you to constantly seek His help and strive harder? Commit to one specific change in your attitude toward your daily deeds.

God Guides Believers and Misguides Disbelievers
Ashari explains divine guidance and misguidance by God's will and ability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ashari affirms that God's guidance and misguidance are acts of His will and power, not outcomes of human merit or divine obligation.

Core Idea
Guidance and misguidance are entirely by God's will, not human deserving.

This passage addresses a central point of contention between Ashari and the Mu'tazila: Is God obligated to do what is best for everyone? Ashari argues that God guides whom He wills and misguides whom He wills, and He is fully able to guide all but chooses not to. The Quranic verse he cites seals the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text and its English translation. Notice the contrast between believers and disbelievers, and the conditional statement.
The passage refutes the Mu'tazila claim that God must do what is best for all.
2
Identify the key claims
Identify the claims Ashari makes: God guides believers, misguides disbelievers, and He is able to guide them but wills otherwise.
3
Understand the Quranic proof
Read the verse from Surah al-A'raf (7:178). How does it support Ashari's position?
The verse directly attributes guidance and misguidance to God.
4
Grasp the theological implication
Reflect on why this matters: it affirms God's absolute sovereignty and rejects the idea that humans can guide themselves or that God is obliged to guide.
This is a key difference from the Mu'tazila doctrine of divine justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۸- وأن الله وفق المؤمنين لطاعته، ولطف بهم ، ونظر إليهم وأصلحهم وهداهم، وأضل الكافرين ولم يهدهم، ولم يلطف بهم ،بالإيمان، كما زعم أهل الزيغ والطغيان، ولو لطف بهم وأصلحهم لكانوا صالحين، ولو هداهم لكانوا مهتدين كما قال تبارك وتعالى: ﴿ مَن يَهْدِ اللَّهُ فَهُوَ الْمُهْتَدِى وَمَن يُضْلِلْ فَأَوَلَيْكَ هُمُ الْخَسِرُونَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۷۸] (٤) . وأن الله يَقْدِر أَن يُصلح الكافرين ، ويلطف بهم حتى يكونوا مؤمنين، ولكنه أراد أن يكونوا كافرين كما علم، وخذلهم وطبع على قلوبهم (٥).
38- And that God granted success to the believers for His obedience, and was kind to them, and looked upon them, and set them aright, and guided them; and He led the disbelievers astray, and did not guide them, and was not kind to them with faith, as the people of deviation and transgression claim. And if He had been kind to them and set them aright, they would have been righteous; and if He had guided them, they would have been guided, as He, Blessed and Exalted, said: 'Whomsoever God guides, he is the guided; and whomsoever He leads astray, those are the losers' [7:178]. And that God is able to set the disbelievers aright and be kind to them so that they become believers, but He willed that they be disbelievers as He knew, and He abandoned them and sealed their hearts.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage addresses the doctrine of divine guidance and misguidance. Ashari first describes God's actions toward believers: He grants them success (tawfiq), kindness (lutf), oversight, rectification, and guidance. In contrast, toward disbelievers, He leads them astray, withholds guidance and kindness (specifically the kindness of faith). This refutes the Mu'tazila (called 'people of deviation and transgression') who claimed God must do what is best for all. Ashari argues that if God had treated disbelievers as He did believers, they would have been righteous and guided. He cites the Quranic verse from al-A'raf (7:178) that explicitly links guidance and misguidance to God's will. He then clarifies that God is fully capable of guiding disbelievers and rectifying them, but He willed that they remain disbelievers according to His eternal knowledge, and as a result He abandoned them and sealed their hearts. This underscores God's absolute sovereignty and wisdom in decreeing belief and disbelief.

Key Terms
وفق
أضل
خذل
طبع على قلوبهم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God is obligated to guide every person equally, and if He fails to guide, it is unjust.
Correction: Ashari teaches that God guides whom He wills and misguides whom He wills, and He is not obliged to guide anyone. His action is based on His wisdom and will.

Checkpoint
According to Ashari, why are disbelievers not guided?
A) God is unable to guide them
B) God willed them to be disbelievers
C) They have free will to choose
D) God does not care about them

Key Takeaway
God's guidance and misguidance are acts of His sovereign will and power, not outcomes of human merit or divine obligation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your own faith is a gift from God, not a product of your intelligence or effort? How does that realization humble you when you see others who are not guided?
?
When you encounter persistent disbelief or sin in yourself or others, do you attribute it solely to the person's free will, or do you see God's will behind it? Which view makes you more reliant on God's mercy?
?
If God had willed, everyone would be guided. How does this truth change the way you pray for guidance for yourself and for those dear to you? Does your prayer reflect a deep dependence on God's sovereign choice?

Allah's Absolute Will in Guidance and Misguidance
Al-Ash'ari affirms that Allah guides believers and misguides disbelievers by His will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's will is effective in both guidance and misguidance, and that He has the power to guide all but wills otherwise.

Core Idea
Allah's will determines both guidance and misguidance, and He is not compelled to guide anyone.

In this passage, Imam al-Ash'ari affirms the Ash'ari position on qadar: Allah guides whom He wills and leads astray whom He wills. He refutes the Mu'tazilite claim that Allah must treat all equally, and instead asserts that Allah's will is absolute and His actions are not subject to obligation. Let’s examine his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the key terms like هداية and إضلال.
Notice the flow from affirmation to proof.
2
Identify the key claims
List the specific claims: Allah guides believers, misguides disbelievers, and He is able to guide them but willed otherwise.
This forms the core of the Ash'ari doctrine.
3
Examine the proof
Al-Ash'ari uses a conditional argument and a Quranic verse (7:178). Understand how the proof supports the claim.
The verse shows that guidance and misguidance are entirely up to Allah.
4
Address the misconception
The passage does not say Allah forces disbelief; it says He wills it and seals hearts. Consider how human responsibility is preserved.
This is a common point of confusion.
5
Summarize the stance
Write a one-sentence summary of al-Ash'ari's position on divine will and human guidance.
Check if you captured the absolute nature of Allah's will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۸- وأن الله وفق المؤمنين لطاعته، ولطف بهم، ونظر إليهم وأصلحهم وهداهم، وأضل الكافرين ولم يهدهم، ولم يلطف بهم بالإيمان، كما زعم أهل الزيغ والطغيان، ولو لطف بهم وأصلحهم لكانوا صالحين، ولو هداهم لكانوا مهتدين كما قال تبارك وتعالى: ﴿ مَن يَهْدِ اللَّهُ فَهُوَ الْمُهْتَدِى وَمَن يُضْلِلْ فَأُولَـٰئِكَ هُمُ الْخَاسِرُونَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۷۸] (٤). وأن الله يَقْدِر أَن يُصلح الكافرين، ويلطف بهم حتى يكونوا مؤمنين، ولكنه أراد أن يكونوا كافرين كما علم، وخذلهم وطبع على قلوبهم (٥)
38. And that Allah granted success to the believers for His obedience, and was kind to them, and looked upon them and set them aright and guided them, and led the disbelievers astray and did not guide them, and was not kind to them with faith, as the people of deviation and transgression claim. And if He had been kind to them and set them aright, they would have been righteous, and if He had guided them, they would have been guided, as the Blessed and Exalted said: "Whomever Allah guides, he is the rightly guided; and whomever He leads astray – those are the losers" [7:178]. And that Allah is able to set the disbelievers aright and be kind to them so that they become believers, but He willed that they be disbelievers as He knew, and He abandoned them and set a seal upon their hearts.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal affirmation regarding divine guidance and misguidance. Al-Ash'ari first states that Allah grants success, kindness, and guidance to believers, while He leads disbelievers astray and does not guide them or show them kindness towards faith. This is in opposition to the claims of deviant sects (such as the Mu'tazila) who assert that Allah must act in a certain way. Al-Ash'ari then argues that if Allah had willed to guide the disbelievers, they would have been guided, quoting verse 7:178 to prove that guidance and misguidance are entirely up to Allah. He further emphasizes that Allah has the power and ability to set the disbelievers aright and cause them to believe, but He willed for them to be disbelievers based on His eternal knowledge, and consequently He abandons them and seals their hearts. This affirms the Ash'ari position that divine will is absolute and all actions, including unbelief, occur by Allah's decree.

Key Terms
هداية
إضلال
مشيئة
خذلان
طبع على القلوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah forces people to disbelieve.
Correction: The passage affirms that Allah wills their disbelief, but humans are still accountable for their choices; Allah's will does not negate human responsibility.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ash'ari in this passage, why do disbelievers remain disbelievers?
A) Because Allah is unable to guide them
B) Because Allah willed them to be disbelievers and abandoned them
C) Because they were created with free will independent of Allah
D) Because they rejected guidance after Allah guided them

Key Takeaway
Allah's will is absolute; He guides whom He wills and leads astray whom He wills, and He is not compelled to guide anyone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a non-Muslim who seems good-hearted, do you assume Allah must guide them? How does this passage challenge your assumption about the absolute nature of Allah's will? Will you still pray for their guidance with full reliance on His will?
?
Reflect on your own obedience to Allah. Do you secretly believe it is because you are better or more deserving? How does the phrase 'Allah granted success to the believers' (وَفَّقَ اللَّهُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ) humble you? What changes in your worship if you truly attribute every good deed to His tawfiq?
?
Can you think of a person you have given up hope for, assuming they will never be guided? According to this passage, if Allah willed, He could guide them instantly. Does that realization increase your hope in du'a, or does it make you question why He does not? How should you respond to the mystery of His will?

Divine Decree

Good and Evil Are by Allah's Decree
Al-Ash'ari affirms divine decree and human dependence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to al-Ash'ari, all good and evil occur by Allah's decree, and that human beings have no independent power to bring benefit or harm to themselves, relying entirely on Allah's will.

Core Idea
Good and evil, benefit and harm — all are from Allah's decree alone.

In this short but powerful passage, Imam al-Ash'ari states a core principle of Ahl al-Sunnah: that everything that happens, whether good or evil, sweet or bitter, is by Allah's decree and predestination. He then reminds us that we own no benefit or harm for ourselves except what Allah wills, grounding this in a verse where even the Prophet declares his complete dependence on Allah. This lesson unpacks these statements and clarifies the correct belief about divine decree.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the literal translation to grasp the flow.
2
Identify key affirmations
Notice that al-Ash'ari makes two main affirmations: (a) good and evil are by Allah's decree, and (b) we own no benefit or harm except by Allah's will. List them.
3
Connect to the Quranic evidence
Read the verse cited (7:188). How does al-Ash'ari use it to support his point? What does it teach about the Prophet's reliance on Allah?
This verse is often used to negate any claim of independent power in creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۹ - وأن الخير والشر بقضاء الله وقدره وأنا نؤمن بقضاء الله وقدره، خيره وشره، حلوه ومره، ونعلم أن ما أصابنا لم يكن ليخطئنا، وما أخطأنا لم يكن ليصيبنا (١). وأنا لا نملك لأنفسنا نفعاً ولا ضراً (۲) إلا ما شاء الله، كما قال عز وجل: ﴿ قُل لَّا أَمْلِكُ لِنَفْسِي نَفْعًا وَلَا ضَرًّا إِلَّا مَا شَاءَ اللهُ ﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۸۸] (۳)
39. And that good and evil are by the decree and predestination of Allah, and we believe in the decree and predestination of Allah, its good and its evil, its sweet and its bitter, and we know that what has befallen us was not going to miss us, and what missed us was not going to befall us. And that we do not own for ourselves benefit or harm except what Allah wills, as the Mighty and Majestic said: "Say, 'I do not own for myself benefit or harm except what Allah wills'" [7:188].
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage affirms the Ash'ari doctrine of predestination (qada and qadr). Al-Ash'ari states that good and evil both occur by Allah's decree and predestination. He then emphasizes that believers accept all aspects of divine decree – its good and evil, sweet and bitter. This acceptance is based on the knowledge that nothing befalls a person except what was decreed, and what was not decreed cannot occur. This is a reference to the well-known hadith about the pens having dried. He then adds that humans do not possess independent power to bring benefit or harm to themselves; all such outcomes are subject to Allah's will. He supports this with verse 7:188, where the Prophet is commanded to declare that he owns no benefit or harm except by Allah's will, setting an example of complete reliance on Allah.

خير
شر
نفع
ضر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That this teaching eliminates human responsibility or effort.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari is affirming that all outcomes are ultimately from Allah, but this does not negate human accountability; rather, it establishes tawheed in rububiyyah and the fact that all power belongs to Allah. Human actions are still subject to reward and punishment as per sharia.

Checkpoint
What does al-Ash'ari say about good and evil in relation to Allah?
A) Good is from Allah, evil is from humans
B) Both good and evil are by Allah's decree and predestination
C) Neither good nor evil are predestined
D) Only good is predestined, evil is from Shaytan

Key Takeaway
Everything that occurs, whether good or evil, benefit or harm, is by Allah's decree and predestination, and we have no independent power to bring about any outcome except by Allah's will.

?
وأنتم تقرؤون هذا النص، هل تعتقد حقًا أن كل ما أصابك من سوء—كل خيبة أمل، كل خسارة—هو بقضاء الله وقدره؟ هل يمكنك أن تتذكر موقفًا محددًا ألومت فيه نفسك أو الآخرين بدلًا من أن تتقبله كقضاء من الله؟ ما الذي سيتغير في قلبك لو تيقنت من ذلك؟ وهل ستتوب اليوم من تلك النظرة؟

في أي مجالات حياتك تتصرف وكأنك تملك النفع والضر بنفسك—صحتك، مالك، علاقاتك؟ وما هو النتيجة المحددة التي تسعى إليها الآن وكأنها تعتمد عليك وحدك؟ كيف يمكنك أن تحوِّل ذلك إلى 'إلا ما شاء الله'؟

Belief in Divine Decree: Good and Evil from Allah
Al-Ash'ari affirms belief in qadr and that all good and evil are by Allah's decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic belief in divine decree (qadr) and that all good and evil occur by Allah's will and decree.

Core Idea
Everything that happens is by Allah's decree, including good and evil.

This passage from Al-Ash'ari's creed affirms a fundamental belief in qadr: that Allah decrees all things, good and evil alike. The author emphasizes total reliance on Allah and cites a Quranic verse to show that humans own no independent power. Let's examine the text to grasp this essential teaching.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once, then read the English translation. Notice the key terms: قضاء, قدر, خير, شر.
The passage is a creedal statement; focus on its concise structure.
2
Identify the affirmation of qadr
Recognize that the author affirms belief in both good and evil aspects of decree, using phrases like 'its sweet and its bitter'.
This shows that qadr encompasses all events, whether pleasant or painful.
3
Understand the Quranic proof
The author quotes Quran 7:188 to prove that humans cannot benefit or harm themselves except by Allah's will. Reflect on how this confirms dependence on Allah.
This verse is used to counter any notion of independent human power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأن الخير والشر بقضاء الله وقدره وأنا نؤمن بقضاء الله وقدره، خيره وشره، حلوه ومره، ونعلم أن ما أصابنا لم يكن ليخطئنا، وما أخطأنا لم يكن ليصيبنا. وأنا لا نملك لأنفسنا نفعاً ولا ضراً إلا ما شاء الله، كما قال عز وجل: ﴿ قُل لَّا أَمْلِكُ لِنَفْسِي نَفْعًا وَلَا ضَرًّا إِلَّا مَا شَاءَ اللهُ ﴾ [الأعراف: ١٨٨]

And we do not own for ourselves benefit or harm except what Allah wills, as He, Mighty and Majestic, said: 'Say: I do not own for myself benefit or harm except what Allah wills.' [Al-A'raf: 188]
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a creedal statement affirming belief in divine decree (qadr). The author begins by stating that good and evil occur by Allah's decree and predestination. He then expresses the believer's acceptance of all aspects of decree — good and evil, sweet and bitter. He further asserts the certainty that whatever afflicts a person could not have missed him, and whatever misses could not have afflicted him, reflecting the prophetic teaching from the hadith of Ibn Abbas. Finally, he declares that humans do not independently possess power to benefit or harm themselves, citing Quran 7:188 to emphasize absolute dependence on Allah's will.

خير
شر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Belief in qadr leads to fatalism and abandoning effort.
Correction: The passage teaches that we own no independent power, not that we should abandon actions; we rely on Allah while still acting.

B) The Quranic verse from Surah Al-A'raf
C) The consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
All good and evil occur by Allah's decree, and humans are completely dependent on His will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Reliance on Allah and Affirming Neediness
Al-Ash'ari states reliance and constant neediness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that a believer's relationship with Allah is characterized by turning to Him in all matters and affirming constant neediness and poverty before Him.

Core Idea
We are always in need of Allah; turning to Him is our constant posture.

This passage from Imam al-Ash'ari captures a fundamental attitude of the believer: total reliance on Allah. It is not merely a pious phrase but a doctrinal stance that affirms human contingency and divine sovereignty. Let's unpack its meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once. Notice the verbs 'naj'aa' (we seek refuge) and 'nuthbitu' (we affirm).
The Arabic is concise but loaded.
2
Understand the key terms
Focus on 'lujuu'' (seeking refuge), 'hajah' (need), and 'faqr' (poverty). These express complete dependence on Allah.
In Islamic theology, 'faqr' means existential neediness, not just financial poverty.
3
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: Why does the author stress 'at every time' (fi kulli waqt)? How does this shape a believer's daily life?
This counters the idea that we only need Allah in times of hardship.
4
Address the common misunderstanding
Some may think this negates human effort. The commentary clarifies that neediness reminds us that all ability comes from Allah, not that we should be passive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And we seek refuge in our affairs to Allah, and we affirm neediness and poverty at every time to Him.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This short passage is a statement of reliance and dependence on Allah. The author declares that in all matters we turn to Allah for refuge, and we affirm that we are in constant need and poverty before Him at every moment. This reinforces the Ash'ari emphasis on human contingency and Allah's absolute sovereignty.

All Provision Comes from Allah; Satan's Whispers Are Real
Affirming divine provision and Satanic whispering.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all provision, whether lawful or unlawful, is from Allah, and that Satan genuinely whispers to humans causing doubt and confusion, as affirmed by Quranic verses and in opposition to rationalist sects.

Core Idea
Every morsel is from Allah; every whisper is from Satan.

The Imām now turns to two related doctrines often denied by rationalist theologians: that Allah provides both halal and haram sustenance, and that Satan has real power to whisper confusion into human hearts. This passage anchors these beliefs in two clear Quranic verses and explicitly rejects the positions of the Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal translation. Notice the two claims: provision from Allah, and Satan's whispering. The Imām states each as a matter of '...and that...'.
2
Identify the Quranic proofs
The Imām cites two verses. Reflect on how each verse supports the claims. The first verse links usury-consumers to being touched by Satan. The second describes the whispering of Satan into hearts.
3
Understand the sectarian context
The Imām explicitly says this is contrary to Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya. Ask: why would they deny these? Because they emphasize human free will and deny any external influence on human actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأن الأرزاق من قبل الله عز وجل، يرزقها عباده حلالاً وحراماً، وأن الشيطان يوسوس للإنسان ويشككه ويتخبَّطه خلافاً لقول المعتزلة والجهمية، كما قال الله عز وجل: ( الَّذِينَ يَأْكُلُونَ الرِّبوا لَا يَقُومُونَ إِلَّا كَمَا يَقُومُ الَّذِي يَتَخَبَّطُهُ الشَّيْطَانُ مِنَ الْمَسِ ) [البقرة: ٢٧٥] وكما قال: ( مِن شَرِّ الْوَسْوَاسِ الْخَنَّاسِ الَّذِي يُوَسْوِسُ فِي صُدُورِ النَّاسِ * مِنَ الْجِنَّةِ وَالنَّاسِ ) [ الناس: ٤-٦].

And that Satan whispers to man and causes him doubt and confuses him, contrary to the saying of the Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya. As Allah Almighty said: 'Those who consume usury will not stand except as one whom Satan has touched by insanity' [Al-Baqarah 275]. And as He said: 'From the evil of the whisperer who withdraws, who whispers in the breasts of mankind, from among jinn and mankind' [An-Nas 4-6].
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage affirms two doctrines: (1) All provision (rizq) comes from Allah, whether it is lawful or unlawful—meaning that even the food a person earns through haram means is still provided by Allah's decree. (2) Satan has real influence over humans, causing whisperings and confusion, which is denied by the Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya. The Imām supports this with Quranic verses showing that usury-consumers are like those touched by Satan, and that Satan whispers into hearts.

Key Takeaway

Death and Killing Are by the Appointed Term
Affirmation that death and killing are by the appointed term.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that death and killing occur exactly at the preordained term (ajal) and why this doctrine refutes the idea that murder cuts life short.

Core Idea
Both natural death and murder happen at Allah's appointed time.

This passage from Imam al-Ash'ari's al-Ibanah affirms a core tenet of Sunni predestinarian theology: that every death, whether natural or violent, occurs precisely at the term Allah has decreed. The article is short but packs immense theological weight, rejecting any notion that human actions can alter the divinely fixed lifespan.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic sentence carefully, then its literal translation. Notice the structure: 'And that whoever dies or is killed... by his appointed term.'
The phrase 'bi-ajalihi' is the theological crux.
2
Reflect on 'ajal' (appointed term)
Consider what 'ajal' means in Islamic theology: a fixed, unchangeable time decreed by Allah for each person's death. This covers both natural and violent ends.
The term is from the root 'a-j-l', meaning 'to delay'. It implies a divinely set limit.
3
Consider the theological implication
Think about the common misconception that murder shortens a victim's life. This statement directly refutes that, affirming that the time of death was already decreed and the killing occurred exactly at that moment.
This doctrine is part of affirming Allah's absolute decree (qadar).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٦٥ - وأن من مات وقتل فبأجله مات وقتل
65 - And that whoever dies or is killed, it is by his appointed term that he died or was killed.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This article affirms predestination regarding the time of death: whether someone dies naturally or is killed, it occurs exactly at the preordained term (ajal). This refutes the idea that murder cuts short a person's life.

Key Terms
أجل
موت
قتل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Murder causes a person to die before their natural term.
Correction: This article teaches that even when killed, the death occurs at the appointed term; the term is not shortened by the action.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Death, whether natural or violent, occurs at Allah's appointed term.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you hear news of a murder, do you feel only anger at the killer, or do you also submit to the fact that the victim's term had come? How can you train yourself to see both the justice of accountability and the wisdom of divine decree?
?

Provision from Allah and Shaitan's Whispers
Imam al-Ash'ari affirms provision from Allah and the reality of shaitan's whispers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all provision, whether halal or haram, is from Allah, and that shaitan's whispers have real effects, as affirmed by the Quran and in contrast to the Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya.

Core Idea
Allah provides both halal and haram; shaitan's whispers are real and disturbing.

Imam al-Ash'ari affirms two fundamental truths: that all provision, lawful or unlawful, originates from Allah, and that shaitan's influence on humans is real, causing doubt and even physical disturbance. These affirmations directly oppose the rationalist sects who denied these realities. The passage cites two Quranic verses as clear evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text and its English translation once to get a sense of the author's concise style and the two affirmations.
Notice the numbered article (66) and the two Quranic citations.
2
Identify the two affirmations
The passage makes two distinct doctrinal points: (1) all provisions are from Allah, and (2) shaitan whispers and disturbs humans. Underline each in the text.
The refutation of Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya is tied to the second point.
3
Analyze the scriptural proofs
Read the two Quranic verses: al-Baqara 2:275 (usury and shaitan's touch) and an-Nas 114:4-6 (the whispering shaitan). Consider how each supports the respective affirmation.
The first verse shows a physical effect; the second describes the source of whispers.
4
Understand the refutation
The Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya denied that shaitan could cause real disturbance. Note how the verses prove otherwise.
This refutation is a key element of Sunni 'aqida.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٦٦ - وأن الأرزاق من قبل الله عز وجل، يرزقها عباده حلالاً وحراماً، وأن الشيطان يوسوس للإنسان ويشككه ويتخبَّطه خلافاً لقول المعتزلة والجهمية، كما قال الله عز وجل: (الذين يأكلون الربوا لا يقومون إلا كما يقوم الذي يتخبطه الشيطان من المس) [البقرة: ٢٧٥] وكما قال: (من شر الوسواس الخناس الذي يوسوس في صدور الناس * من الجنة والناس) [الناس: ٤-٦].
66 - And that provisions are from Allah, may He be mighty and majestic; He provides them to His servants, halal and haram; and that shaitan whispers to man and causes him to doubt and disturbs him, contrary to the saying of the Mu'tazila and the Jahmiyya, as Allah, may He be exalted, said: (Those who consume usury will not stand except as one stands whom shaitan has struck with insanity) [al-Baqara: 275] and as He said: (From the evil of the withdrawing whisperer who whispers into the breasts of mankind, from among jinn and mankind) [an-Nas: 4-6].
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This article makes two points with scriptural proofs: (1) All provisions come from Allah, both lawful (halal) and unlawful (haram). (2) Shaitan's influence is real—he whispers (waswasa), causes doubt, and disturbs (yatakhabbat) humans. This refutes the Mu'tazila and Jahmiyya who denied shaitan's effect. The author supports with two Quranic verses: one about the effect of shaitan on usurers (al-Baqara 2:275), and the other from Surat an-Nas (114:4-6) about the whispering of shaitan.

Key Terms
الأرزاق
حلال
حرام
الشيطان
وسوسة
المعتزلة
الجهمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think shaitan only tempts but does not affect the body; the Mu'tazila denied any real effect of shaitan on humans.
Correction: The Quran links shaitan's touch to physical disturbance (al-Baqara 2:275) and affirms his whispering (an-Nas 114:4-6), proving real influence.

Checkpoint
What does this article affirm about shaitan's action?
A) Shaitan only tempts but does not whisper
B) Shaitan whispers and disturbs man
C) Shaitan has no real effect
D) Shaitan controls man's decisions

Key Takeaway
Allah is the sole provider of all provisions, and shaitan's whispers have real effects that disturb humans, as proven by the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every provision you have—including what you earn through halal or haram—comes from Allah alone? How does this belief affect your daily choices when faced with an opportunity that mixes the two?
?
When you feel a sudden doubt or disturbance in your heart about your faith, do you recognize it as the whisper of shaitan, or do you dismiss it as your own thoughts? What will you do the next time that happens to actively seek refuge in Allah?
?
The verse about usury shows that shaitan's whispers can even have physical effects. Have you ever experienced a physical reaction—like anxiety or restlessness—during a moment of spiritual weakness? How will you use this lesson to fortify your heart against such attacks?

The Compelling Argument: God's Will and Human Actions
Ash'ari argues that if servants do what God dislikes, they would compel Him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the kalam argument that if servants do what God dislikes, it would imply they compel God, and why that is impossible.

Core Idea
If God dislikes an action yet it occurs, the doer compels God — impossible.

This passage presents a powerful refutation used by Imam al-Ash'ari against those who claim that God does not will all human actions. The argument uses a reductio ad absurdum: if actions happen that God dislikes and does not will, then the servants are compelling God. Since compulsion is impossible for God, the premise that He does not will those actions must be false.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the concise, dialectical style typical of kalam texts.
The passage is a single short argument (mas'ala).
2
Identify the logical structure
Break the argument into three parts: (1) premise that some actions anger God, (2) conditional that if God does not will them then servants compel Him, (3) conclusion that compulsion is impossible for God.
3
Reflect on the will vs. pleasure distinction
Consider how God can will an action in terms of decree and creation while still being angered by it. This distinction is crucial for understanding qadar.
The passage does not explicitly state this distinction, but it is implied.
4
Connect to the broader qadar debate
Understand that this argument defends the Ash'ari position that God's will encompasses all things, without implying moral approval of sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۹۰ - مسألة : ويقال لهم : أليس مما فعل العباد ما يُسخطه تعالى وما يغضب عليهم إذا فعلوه، فقد أغضبوه وأسخطوه؟ فلا بد من نعم . يقال لهم : فلو فعل العباد ما لا يريد وما يكرهه لكانوا أكرهوه، وهذه صفة القهر، تعالى الله عن ذلك علواً كبيراً .
190 - Issue: And it is said to them: Is there not among the actions of servants what angers God Almighty and makes Him wrathful against them when they do it? Thus they have angered Him and enraged Him. There is no escape from 'yes'. It is said to them: So if the servants do what He does not will and what He dislikes, they would have compelled Him. And this is the attribute of compulsion. God is exalted above that by a great exaltation.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is another refutation (mas'ala) that builds on the previous one. The author first establishes a point the opponents would accept: some actions of servants anger God and make Him wrathful. The author then argues: if those actions were done while God does not will them and dislikes them, then the servants would be compelling God to accept them — which is the attribute of being overpowered (qahr). Since God is beyond being compelled, the premise that God does not will those actions is false. Therefore, God must will all actions of servants, including sinful ones, in the sense that He permits or decrees them, though He may dislike them in terms of moral judgment.

Key Terms
سخط
غضب
القهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God wills all actions, then He must be pleased with sin.
Correction: God's will of creation (iraada kawniyya) is distinct from His legislative will (iraada shar'iyya). He may decree an action while morally disapproving of it.

Checkpoint
In this passage, what does the author conclude if servants do what God does not will?
A) They have compelled God.
B) They have earned His mercy.
C) They have proven His weakness.
D) They have shown His ignorance.

Key Takeaway
God wills all human actions, but His will does not imply His moral approval; otherwise, forbidding what one wills would be incoherent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God wills every action of yours—including every sin—does that make you feel excused or terrified? How does this truth change the way you seek forgiveness today, not just tomorrow?
?
Since God wills your sins but hates them, what does that say about the nature of your repentance? Is your repentance genuine if you continue to sin while knowing God's will encompasses it?
?
Think of one sin you have committed repeatedly. Knowing that God willed it to happen but is not pleased with it, can you still say 'I had no choice'? What choice are you making right now in response to that sin?
