The Question of Willing Evil
A rhetorical challenge to opponents on divine will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a rhetorical question can be used in kalam to expose inconsistencies in an opponent's position on divine will and moral evil.

Core Idea
A rhetorical question can reveal contradictions in rejecting divine will for evil deeds.

Imam al-Ash'ari confronts those who deny that Allah wills unbelief. His question is not a statement of doctrine but a logical probe: if Allah knows that unbelief will occur, on what rational grounds can you refuse that He wills it? This lesson unpacks the argumentative strategy behind this pointed question.

Guided Path
1
Read the rhetorical question
Read the Arabic and English translation of the question slowly. Notice the phrasing: 'Why do you refuse...' This is a direct challenge.
2
Identify the opponents' assumption
The opponents refuse because unbelief is 'ugly, corrupt, contradictory, contrary to faith.' They assume moral evil cannot be willed by God.
3
Reflect on the underlying logic
Ash'ari implies that knowledge of an event does not determine its moral value. God knows unbelief will happen, so refusing that He wills it requires a separate argument.
4
Consider the purpose of the question
This question forces opponents to either abandon their refusal or provide a rational justification. It is a dialectical tool, not an assertion.
Common misunderstanding: some might think Ash'ari affirms willing evil in a moral sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال لهم : لم أبيتم أن يريد الله الكفر الذي علم أنه يكون قبيحاً فاسداً متناقضاً خلافاً للإيمان؟
And it is said to them: Why do you refuse that Allah wills unbelief which He knows will occur, [it being] ugly, corrupt, contradictory, and contrary to faith?
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This is a rhetorical question directed at the opponents. The Ash'ari asks why the opponents refuse to accept that Allah wills unbelief, even though He knows it will occur. The opponents' objection might be based on the moral quality of unbelief (ugly, corrupt, contradictory to faith). The question challenges them to justify their refusal on rational grounds, implying that the nature of the thing willed does not affect the necessity of divine will for all occurrences.

Key Terms
الكفر
القبيح
الفاسد
المتناقض
الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that this question implies Ash'aris affirm that Allah wills evil in a moral sense, meaning He desires sin for its own sake.
Correction: The question is a dialectical tool to challenge opponents; it does not assert a moral stance. Ash'aris distinguish between divine will (everything that occurs is willed by Allah) and divine love or approval (Allah does not love evil).

Checkpoint
What is the basis on which the opponents refuse that God wills unbelief?
A) That God does not know it
B) That it is ugly, corrupt, and contrary to faith
C) That God is incapable of creating it
D) That it is impossible

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ash'ari challenges opponents by asking why they refuse that Allah wills unbelief, given that He knows it will occur, thereby exposing a potential inconsistency in their position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face hardship or witness evil, do you ever resent Allah or question His wisdom? How does this passage's teaching that Allah's will encompasses all events—even the ugly and corrupt—challenge you to deepen your trust in His decree?
?
There is a sin you commit repeatedly. Do you ever excuse it by saying 'Allah willed it' to avoid personal responsibility? How can you honestly hold onto both Allah's complete will and your own accountability after reflecting on this rhetorical question?
?
If Allah knows and wills all things, including your moments of disobedience, does that make your repentance less sincere? What does this passage demand of your heart in terms of humility before the mystery of divine will and human choice?

Necessity of God's Will for What He Creates
Ash'ari proves that God must will what He creates and that His dominion cannot contain what He does not will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ash'ari's argument that God must will everything He creates, and that any contrary belief implies deficiency in God.

Core Idea
God's will is comprehensive; whatever exists He wills.

Ash'ari begins by establishing a necessary connection between God's act of creation and His will. If God creates something, He must will it. But he also provides a deeper argument: that God's dominion cannot contain anything He does not will, otherwise that would imply forgetfulness or weakness in God. This passage is fundamental to the Ash'ari understanding of qadar (divine decree) and the attribute of will.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Ash'ari uses a very concise style here.
2
Identify the two arguments
The passage presents two main proofs: first, if God creates something, He must will it; second, that God's dominion cannot contain anything He does not will, otherwise it would imply deficiencies like forgetfulness or weakness.
The second argument is introduced with 'وجواب آخر' (and another answer).
3
Reflect on the implication for evil
Ash'ari applies the same reasoning to acts of disobedience. He argues that if they occurred against God's will, that would be a sign of weakness. Therefore, even unbelief is willed by God.
This is a key point in Ash'ari qadar theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجب أن الله سبحانه خالق لذلك، فقد وجب أنه مريد له؛ لأنه لا يجوز أن يخلق مالا يريده .
وجواب آخر : أنه لا يجوز أن يكون في سلطان الله عز وجل من إكساب العباد مالا يريده، كما لا يجوز أن يكون من فعله المجمع على أنه فعل مالا يريده؛ لأنه لو وقع من فعله مالا يعلمه لكان في ذلك إثبات النقصان وكذلك القول لو وقع من عباده مالا يعلمه، فكذلك لا يجوز أن يقع من عباده مالا يريده ; لأن ذلك يوجب أن يقع عن سهو وغفلة، أو عن ضعف وتقصير عن بلوغ ما يريده كما يجب ذلك لو وقع من فعله المجمع على أنه فعله مالا يريده وأيضاً فلو كانت المعاصي - وهو لا يشاء أن تكون المعاصي - كائنة شاء الله أم أبى، وهذه صفة الضعف . تعالى الله عن ذلك علواً كبيراً . وقد أوضحنا أن الله لم يزل مريداً على الحقيقة التي علمه عليها، فإذا كان الكفر مما يكون وقد علم ذلك فقد أراد أن يكون .
It is necessary that God, exalted, is the Creator of that, so it is necessary that He is willing of it; because it is not permissible that He creates what He does not will. And another answer: it is not permissible that there be in the dominion of God, mighty and majestic, from the acquisition (iktiṣāb) of the servants what He does not will, just as it is not permissible that there be from His act that which is agreed upon that He does something He does not will; because if there occurred from His act something He does not know, in that would be an affirmation of deficiency, and likewise in saying if there occurred from His servants what He does not know, so likewise it is not permissible that there occur from His servants what He does not will; because that requires that it occur from forgetfulness and negligence, or from weakness and shortcoming in attaining what He wills, as that would be required if there occurred from His act that which is agreed upon that He does something He does not will. And also, if acts of disobedience were - while He does not want them to be - occurring whether God wills it or not, that is an attribute of weakness. Exalted is God above that by a great exaltation. And we have made clear that God has never ceased to be willing according to the reality which He knew Him to be upon [or: which He knew it to be upon], so since unbelief is something that occurs and He has known that, He has willed that it occur.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage contains a proof and an additional answer regarding the relationship between God's creation and His will. The author begins by stating that if God is the Creator of something, then necessarily He is willing it; it is impossible for Him to create something He does not will. Then a second answer is given: it is impossible for God's dominion to include any action of His servants that He does not will, analogously to the impossibility that His own action would be something He does not will. The reasoning is that if such an action occurred without His will, it would imply deficiency in Him (like forgetfulness or weakness). The author then applies this to acts of disobedience: if they occurred against His will, that would be a sign of weakness. He concludes by reiterating that God is eternally willing in truth, and since He knew that unbelief would occur, He must have willed it.

Key Terms
مريد (willing)
سلطان (dominion)
كسب (acquisition)
سهو (forgetfulness)
غفلة (negligence)
ضعف (weakness)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God does not will evil or acts of disobedience.
Correction: Ash'ari argues that if God did not will them, that would imply forgetfulness or weakness in God, which is impossible. Therefore, God wills all that occurs, including evil.

Checkpoint
Why does Ash'ari argue that it is necessary for God to will what He creates?
A) Because creation implies knowledge of it
B) Because otherwise it would imply forgetfulness or weakness in God
C) Because the Qur'an says so
D) Because God's will is identical to His essence

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari proves that God's will encompasses all of creation, including acts of disobedience, because any other view would imply imperfection in God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every trial, failure, and sinful desire in your life was willed by God before it ever happened? If so, does that humble you to seek His mercy, or does it tempt you to blame Him? Confront that now.

You have committed sins that you knew were displeasing to God. Yet this lesson says God willed those very acts. How does knowing that your sin was not outside God's decree change how you view your accountability? Will you use it as an excuse or as a reason to repent more sincerely?

If you have ever secretly wished that your disobedience was outside God's will to absolve yourself of responsibility, you are attributing weakness to God. Will you accept that His will is perfect and that your sin was included in His plan, then ask Him to forgive what He willed? What is holding you back from that repentance?

The Dilemma of God's Will and Knowledge
Ash'ari presents a dilemma about God's will and knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical dilemma used by Ash'ari to refute the claim that God does not will unbelief.

Core Idea
God's will cannot oppose His knowledge — a logical impossibility.

This passage presents a crisp objection from Ash'ari against those who argue that God does not will unbelief. Using a dilemma, he shows that if God knew unbelief would occur but willed it not to, that would force an impossible contradiction. The passage is a masterclass in logical argument within kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the structure of the dilemma sink in.
The passage is a single sentence but contains two conditional steps.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
Find the two impossible outcomes that result from the assumption that God knows unbelief will occur but wills it not to. Notice how each horn is rejected as impermissible.
The first horn is willing contrary to knowledge; the second is willing what one does not know.
3
Understand the refutation
Ask yourself: why does this dilemma force the opponent to accept that God wills unbelief? Because the only consistent alternative is that God's will aligns with His knowledge.
This is a classical kalam argument: if a premise leads to absurdity, the premise must be false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : ويقال لهم : إذا كان الله عز وجل علم أن الكفر يكون، وأراد أن لا يكون، فقد أراد أن يكون ما علم على خلاف ما علم، وإذا لم يجز ذلك، فقد أراد أن يكون ما لم يعلم كما علم
Issue: And it is said to them: If God, mighty and majestic, knew that unbelief would occur, and willed that it not occur, then He willed that what He knew be contrary to what He knew, and if that is not permissible, then He willed that what He did not know be as He knew.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the position that God does not will unbelief. The opponents argue that if God knew that unbelief would occur but willed it not to occur, then He would be willing something contrary to His own knowledge. Since that is impossible, the only alternative is that God willed what He did not know (which is also impossible). Thus, the hypothetical that God does not will unbelief leads to a contradiction. This is a dilemma forcing the conclusion that God must will what He knows will occur.

Key Terms
علم (knowledge)
أراد (willed)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument is about fatalism, forcing God to will evil.
Correction: This argument is about the logical consistency of God's attributes. It does not address moral responsibility but rather shows that if God knows something will happen, He must will it in a way that is consistent with His knowledge.

Checkpoint
What is the dilemma presented in this objection?
A) Either God knows the future or He doesn't
B) Either God wills unbelief or He wills faith
C) Either God's will aligns with His knowledge or else He wills what He does not know
D) Either God creates evil or He is not omnipotent

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari uses a logical dilemma to prove that God's will must correspond to His knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that God's will is perfectly aligned with His knowledge, and He knows everything that will happen, why do you still resist submitting to His decree in matters of your life? What area of your life are you trying to will against what you know He has decreed?
?
When you face a hardship that you did not will, do you find yourself questioning God's wisdom? This lesson shows that even a logical impossibility is to separate God's will from His knowledge. How does this affect your trust in Him today?
?
Consider a sin you struggle with. God knows it will occur and He wills it in the sense of allowing it. How does knowing that His will is not separate from His knowledge change your view of your own responsibility? Are you using God's will as an excuse or as a call to humility?

The Objection: Does God Will Evil?
Ash'ari asks why opponents deny that God wills evil, given He knows it will occur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical basis of the Ash'ari objection to those who deny that God wills evil, specifically the implication of divine knowledge for divine will.

Core Idea
God's knowledge of evil implies He wills it.

This short but powerful objection cuts to the heart of a major theological debate. If God knows that unbelief will occur, why would His opponents insist He does not will it? The passage forces us to consider the relationship between divine knowledge and divine will, challenging the consistency of denying God's will for what He knows will happen.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to grasp the question being asked. Notice the key terms used to describe unbelief: ugly, corrupt, contradictory.
The objection is posed to those who say God does not will evil.
2
Analyze the logical structure
Identify the premise: God knows that unbelief will occur. The question challenges: If He knows it, why do you deny He wills it? The implication is that knowledge entails will.
This links epistemology (knowledge) to volition (will).
3
Consider the force of the objection
Think about why this is a challenge. The opponent must explain why God's knowledge does not lead to His will. This exposes a potential inconsistency in their position.
The objection does not claim God approves of evil, only that He wills it in some sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : ويقال لهم : لم أبيتم أن يريد الله الكفر الذي علم أنه يكون قبيحاً فاسداً متناقضاً خلافاً للإيمان؟
Issue: And it is said to them: Why do you refuse that God wills unbelief, which He knew would be ugly, corrupt, contradictory, contrary to faith?
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This short objection questions the position of those who deny that God wills evil. If God knows that unbelief is ugly and corrupt and will occur, why do they insist that He does not will it? The implication is that denying God's will for something He knows will occur is arbitrary. This forces the opponent to justify their refusal.

Key Terms
أبيتم (you refuse)
قبيح (ugly/evil)
متناقض (contradictory)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this objection means God approves of evil.
Correction: Actually, it is a logical challenge linking God's knowledge to His will, not a statement of moral approval.

Checkpoint

A) That God cannot will evil because He is good
B) That God's knowledge of evil implies He wills it
C) That unbelief is ugly and contradictory
D) That the Qur'an says God does not will evil

Key Takeaway
The objection argues that if God knows evil will occur, His knowledge implies He wills it, making denial of His will inconsistent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you see evil in the world, does your heart accept that God willed it, or do you secretly wish to exempt Him? What does that reveal about your trust in His wisdom?
?
If God wills unbelief, and you are a believer, is your faith not a sheer gift? How does that strip you of all pride and drive you to constant gratitude?

Willing Evil Does Not Make One Foolish
Ash'ari refutes the objection using Qur'anic examples (Abel and Yusuf).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ash'ari uses scriptural examples to refute the claim that willing evil makes God foolish.

Core Idea
Willing evil for a greater good does not make one foolish.

In this passage, Imam al-Ash'ari directly addresses an objection: if God wills evil deeds from His servants, does that not make Him foolish? He counters with two Qur'anic examples where righteous individuals willed evil acts without being considered foolish. This shows that the intention behind willing evil matters, and that God's willing of evil in creation does not detract from His perfection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Opponent's Claim
Read the opening line: 'Because the one who wills foolishness is a fool.' This is the premise Ash'ari will refute.
The opponent equates willing foolishness with being foolish.
2
Examine the First Example (Abel)
Look at the story of Cain and Abel. Abel willed his own murder (an evil act) so that his brother would bear sin, yet Abel is not considered foolish.
Abel's intention was to avoid sin himself and expose his brother's sin.
3
Examine the Second Example (Yusuf)
Yusuf willed imprisonment (an act of disobedience by his brothers) rather than commit sin. He is not considered foolish despite willing evil.
Yusuf preferred the lesser evil to preserve his own piety.
4
Conclude the Argument
If humans can will evil for good reasons without being foolish, then God, who is infinitely wise, can also will evil from servants without being foolish.
Ash'ari ends with a rhetorical question driving this point home.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: لأن مريد السفيه سفيه .
قيل لهم : ولم قلتم ذلك؟ أو ليس قد أخبر الله تعالى عن ابن آدم أنه قال لأخيه : ( لَئِن بَسَطتَ إِلَيَّ يَدَكَ لِتَقْتُلَنِي مَا أَنَا بِبَاسِطِ يَدِى إِلَيْكَ لِأَقْتُلَكَ إِنِّي أَخَافُ الله رَبَّ الْعَالَمِينَ * إِنِّي أُرِيدُ أَن تَبُوءَ بِإِثْمِي وَإِثْمِكَ فَتَكُونَ مِنْ أَصْحَابِ النَّارِ ) فأراد أن لا يقتل أخاه لئلا يعذب وأن يقتله أخوه حتى يبوء بإثم قتله له وسائر آثامه التي كانت عليه، فيكون من أصحاب النار، فأراد قتل أخيه الذي هو سفه ، ولم يكن بذلك سفيها ، فلم زعمتم أن الله سبحانه إذا أراد سفه العباد وجب أن ينسب ذلك إليه؟
مسألة : ويقال لهم : قد قال يوسف عليه السلام: ( رَبِّ السِّجْنُ أَحَبُّ إِلَيَّ مِمَّا يَدْعُونَنِي إِلَيْهِ ) وكان سجنهم إياه معصية، فأراد المعصية التي هي سجنهم إياه دون فعل ما يدعونه إليه، ولم يكن بذلك سفيهاً، فما أنكرتم من أن لا يجب إذا أراد الباري سبحانه سفه العباد - بأن يكون قبيحاً منهم خلافاً للطاعة ـ أن يكون سفيهاً .
For if they say: Because the one who wills foolishness is a fool. It is said to them: Why did you say that? Or has God not informed about the son of Adam that he said to his brother: "If you extend your hand to me to kill me, I am not one to extend my hand to you to kill you; indeed I fear God, Lord of the worlds. Indeed I desire that you bear my sin and your sin, so that you become among the companions of the Fire." So he willed not to kill his brother so as not to be punished, and he willed that his brother kill him so that he would bear the sin of killing him and the rest of his sins that were upon him, so that he would be among the companions of the Fire. So he willed the killing of his brother, which is foolishness, and he was not thereby a fool. So why do you claim that if God wills the foolishness of the servants, it is necessary that this be attributed to Him? Issue: And it is said to them: Yusuf, peace be upon him, said: "O my Lord, prison is more beloved to me than that to which they call me." And their imprisoning him was an act of disobedience, so he willed the disobedience which was their imprisoning him, rather than doing what they called him to, and he was not thereby a fool. So what have you denied that when the Exalted Creator wills the foolishness of the servants - that it be ugly from them, contrary to obedience - that He should be a fool?
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage provides two scriptural examples to refute the claim that willing evil makes one evil. The opponents had argued that "the one who wills foolishness is a fool." Ash'ari responds by citing the story of Cain and Abel: Abel willed that his brother kill him (an act of evil) yet he is not considered foolish. Then the story of Yusuf: Yusuf willed that his brothers imprison him (an act of disobedience) rather than commit sin, yet he is not a fool. Thus, willing evil can be for a good purpose and does not necessitate being evil oneself. The same applies to God: He may will the foolishness of His servants for a greater wisdom without being foolish Himself.

Key Terms
سفه (foolishness)
سفيه (fool)
إرادة (will)
معصية (disobedience)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Willing an evil act necessarily makes the willer evil or foolish.
Correction: Both Abel and Yusuf willed evil acts (murder and imprisonment) but are not considered foolish because their intentions were good. Thus, willing evil does not automatically make one evil.

Checkpoint
What do the examples of Abel and Yusuf demonstrate?
A) That prophets never will evil
B) That willing evil always makes one evil
C) That one can will an evil act for a good reason without being evil oneself
D) That God does not will evil

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari demonstrates through prophetic examples that willing evil for a greater good does not imply foolishness, thus defending God from this charge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever willed something that others considered foolish or evil, yet your intention was for a greater good? How does Abel's example challenge your assumptions about your own motives?
?
If God can will evil actions from His servants without being foolish, what does that mean for how you view difficult trials in your life? Will you trust His wisdom even when His will seems harsh?
?
You have likely judged others or yourself for having 'bad' desires. After this lesson, can you honestly examine if your will is ever for something seemingly wrong but with a righteous aim? Commit to one area where you need to align your will with God's greater purpose.

Objection: Seeing Evil Without Being Evil
Ash'ari uses the analogy of seeing evil to argue that willing evil does not make God evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari uses an analogy from sight to defend God's transcendence regarding the divine will.

Core Idea
Seeing evil does not make God evil; willing evil does not either.

This passage presents a clever argument by analogy. The opponents claim that if God wills evil, He would be evil. Ash'ari counters by pointing out that God sees evil acts without being termed a fool. So why should willing evil be different? The argument defends God's transcendence from any imperfection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then the translation. Let the author's argumentative flow come through.
Notice the concise style of this 'mas'ala'.
2
Identify the analogy
Identify the two parts: the opponent's admission about seeing, and Ash'ari's conclusion about willing. Notice how the same logic is applied.
The key is that the attribute (seeing/willing) does not transfer the quality of the object to the subject.
3
Understand the conclusion
Ash'ari ends by affirming God's transcendence: 'Exalted is God above that.' Reflect on how this analogy defends God's perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة أخرى : ويقال لهم : أليس من يرى منا جرم المسلمين كان سفيها، والله سبحانه يراهم ولا يُنسب إلى السفه؟ فلا بد من نعم . فيقال لهم : فيما أنكرتم أن من أراد السفه منا كان سفيها، والله سبحانه يريد سفه السفهاء ولا ينسب إلى الله تعالى سفه، تعالى الله عن ذلك
Another issue: And it is said to them: Is not one among us who sees the crime of the Muslims a fool, while God, exalted, sees them and is not attributed with foolishness? So they must say yes. Then it is said to them: So what do you deny that one among us who wills foolishness is a fool, while God, exalted, wills the foolishness of the foolish and is not attributed with foolishness? Exalted is God above that.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This is another argument by analogy. The opponents hold that willing evil makes one evil (foolish). Ash'ari points out that seeing evil does not make one evil; God sees all evil acts yet is not termed foolish. Similarly, willing evil should not make God evil. The analogy forces the opponent to admit that the attribute (seeing) does not transfer the quality of the act to the subject. They apply the same reasoning to will.

Key Terms
يرى
سفيه
سفه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The analogy compares God to humans in a literal sense.
Correction: The analogy is used to demonstrate inconsistency in the opponents' reasoning, not to equate God with humans. It argues that if a certain attribute (seeing) does not entail becoming evil, then another attribute (willing) should also not entail it.

Checkpoint
What is the analogy used in this مسألة?
A) God's hearing is like human hearing
B) Seeing evil does not make the seer evil, likewise willing evil does not make the willer evil
C) Humans are fools when they see crime
D) God does not see evil

Key Takeaway
God's will is not tainted by the evil He wills, just as His sight is not tainted by the evil He sees.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness or experience evil, do you ever feel that God is responsible in a way that makes you question His goodness? How does this lesson's argument that 'seeing evil does not make God evil, and neither does willing evil' correct that feeling? Commit to one specific action you will take the next time such a thought arises.
?
If God's will is not tainted by the evil He wills, what does that mean for your own will when you make mistakes? Are you more forgiving of yourself because God's will is pure despite willing evil? Write down one area where you are too harsh on yourself and one where you are too lenient.
?
Think of one specific evil event you have seen or experienced. After this lesson, can you honestly say that God's sight and will regarding that event do not make Him evil? What does that demand of your trust in Him, especially when you do not understand His wisdom?

God's Will and Guidance: The Objection of Compulsion Refuted
Al-Ash'ari defends that God does not guide all, and responds to the objection about compulsion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari defends God's will and guidance using the Quranic verse and refutes the objection that it implies compulsion.

Core Idea
God's will determines guidance; compulsion would not yield true guidance.

This lesson examines al-Ash'ari's argument that God does not guide everyone. He cites a Quranic verse to show that God's decree to punish some is fulfilled by not giving them guidance. The objectors reinterpret the verse as compulsion. Al-Ash'ari responds logically, showing the flaws in their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and objection
Read the Arabic passage including the verse (32:13) and the objectors' reinterpretation. Note how al-Ash'ari sets up the debate.
The verse is clear: God could have guided all but chose not to.
2
Analyze al-Ash'ari's first response
Focus on the logical argument: if compulsion made them guided, then creating disbelief would make them disbelievers. This contradicts the objectors' own claim.
The objectors claim only a disbeliever creates disbelief.
3
Understand the second response
Al-Ash'ari asks: if guidance is given by coercion, does it benefit? The objectors say no, undermining their position that coerced guidance is true guidance.
The variant reading in some manuscripts shows disagreement among objectors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال لهم : قال الله عز وجل: ﴿ وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَا نَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَنهَا وَلَكِن حَقَّ الْقَوْلُ مِي لَأَمْلَأَنَّ جَهَنَّمَ مِنَ الْجِنَّةِ وَالنَّاسِ أَجْمَعِينَ ) [السجدة : ۱۳] ، وإذا حق القول بذلك فما شاء أن تؤتي كل نفس هداها ؛ لأنه إذا لم يؤتها هداها لمـا حق القول بتعذيب الكافرين، وإذا لم يرد ذلك فقد شاء ضلالتها •
فإن قالوا: معنى ذلك لو شئنا لأجبرناهم على الهدى واضطررناهم إليه
قيل لهم : فإذا أجبرهم على الهدى واضطرهم إليه أيكونون مهتدين؟ فإن قالوا: نعم .
قيل لهم : فإذا كان إذا فعل الهدى كانوا مهتدين، فما أنكرتم لو فعل كفر الكافرين لكانوا كافرين، وهذا هدم لقولهم ؛ لأنهم زعموا أنه لا يفعل الكفر إلا كافر .
ويقال لهم أيضاً على أي وجه يؤتيهم الهدى لـو آتاهم إياه، وشاء ذلك لهم؟
فإن قالوا على الإلجاء .
قيل لهم : وإذا ألجأهم إلى ذلك هل ينفعهم ما يفعلونه على طريق الإلجاء؟ فإن قالوا: لا (۱).
(۱) في نسخ : نعم
And it is said to them: Allah, mighty and majestic, said: 'And if We had willed, We would have given every soul its guidance, but the word from Me has been justified: I will surely fill Hell with jinn and people all together' (al-Sajda 32:13). And when the word is justified by that, then He did not will to give every soul its guidance; because if He had given them their guidance, the word about tormenting the disbelievers would not have been justified. And if He did not will that, then He willed their misguidance.
If they say: The meaning is: if We had willed, We would have compelled them to guidance and forced them to it.
It is said to them: So if He compels them to guidance and forces them to it, would they be guided? If they say: Yes.
It is said to them: So if it is that when He creates guidance in them they become guided, then why do you deny that if He were to create disbelief in the disbelievers, they would be disbelievers? And this demolishes their claim, because they claim that only a disbeliever creates disbelief.
And it is also said to them: In what manner would He give them guidance if He were to give it to them and will that for them?
If they say: By coercion (ilja').
It is said to them: And if He compels them to that, would what they do by way of compulsion benefit them? If they say: No.
(Footnote: In some copies: Yes.)
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage contains a proof from Quran and a refutation of an objection. The verse (32:13) states that God could have guided all, but He decreed to fill Hell with some. So the actual non-guidance of some is by God's will. The objectors reinterpret 'if We willed' as 'if We compelled them to guidance'—saying God could have compelled them to obey. Al-Ash'ari responds: if compulsion made them guided, then they would become guided (i.e., obedient). But then by the same logic, if God were to create disbelief in them, they would become disbelievers—contrary to their claim that only a disbeliever can create disbelief. This undermines their position. Then he presses further: if guidance were given by coercion, would it benefit them? The objectors say 'No' (or according to some manuscripts 'Yes'). If no, then coerced guidance is not true guidance. The argument aims to show that God's will is not limited by human categories of compulsion; He is the creator of all acts, good and evil.

Key Terms
الهدى (al-huda)
الضلالة (al-dalala)
الإلجاء (al-ilja')
الاضطرار (al-idtirar)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's not guiding some means He is unjust; the verse shows it fulfills His decree.
Correction: God's non-guidance is part of His just decree, not a failure or injustice.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ash'ari, what do the objectors claim about the phrase 'if We had willed' in al-Sajda?
A) It means God does not will guidance for anyone
B) It means compulsion to guidance
C) It means God is unable to guide
D) It is a metaphor only

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari proves that God's will is absolute; He guides and misguides as He wills, and compulsion is irrelevant to true guidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever thought you could earn God's guidance by your own effort? This lesson shows guidance is entirely by God's will. What does that do to your reliance on yourself? Will you ask Him more humbly for it?
?
Do you secretly believe that some people's misguidance is because God is unjust? How does this verse and the argument that compulsion wouldn't benefit challenge that assumption? Are you ready to submit to His decree without accusation?
?
Are you comfortable that God's will is absolute, or does it make you uneasy about your own accountability? After reading that coerced guidance would not benefit, how does that deepen your understanding of true guidance? Will you stop pretending you are self-guided and beg Him instead?

Divine Decree
intermediate
5 min
Guidance cannot benefit if decree of punishment is inevitable
Refutation of the claim that God could guide all if He willed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine decree overrides the possibility of universal guidance, and that forced guidance does not benefit those destined for punishment, as illustrated by Pharaoh's case.

Core Idea
God's decree of punishment makes forced guidance useless, like Pharaoh's faith at drowning.

This passage tackles a common objection: if God can guide all, why does He not? The author refutes this by pointing to God's decree to fill Hell and the example of Pharaoh. Even if God compelled guidance, it would not benefit those already destined for punishment. This shows the error of thinking that universal guidance could avert divine justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the refutational style beginning with 'It is said to them'.
The passage is concise but packs a logical argument.
2
Identify the objection being refuted
The objectors claim that if God willed, He could give guidance to all. Find where this claim is implied in the passage.
The phrase 'if He willed He would have given them guidance' is the objectors' premise.
3
Examine the two key replies
First, God has decreed to fill Hell, so guidance would not benefit. Second, forced guidance didn't save Pharaoh. Note how these refute the objection.
Pharaoh's faith at drowning was compelled by the sight of death, yet it did not save him.
4
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that the objectors' statement has no meaning because guidance, even if given as they claim, does not remove punishment for those decreed to Hell.
This highlights the sovereignty of divine decree over human guidance.
5
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider how this argument relates to the concept of qadar and the balance between divine will and human responsibility.
This is a classic Ash'ari response against Qadariyya reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قيل لهم : فإذا أخبر أنه لو شاء لآتاهم الهدى لولا ما حق منه من القول أنه يملأ جهنم، وإذا كان لو ألجأهم لم يكن نافعاً لهم ولا مزيلاً للعذاب عنهم، كما لم ينفع فرعون قوله الذي قاله عند الغرق والإلجاء، فلا معنى لقولكم، لأنه لولا ما حق من القول لأوتيت كل نفس هداها، وإتيان الهدى على الوجه الذي قلتموه لا يزيل العذاب .
It is said to them: Since He informed that if He willed He would have given them guidance, were it not for the word that has been decreed from Him that He will fill Hell, and if He were to compel them it would not benefit them nor remove punishment from them, just as the saying of Pharaoh which he said at the time of drowning and compulsion did not benefit him, so your statement has no meaning, because were it not for the word that has been decreed, every soul would have been given its guidance, and the bringing of guidance in the manner you claim does not remove punishment.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection raised by the Qadariyya or similar groups. The objectors argued that if God willed, He could give guidance to all, so why does He not? The author replies by first noting that God has already informed that He has decreed to fill Hell with jinn and mankind. Therefore, even if God were to compel guidance, it would not benefit those destined for punishment, just as Pharaoh's declaration of faith at the moment of drowning—when he was compelled by the sight of death—did not save him. The author concludes that the objectors' premise that universal guidance would remove punishment is false; divine decree overrides mere guidance.

Key Terms
الهدى
العذاب
الإلجاء
القول الحق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God willed to guide all, He would save all, implying He must do so.
Correction: God's decree to fill Hell overrides any universal guidance; forced guidance does not remove punishment, as Pharaoh's case demonstrates.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that forced guidance would not benefit those destined for Hell?
A) Because guidance is only beneficial when chosen freely.
B) Because Pharaoh's forced faith at drowning did not save him.
C) Because God's decree of punishment overrides any guidance.
D) Because the objectors misinterpreted the verse.

Key Takeaway
Divine decree of punishment renders forced guidance ineffective; the example of Pharaoh proves that compulsion cannot remove divine punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever put off sincere repentance, hoping that a last-minute, forced change of heart would save you from consequences you knew were coming? Pharaoh's faith at drowning was too late and didn't benefit him. What does that teach you about the urgency of genuine submission to God's decrees today?
?
Read the passage again: 'the bringing of guidance in the manner you claim does not remove punishment.' In what area of your life are you relying on a formality of faith—like just saying words or performing rituals—rather than a deep, lived obedience that transforms your relationship with God's will? What concrete step can you take this week to move from forced habit to authentic guidance?
?
If you truly believed that God's decree of punishment is certain for some, would your prayers and efforts to guide others change? How does this passage confront any complacency you might have about sharing faith with those who seem far from God?

Divine Decree
intermediate

God Withholds Provision to Prevent Universal Rebellion
Proof from Quran that God's withholding of provision is wise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's withholding of provision is an act of divine wisdom, as demonstrated by two Quranic verses.

Core Idea
God's restraint in provision prevents widespread transgression and disbelief.

This lesson examines a key argument from Imam al-Ash'ari's Al-Ibanah. Using two Quranic verses, the author demonstrates that God's deliberate withholding of provision is not a flaw but a wise measure to prevent universal rebellion and disbelief. The passage refutes those who question why God does not give more to all people.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and verses
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the two Quranic verses cited: al-Shura 27 and al-Zukhruf 33.
The verses are central to the argument.
2
Understand the logic of divine knowledge
The author argues that God's knowledge of outcomes determines His actions. He knows that if He extended provision, people would transgress; if He gave disbelievers luxury, all would follow disbelief.
This shows God's wisdom in restraint.
3
Reflect on the refutation
The author challenges objectors to deny this logic. God's actions are consistent with His will and knowledge.
The passage defends God's wisdom against criticism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٠٥- مسألة أخرى : ويقال لهم : قال الله عز وجل : ( وَلَوْ بَسَط اللهُ الرِّزْقَ لِعِبَادِهِ، لَبَغَوْا فِي الْأَرْضِ ) [الشورى: ٢٧] وقال تعالى: ﴿ وَلَوْلَا أَن يَكُونَ النَّاسُ أُمَّةً وَاحِدَةً لَجَعَلْنَا لِمَن يَكْفُرُ بِالرَّحْمَنِ لِبُيُوتِهِمْ سُقفا من فِضَّةٍ ﴾ [الزخرف:٣٣] مخبراً أنه لولا أن يكون الناس مجتمعين على الكفر لبسط للكافرين الرزق، وجعل لبيوتهم سقفاً من فضة، لكنه لم يبسط لهم الرزق، ولم يجعل للكافرين سقفاً من فضة، فما أنكرتم من أنه تعالى لو لم يرد أن يكون الكافرون ما خلقه، علمه بأنه إذا خلقهم كانوا كافرين، كما أنه لو أراد أن يكون الناس على الكفر مجتمعين لجعل للكافرين سقفاً من فضة ومعارج عليها يظهرون ؛ لكنه لم يجعل للكافرين سقفاً من فضة ومعارج عليها يظهرون، لئلا يكونوا الناس جميعاً على الكفر متطابقين، إذا كان في علمه أنه لو فعل ذلك لكانوا جميعاً على الكفر متطابقين .
Another issue: And it is said to them: Allah Almighty said: {And if Allah had extended provision for His servants, they would have transgressed in the earth} [al-Shura:27], and He said: {And were it not that the people would become one community [of disbelievers], We would have made for those who disbelieve in the Most Merciful roofs of silver for their houses} [al-Zukhruf:33], informing that were it not that people would become united upon disbelief, He would have extended provision for the disbelievers and made for their houses roofs of silver. But He did not extend provision for them, nor did He make for the disbelievers roofs of silver. So what do you deny of the fact that the Exalted, if He did not will that the disbelievers be as He created them, [yet] He knew that if He created them they would be disbelievers, just as if He willed that people be united upon disbelief, He would have made for the disbelievers roofs of silver and stairways upon which they ascend? But He did not make for the disbelievers roofs of silver and stairways upon which they ascend, lest all people become mutually agreeing upon disbelief, because in His knowledge, if He did that they would all be mutually agreeing upon disbelief.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a proof using two Quranic verses to refute the claim that God should have given all people guidance or wealth. The author presents two divine actions: God withholds abundant provision to prevent transgression (baghy), and He withholds material blessings from disbelievers to prevent universal agreement on disbelief. The argument is that God's knowledge of outcomes determines His actions: He knows that if He provided all, they would rebel; if He gave disbelievers luxury, all would follow disbelief. Therefore, God's wise restraint is consistent with His will and knowledge. The author challenges the objectors to deny this logic.

Key Terms
الرزق
البغي
الكفر
الأمة الواحدة
المعارج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because God has the power to give more, He should give more to everyone, and His withholding seems arbitrary or cruel.
Correction: The verses show that God's withholding is a wise act based on His knowledge that abundance would lead to transgression and universal disbelief, preventing greater harm.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does God not provide all people with abundant wealth?
A) Because He is not able to.
B) Because it would lead to transgression in the earth.
C) Because it would make people disbelieve.
D) Because the disbelievers do not deserve it.

Key Takeaway
God's withholding of provision is a wise act based on His knowledge that abundance would lead to transgression and disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that God is holding back something you deserve, like wealth or success? After reading this lesson, could there be a wisdom in that withholding that you didn't see? Will you trust His knowledge over your feelings?
?
If you knew that having more money would make you arrogant, neglect prayer, or mistreat others, would you still ask God for it? How should this lesson change the way you make dua for provision?
?
Are you secretly envious of those who have more worldly blessings, forgetting that God may be protecting your faith by not giving you everything? How can you actively combat that envy with the truth from this passage?

God's Power and the Refutation of the Qadariyya
Refutation of Qadariyya on God's ability to create disbelief

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the analogical argument used by Imam al-Ash'ari to refute the Qadariyya claim that God cannot create disbelief.

Core Idea
God's power over disbelief is proven by His empowering servants over it.

Imam al-Ash'ari presents a crisp logical refutation of the Qadariyya who deny that God creates evil acts. He uses an analogy from God's knowledge to God's power, showing consistency in divine attributes. This passage grounds the Ash'ari position on qadar.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: a heading, then a question to the Qadariyya, then an analogy, then a conclusion with a Qur'anic verse.
The passage is a single continuous argument.
2
Identify the analogy
Find the two parallel statements: about teaching and about empowering. Understand how they are used to force a conclusion about God's ability to create disbelief.
3
Understand the implication about God's will
The passage concludes by quoting a verse about God doing whatever He wills. Reflect on how this connects God's will to His creation of disbelief.
This is a key point in the Ash'ari doctrine of qadar.
4
Consider the refutation
Ask yourself: how does this argument refute the Qadariyya position? The commentary will help clarify the logical steps.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٠٦ - مسألة : الباب الحادي عشر في تقدير أعمال العباد والاستطاعة والتعديل والتجوير (1) يقال للقدرية : هل يجوز أن يُعلم الله عز وجل عباده شيئاً لا يعلمه؟ فإن قالوا: لا يُعلم الله عباده شيئاً إلا وهو به عالم. قيل لهم : فكذلك لا يقدرهم على شيء إلا وهو عليه قادر، فلا بد من الإجابة إلى ذلك. فيقال لهم: فإذا أقدرهم على الكفر، فهو قادر أن يخلق الكفر لهم، وإذا قدر على خلق الكفر لهم فلم أثبتم أن يخلق كفرهم فاسداً متناقضاً باطلاً، وقد قال تعالى: (فَعَالُ لِمَا يُرِيدُ) [هود:107، البروج:16] وإذا كان الكفر مما أراد الله فقد فعله وقَدَّرَهُ
206 – Issue: The eleventh chapter on the decree of the deeds of servants, and capacity, and the assertion of justice and injustice. It is said to the Qadariyya: Is it permissible that Allah Almighty teaches His servants something He does not know? It is said to them: Likewise, He does not empower them over anything except that He is capable of it, so there is no avoiding agreement to that. And He said: {Doer of whatever He wills} [Hud:107, al-Buruj:16]. And if disbelief is something Allah willed, then He has done it and decreed it.

Commentary
This passage begins with a chapter heading on predestination of actions, capacity, and divine justice. The author then presents a refutation of the Qadariyya (those who deny predestination of evil). The argument proceeds analogically: just as God does not teach something He does not know, He does not empower someone over something He is not able to do. Therefore, if God empowers a person over disbelief, He is necessarily able to create that disbelief in them. Denying that God creates disbelief is contradictory. The author cites the verse 'Doer of whatever He wills' to assert that God's will encompasses disbelief, and thus He creates and decrees it.

Refuting the Qadariyya on Divine Kindness
Refutation of the Qadariyya argument about God's grace

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's withholding of certain blessings is itself an act of wisdom, refuting the Qadariyya claim that God must always grant grace.

Core Idea
God's kindness includes withholding what would cause harm.

The Qadariyya argued that God's grace requires Him to always benefit His creation. Imam al-Ash'ari responds by citing divine foreknowledge: God knows that certain blessings would lead to transgression or disbelief, so He withholds them out of wisdom. This passage anchors that argument in a Quranic verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the rhetorical question that challenges the Qadariyya position.
The verse is from Surah ash-Shura (42:27).
2
Identify the Qadariyya claim being refuted
Understand that the Qadariyya believed God's 'lutf' (kindness) obligates Him to always do what is most beneficial for His servants.
The refutation shows that God's knowledge prevents that.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
Read the verse: 'And if Allah had extended provision for His servants, they would have transgressed in the earth.' Note how it directly supports the argument.
4
Reflect on divine wisdom
Consider that God's withholding of blessings is itself an act of kindness, because He knows the harmful consequences.
This principle applies to all divine decrees.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٠٧- مسألة : ويُرَدُّ عليهم في اللطف. يقال لهم : أليس الله عز وجل قادراً على أن يفعل بخلقه من بسط الرزق ما لو فعله بهم لبغوا؟ وأن يفعل بهم ما لو فعله بالكفار لكفروا ؟ كما قال : ( وَلَوْ بَسَط اللهُ الرِّزْقَ لِعِبَادِهِ، لَبَغَوْا فِي الْأَرْضِ )

It is said to them: Is not Allah Almighty capable of doing with His creation such expansion of provision that if He did it they would transgress? And such doing with them that if He did it with the disbelievers they would disbelieve? As He said: {And if Allah had extended provision for His servants, they would have transgressed in the earth}.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya concerning the concept of 'lutf' (divine kindness or grace). The Qadariyya might argue that God should always do what is most kind and beneficial for His servants, such as giving them guidance or prosperity. The author responds by pointing out that God is indeed powerful enough to expand provision or grant signs that would lead people to faith. However, He refrains because He knows through His foreknowledge that such actions would lead to transgression or disbelief, not benefit. The verse from al-Shura is cited to support this: God withholds provision to prevent rebellion. Thus, God's withholding is itself an act of wisdom and kindness.

C) Because the Qadariyya deny it.

Key Takeaway
God's foreknowledge of harm justifies His withholding of certain blessings, which is itself an act of divine kindness and wisdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Refuting Qadariyya on God's Power and Creation of Actions
Al-Ash'ari refutes the Qadariyya using a logical parallel and a Quranic verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari uses the parallel between God's knowledge and power to refute the Qadariyya on the creation of human actions.

Core Idea
God's empowerment implies His ability to create; nothing escapes His will.

In this passage, al-Ash'ari presents a concise logical argument against the Qadariyya, who deny that Allah creates human actions. By drawing a parallel between God's knowledge and His power, he shows that if God empowers someone for an act, He must be able to create that act. This leads to the conclusion that disbelief, if willed by God, is created by Him.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing, then read the full translation. Notice the structure: a chapter title, then a refutation in the form of a question-and-answer.
The title indicates the topic: the decree of actions, capability, and the issue of justice.
2
Trace the logical argument
Identify the parallel al-Ash'ari draws between God's teaching and His empowering. Just as God only teaches what He knows, He only empowers for what He is capable of. Then see how this leads to the conclusion that if God empowers for disbelief, He must be able to create disbelief.
This is a qiyas (analogical reasoning) that forces the opponent to accept the consequence.
3
Reflect on the Quranic proof
Al-Ash'ari cites the verse 'Doer of whatever He wills' to support that if disbelief is willed by God, He does it and decrees it. Consider how this verse seals the argument against the Qadariyya.
The verse establishes that God's will is always effective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الحادي عشر في تقدير أعمال العباد والاستطاعة والتعديل والتجوير
يقال للقدرية : هل يجوز أن يُعلم الله عز وجل عباده شيئاً لا يعلمه؟ فإن قالوا: لا يُعلم الله عباده شيئاً إلا وهو به عالم.
قيل لهم : فكذلك لا يقدرهم على شيء إلا وهو عليه قادر، فلا بد من الإجابة إلى ذلك.
فيقال لهم: فإذا أقدرهم على الكفر، فهو قادر أن يخلق الكفر لهم، وإذا قدر على خلق الكفر لهم فلم أثبتم أن يخلق كفرهم فاسداً متناقضاً باطلاً، وقد قال تعالى: (فَعَالُ لِمَا يُرِيدُ) [هود: 107، والبروج: 16] وإذا كان الكفر مما أراد الله فقد فعله وقدره
Chapter Eleven: On the Decree of the Actions of Servants, and Capability, and Justification and Injustice.
It is said to the Qadariyya: Is it permissible for Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, to teach His servants something He does not know? If they say: Allah does not teach His servants anything except that He knows it.
It is said to them: Likewise, He does not empower them for anything except that He is capable of it. So they must answer that.
Then it is said to them: If He empowered them for disbelief, then He is able to create disbelief for them. And if He is able to create disbelief for them, why do you assert that His creating their disbelief is corrupt, contradictory, and false? And He, exalted, said: 'Doer of whatever He wills' [Hud 107; al-Buruj 16]. And if disbelief is something Allah willed, then He has done it and decreed it.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya who deny that Allah creates human actions. Al-Ash'ari begins by establishing a parallel between God's knowledge and His power: just as God does not teach what He does not know, He does not empower for what He is not capable. Therefore, when God empowers someone for disbelief, He must be capable of creating disbelief in them. The Qadariyya claim that God's creating disbelief would be corrupt and false, but Al-Ash'ari counters with the verse 'Doer of whatever He wills', arguing that whatever Allah wills, He does and decrees. Thus, if disbelief is willed by Allah, He creates it, refuting the Qadariyya position.

Key Terms

الاستطاعة
التعديل والتجوير
العلم
القدرة
خلق الكفر
الإرادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qadariyya believe that if God empowers humans for an action, the action is independent of God's creation.
Correction: Empowerment does not imply independence; it implies God's ability to create that action. God's power and will encompass all actions.

Checkpoint
What is the logical consequence of the Qadariyya admitting that God empowers for disbelief?
A) God must be able to create disbelief.
B) God cannot create disbelief.
C) God's knowledge is limited.
D) Humans create their own disbelief.

Key Takeaway
God's empowerment of an act entails His ability to create it, and His will is always effective, so all actions, including disbelief, are created by Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Refuting Qadariyya on Divine Grace (Lutf)
Al-Ash'ari refutes Qadariyya on lutf via Qur'anic precedent and analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Ash'ari's argument that God's ability to cause disbelief implies His ability to cause belief through divine grace (lutf).

Core Idea
If God can cause disbelief, He can cause belief through grace.

Al-Ash'ari challenges the Qadariyya by pointing to Qur'anic verses where God's actions lead to transgression or disbelief. He then uses a parity argument: if God can cause negative outcomes, He can also cause positive ones like faith through lutf. This refutes the Qadariyya denial of God's role in creating belief.

Guided Path
1
Examine the Qur'anic examples
Read the two verses cited and note how God's actions (expanding provision, giving wealth) lead to specific outcomes (transgression, disbelief).
These establish that God's actions can cause human responses.
2
Identify the logical premise
Al-Ash'ari states that God is able to do things that cause disbelief. Accepting this, the Qadariyya cannot deny that God can also do things that cause belief.
The argument uses analogy: if cause A leads to effect B, then similar cause can lead to similar effect.
3
Understand the conclusion
The conclusion is that God is able to grant lutf (divine grace) that would cause all people to believe, just as He is able to cause all to disbelieve.
This undermines the Qadariyya position that God does not create faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويرد عليهم في اللطف. يقال لهم : أليس الله عز وجل قادراً على أن يفعل بخلقه من بسط الرزق ما لو فعله بهم لبغوا؟ وأن يفعل بهم ما لو فعله بالكفار لكفروا؟ كما قال: (وَلَوْ بَسَطَ اللهُ الرِّزْقَ لِعِبَادِهِ لَبَغَوْا فِي الْأَرْضِ) [الشورى: 27] وكما قال: (وَلَوْلَا أَنْ يَكُونَ النَّاسُ أُمَّةً وَاحِدَةً لَجَعَلْنَا لِمَنْ يَكْفُرُ بِالرَّحْمَنِ لِبُيُوتِهِمْ سُقُفًا مِنْ فِضَّةٍ) [الزخرف: 33]. فلا بد من نعم. فيقال لهم : فما أنكرتم من أنه قادر على أن يفعل بهم لطفاً لو فعله بهم لآمنوا أجمعون، كما أنه قادر أن يفعل بهم أمراً لو فعله بهم لكفروا كلهم.
And a refutation is made against them concerning lutf (divine grace). It is said to them: Is not Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, able to do with His creation such an expansion of provision that if He did it they would transgress? And to do with them such that if He did it with the disbelievers they would disbelieve? As He said: 'If Allah had expanded provision for His servants, they would have transgressed in the land' [Ash-Shura 27] and as He said: 'And if it were not that people would become one community, We would have made for those who disbelieve in the Most Merciful ceilings of silver for their houses' [Az-Zukhruf 33]. So a confirmation is necessary. Then it is said to them: So why do you deny that He is able to do with them a grace (lutf) such that if He did it they would all believe, just as He is able to do with them a matter such that if He did it they would all disbelieve.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya regarding the concept of lutf (divine grace). Al-Ash'ari first cites two Quranic verses showing that God's actions (like expanding provision or giving wealth) can lead to specific outcomes—transgression or disbelief. He then argues that if God can cause disbelief by such actions, He must also be able to cause belief by granting a lutf. The Qadariyya cannot deny this power because they already accept that God can cause disbelief. Thus, the argument undermines their position that God does not create faith or disbelief in humans.

Key Terms
اللطف
البغي
القدرة
الإيمان
الكفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qadariyya believe that God cannot cause belief in humans without compulsion.
Correction: The argument shows that God can cause belief through lutf, just as He can cause disbelief through other actions.

Checkpoint
What does Al-Ash'ari argue about God's ability to do lutf?
A) God is unable to do lutf.
B) God can do lutf just as He can do things that cause disbelief.
C) Lutf is impossible.
D) Lutf is only for prophets.

Key Takeaway
God's power to cause disbelief through His actions logically entails His power to cause belief through divine grace.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you recognize that your own faith is a direct gift of God's grace, not a product of your own effort? If God chose to withhold that grace, could you still believe? How does that make you feel right now?
?
When you see others who disbelieve, do you assume it is only due to their choices, or do you acknowledge that God could have caused them to believe (as He could cause you to disbelieve)? How should that humility change the way you view them?
?
If God's power permits Him to cause any human action, including belief and disbelief, are you living today as though your salvation depends entirely on His mercy? What would change in your daily dua and reliance if you truly believed that?

Refuting Qadariyya: God's Specific Grace to Believers
Al-Ash'ari poses a dilemma to the Qadariyya using Quranic verses on God's specific grace.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ash'ari uses Quranic verses to pose a decisive dilemma against the Qadariyya's denial of God's exclusive grace and predestination.

Core Idea
God's special grace to believers proves His will is decisive, not equal treatment.

Al-Ash'ari now turns to a direct scriptural argument. He cites three verses where God explicitly mentions His grace, mercy, and favor upon believers as something that saved them from misguidance and purification. This sets up a powerful dilemma that forces the Qadariyya to either admit God's selective grace or confront a logical impossibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the verses carefully
Read each Quranic verse cited by Al-Ash'ari and note the specific blessing mentioned (grace, mercy, favor). Observe how each one conditions the believers' guidance and purification on God's action.
The verses are from An-Nisa 83, An-Nur 21, and As-Saffat 55-57.
2
Identify the question Al-Ash'ari poses
After citing the verses, Al-Ash'ari asks a direct question: is this grace something God did not do for the disbelievers and specifically gave to believers? Locate this question in the passage.
3
Analyze the two possible answers
Consider both possible responses from the Qadariyya. If they say yes (God withheld it from disbelievers), they contradict their own stance. If they say no (God gave the same to all), then why are disbelievers not purified? Work through the logic.
This is the heart of the dilemma.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال لهم : أليس قد قال الله عز وجل: (وَلَوْلَا فَضْلُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَتُهُ لَاتَّبَعْتُمُ الشَّيْطَانَ إِلَّا قَلِيلًا) [النساء: 83] و(وَلَوْلَا فَضْلُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَتُهُ مَا زَكَى مِنْكُمْ مِنْ أَحَدٍ أَبَدًا) [النور: 21] وقال: (فَاطَّلَعَ فَرَاهُ فِي سَوَاءِ الْجَحِيمِ * قَالَ تَاللهِ إِنْ كِدْتَ لَتُرْدِينِ * وَلَوْلَا نِعْمَةُ رَبِّي لَكُنْتُ مِنَ الْمُحْضَرِينَ) [الصافات: 55-57]. ما الفضل الذي فعله بالمؤمنين، الذي لو لم يفعله لاتبعوا الشيطان، ولو لم يفعله ما زكى منهم من أحد أبدا؟ وما النعمة التي لو لم يفعلها لكانوا من المحضرين؟ وهل ذلك شيء لم يفعله بالكافرين وخص به المؤمنين؟ فإن قالوا: نعم، فقد تركوا قولهم، وأثبتوا الله عز وجل نعماً وفضلاً على المؤمنين ابتدأهم بجميعه، ولم ينعم بمثله على الكافرين، وصاروا إلى القول بالحق وإن قالوا: قد فعل الله ذلك أجمع بالكافرين لما فعله بالمؤمنين فقل لهم. فإذا كان الله قد فعل ذلك أجمع بالكافرين، فلم يكونوا زاكين
And it is said to them: Is it not that Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, said: 'And if not for the grace of Allah upon you and His mercy, you would have followed Shaytan, except a few' [An-Nisa 83] and 'And if not for the grace of Allah upon you and His mercy, not one of you would have ever been purified' [An-Nur 21] and He said: 'Then he looked and saw him in the midst of the Hellfire. He said: By Allah, you almost ruined me. And if not for the favor of my Lord, I would have been among those brought forward [to punishment]' [As-Saffat 55-57]. What is the grace that He did for the believers, such that if He had not done it they would have followed Shaytan, and if He had not done it none of them would ever have been purified? And what is the favor that if He had not done it they would have been among those brought forward? And is that something He did not do for the disbelievers and specified the believers with it? If they say: Yes, then they have abandoned their statement, and they have affirmed that Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, has favors and graces upon the believers that He initiated all of them with, and did not grant the like to the disbelievers, and they have come to the truth. And if they say: Allah has done all of that for the disbelievers just as He did for the believers, then say to them: If Allah has done all of that for the disbelievers, then why were they not purified?
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage presents a dilemma to the Qadariyya. Al-Ash'ari cites three Quranic verses that mention specific graces (fadl, ni'mah) given to believers that prevented them from following Shaytan, purified them, and saved them from punishment. He then asks whether these graces were exclusively given to believers and withheld from disbelievers. If the Qadariyya answer 'yes', they admit that God distinguishes between people with His grace, contradicting their denial of divine predestination. If they answer 'no', claiming that God gave the same to disbelievers, then why were disbelievers not purified? Either way, their position collapses.

Key Terms
الفضل
الرحمة
النعمة
التزكية
المحضرين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Qadariyya believe that God treats all humans equally in terms of guidance, giving everyone the same grace and ability to choose good, independent of divine will.
Correction: The Quranic verses show that God grants specific grace, mercy, and favor to believers that He does not grant to disbelievers, proving that guidance and purification are solely by God's choice, not human will alone.

Checkpoint
What is the dilemma posed to the Qadariyya in this passage?
A) Either God gives special grace to believers or He does not.
B) Either God is unjust or He is omnipotent.
C) Either God creates actions or humans do.
D) Either the Qur'an is created or uncreated.

Key Takeaway
God's selective grace to believers is a clear refutation of Qadari claims that all human outcomes are equally from human free will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your faith is a gift from God, or do you secretly think you earned it? How would your humility change if you fully acknowledged that without His grace you would be lost?
?
If God's grace is selective, does that make you uncomfortable? Are you willing to trust His wisdom even when it challenges your sense of fairness?
?
When you look at disbelievers, do you see them as simply having chosen wrong, or do you recognize that without God's grace, you would be in the same position? How should that shape your attitude toward them?

Refuting the Mu'tazilite View on Equal Divine Favor
Ash'ari refutes Mu'tazilite equal favor theory using Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari uses Quranic verses and rational argument to refute the Mu'tazilite claim that God treats all people equally in terms of divine favor.

Core Idea
Divine favor is not equal; God singles out believers with special grace.

The Mu'tazilites argued that God must grant equal favor to all, or that He does the best for everyone. Imam al-Ash'ari refutes this by pointing to clear Quranic verses that speak of God's special favors to believers—favors that if withheld, would lead to misguidance. This passage challenges us to think about the nature of divine grace and why it is not distributed uniformly.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the rhythm of the argument come through.
Notice the opening assertion 'fala budda min na'am'.
2
Understand the opening assertion
Ash'ari begins by stating that there must be favors—this is a direct refutation of equal treatment. He then asserts God's ability to grant a kindness that would cause all to believe, just as He could cause all to disbelieve.
This sets up the framework for differential divine action.
3
Identify the three Quranic verses
Ash'ari cites verses 4:83, 24:21, and 37:55-57. Read each one and note what they say about God's favor preventing misguidance and punishment.
These verses are the core evidence.
4
Follow the logical questioning
Ash'ari asks: What is this favor? Was it given to disbelievers? If opponents admit it was not, they have conceded the truth. If they claim it was, then why are disbelievers not purified?
The dilemma forces the opponent to accept special favor.
5
Grasp the analogy and conclusion
The analogy of hands and feet shows that if the opponent claims equal favors, the same logic would lead to absurd conclusions. The conclusion is that God singles out believers with tawfiq and tasdid.
This seals the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا بد من نعم . فيقال لهم : فما أنكرتم من أنه قادر على أن يفعل بهم لطفاً لو فعله بهم لآمنوا أجمعون، كما أنه قادر أن يفعل بهم أمراً لو فعله بهم لكفروا كلهم . ۲۰۷- مسألة أخرى : ويقال لهم : أليس قد قال الله عز وجل: وَلَوْلَا فَضْلُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَتُهُ لاتَّبَعْتُمُ الشَّيْطَانَ إِلَّا قَلِيلًا ﴾ [النساء : ۸۳] وَلَوْلَا فَضْلُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَتُهُ مَا زَكَى مِنكُم مِّنْ أحد أبدا [النور: ۲۱] وقال: ﴿ فَاطَّلَعَ فَرَاهُ في سَوَاءِ الجَحِيمِ ﴾ [الصافات: ٥٥] يعني في وسط الجحيم، ﴿ قَالَ تَاللهِ إن كدت لَتُردِينِ * وَلَوْلَا نِعْمَةُ رَبِّ لَكُنتُ مِنَ الْمُحْضَرِينَ ﴾ [الصافات:٥٦-٥٧] . ما الفضل الذي فعله بالمؤمنين، الذي لو لم يفعله لاتبعوا الشيطان، ولو لم يفعله ما زكى منهم من أحد أبداً ؟ وما النعمة التي لو لم يفعلها لكانوا من المحضرين؟ وهل ذلك شيء لم يفعله بالكافرين وخص به المؤمنين؟ فإن قالوا: نعم، فقد تركوا قولهم، وأثبتوا الله عز وجل نعماً وفضلاً على المؤمنين ابتدأهم بجميعه، ولم ينعم بمثله على الكافرين، وصاروا إلى القول بالحق وإن قالوا: قد فعل الله ذلك أجمع بالكافرين لما فعله بالمؤمنين فقل الهم. فإذا كان الله قد فعل ذلك أجمع بالكافرين، فلم يكونوا زاكين وكانوا للشيطان متبعين، وفي النار محضرين وهل يجوز أن يقول للمؤمنين: لولا أني خلقت لكم أيد وأرجل لكنتم للشيطان متبعين؟ وهو قد خلق الأيدي والأرجل للكافرين وكانوا للشيطان متبعین فإن قالوا: لا يجوز ذلك قيل لهم : وكذلك لا يجوز ما قلتموه . وهذا يبين أن الله عز وجل اختص المؤمنين من النعم والتوفيق والتسديد بما لم يُعط الكافرين وفضل عليهم المؤمنين .
So there must be favors. And it is said to them: What prevents you from [accepting] that He is able to do for them a kindness (luṭf) such that if He did it to them they would all believe, just as He is able to do for them a thing such that if He did it to them they would all disbelieve. 207- Another issue: And it is said to them: Did not God Almighty say: 'And if not for the favor of God upon you and His mercy, you would have followed Satan, except a few' (4:83), and 'And if not for the favor of God upon you and His mercy, none of you would have been purified ever' (24:21), and He said: 'And he looked and saw him in the midst of the Blazing Fire, he said: By God, you almost ruined me, and if not for the favor of my Lord, I would have been among those brought [to punishment]' (37:55-57). What is the favor that He did for the believers, which if He had not done they would have followed Satan, and if He had not done, none of them would ever have been purified? And what is the grace that if He had not done, they would have been among those brought [to punishment]? Is that something He did not do for the disbelievers and singled out the believers with it? If they say: Yes, then they have abandoned their statement and affirmed for God Almighty favors and grace upon the believers, initiating them with all of it, and He did not bestow the like of it upon the disbelievers, and they have come to the truth. And if they say: God did all of that for the disbelievers just as He did for the believers, then say: [؟]. So if God did all of that for the disbelievers, why were they not purified and were followers of Satan and were brought into the Fire? Is it permissible to say to the believers: 'If I had not created for you hands and feet, you would have followed Satan'? – when He created hands and feet for the disbelievers and they were followers of Satan? If they say: That is not permissible, it is said to them: Likewise, what you have said is not permissible. And this shows that God Almighty singled out the believers with blessings, success (tawfīq), and guidance (tasdīd) that He did not give to the disbelievers, and He favored the believers over them.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position that God must grant equal favors to all, or that He does the best (al-aṣlaḥ) for everyone. Ash'ari begins by asserting that there must be distinguishing favors from God. He then poses a series of questions to the opponents: Why do you deny that God could grant a kindness (luṭf) that would cause all to believe, just as He could cause all to disbelieve? He then cites three Quranic verses: 4:83 states that without God's favor and mercy, believers would have followed Satan except a few; 24:21 says that without God's favor and mercy, none would ever be purified; 37:55-57 describe a person in Paradise thanking God for saving him from Hell by His grace. Ash'ari then asks: What is this favor that was done for believers, which if not done would have resulted in following Satan and impurity? Was this favor not done for disbelievers but specifically given to believers? If the opponent admits 'Yes,' then they have abandoned their original claim (that God treats all equally) and acknowledged special favors – this is the truth. If they claim that God did the same for disbelievers, then why were disbelievers not purified and why did they follow Satan and end up in Hell? This creates a contradiction. Ash'ari then uses an analogy: If someone said to believers, 'If I had not created hands and feet for you, you would have followed Satan,' yet disbelievers also have hands and feet but still followed Satan, the analogy shows the opponent's position is invalid. The conclusion is that God singles out believers with particular blessings, success (tawfīq), and guidance (tasdīd) not given to disbelievers, thus establishing the reality of divine grace and disproving the Mu'tazilite view of equal treatment.

Key Terms
فضل (favor)
نعمة (grace)
لطف (kindness)
توفيق (success)
تسديد (guidance)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's grace is identical for all people, and He treats everyone equally in terms of favor.
Correction: Ash'ari shows through Quranic verses that believers receive special favors not given to disbelievers, such as guidance and success, that prevent them from following Satan.

Checkpoint
According to Ash'ari's argument, what do the verses from Surah an-Nisa and an-Nur prove about God's favor?
A) God gives equal favors to all people.
B) Without God's favor, believers would follow Satan and be impure.
C) Disbelievers also receive the same favor but reject it.
D) Favor is earned by human effort.

Key Takeaway
Divine favor is not uniform; God grants specific graces to believers that He withholds from others, as shown in the Quran and logic.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own life, can you point to specific moments when God's favor kept you from following Satan? How does this lesson make you accountable for the grace you have received?
?
Do you secretly believe that your faith is due to your own intelligence or effort? How does Ash'ari's refutation force you to admit that without God's exclusive grace, you would be among the disbelievers?
?
If God had not granted you tawfiq and tasdid, where would you be today? How does that realization change the way you view those who have not received the same favor? What is your responsibility toward them?
