Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari uses the analogy of Iblis's call to show that God's call to faith is guidance only for those who accept it, not for those who reject it.

?
If God's guidance is only effective for those who accept, then your faith is proof that He has singled you out. Refuting Universal Guidance with 'Many' vs 'All'
Al-Ash'ari uses Qur'an 2:26 to refute universal guidance by focusing on 'many' not 'all'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari uses a simple linguistic contrast between 'many' and 'all' in Qur'an 2:26 to refute the claim that God guides all of creation.

Core Idea
If God intended to guide all, He would have said 'all' – but He said 'many' instead.

This lesson presents al-Ash'ari's concise argument from al-Ibanah. He quotes a Quranic verse and highlights that the word 'many' (كثير) is used, not 'all' (الكل). By drawing attention to this choice of wording, he shows that the verse actually contradicts the Mu'tazilite position of universal guidance. Let's see how he builds this argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Pay attention to the key words 'كثيرًا' and 'الكل'.
The verse is from al-Baqarah 2:26.
2
Identify the key contrast
Note that the verse uses 'كثيرًا' (many) for both leading astray and guiding. Al-Ash'ari contrasts this with 'الكل' (all).
3
Follow the logical implication
Al-Ash'ari argues: if God intended to lead all astray or guide all, He would have said 'all'. Since He said 'many', it implies not all.
This is a simple linguistic argument based on word choice.
4
See the invalidation of the opponent's claim
The opponent's statement that God guides all of creation (هدى الخلق أجمعين) is directly contradicted by the verse, which says He guides 'many' not 'all'.
5
Reflect on the method
Notice how al-Ash'ari uses a single verse's wording to refute a theological position. This is a common method in kalam: using precise Quranic language as evidence.
Linguistic analysis is a key tool in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال لهم: أليس قال الله عز وجل: ﴿يُضِلُّ بِهِ كَثِيرًا وَيَهْدِي بِهِ كَثِيرًا﴾ [البقرة: ٢٦] فهل يدل قوله: ﴿يُضِلُّ بِهِ كَثِيرًا﴾ على أنه لم يضل الكل؛ لأنه لو أراد الكل لقال: يضل به الكل، فلما قال: ﴿يُضِلُّ بِهِ كَثِيرًا﴾ علمنا أنه لم يضل الكل؟ فلا بد من نعم. فيقال لهم: فما أنكرتم أن قوله تعالى: ﴿وَيَهْدِي بِهِ كَثِيرًا﴾ دليل على أنه لم يرد الكل؛ لأنه لو أراد الكل لقال: ويهدي به الكل، فلما قال: ﴿وَيَهْدِي بِهِ كَثِيرًا﴾ علمنا أنه لم يهد الكل، وفي هذا إبطال قولكم: إن الله هدى الخلق أجمعين.
And it is said to them: Did not God say: 'He leads astray many thereby and guides many thereby' (al-Baqarah 2:26)? Does His saying 'He leads astray many' indicate that He did not lead all astray? Because if He intended all, He would have said 'He leads all astray'. When He said 'He leads astray many', we know that He did not lead all astray. So they must answer yes. Then it is said to them: So why do you deny that His saying 'and He guides many' is evidence that He did not intend all? Because if He intended all, He would have said 'and He guides all'. When He said 'and He guides many', we know that He did not guide all. And in this is an invalidation of your statement that God guided all of creation.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is another polemical argument (مسألة) that uses a direct Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:26) to refute the Mu'tazilite claim that God guides all people (هدى الخلق أجمعين). The argument is a simple linguistic one: the verse uses the word 'many' (كثيرًا) for both leading astray and guiding. If God intended universal guidance and misguidance, He would have said 'all' (الكل). Since He said 'many', it implies exclusivity. The opponents are forced to admit that the verse does not indicate universal guidance. Al-Ash'ari then concludes that this invalidates their position. The argument relies on the principle that the choice of wording (كثير vs. كل) is deliberate and meaningful.

Key Terms
يضل

Reductio on Guidance: Why God's Call Cannot Benefit Rejectors
Al-Ash'ari argues against Mu'tazilite view on guidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari uses a reductio argument to show that calling God's call 'guidance' for rejecting disbelievers leads to contradictions.

Core Idea
If the call is guidance, then disbelievers must also be reformed and protected—but they are forsaken.

Al-Ash'ari confronts a Mu'tazilite claim head-on. If God's call to faith is truly 'guidance' for those who reject it, then it must also be 'benefit' and 'reform' for them. But that leads to an impossibility: that God grants success (tawfiq) to those who remain disbelievers. This passage is a masterclass in logical entailment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation. Let the argument unfold without immediate analysis.
Notice the rhetorical questions: 'why do you deny?'
2
Identify the opponent's claim
The Mu'tazila claim that God's call to faith is guidance (huda) for disbelievers even if they reject it. Pinpoint this in the text.
3
Follow the reductio
Al-Ash'ari draws out implications: if it's guidance, it must also be benefit, reform, direction, and protection. See how each term is introduced.
The terms are نفع, صلاح, تسديد, عصمة.
4
Understand the conclusion
The implications lead to an absurdity: that God grants success to disbelievers while they remain disbelievers. This is impossible because disbelievers are forsaken (makhdhulun). Therefore the original claim is false.
The key contradiction: كيف يكونون موفقين للإيمان وهم مخذولون؟

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال لهم : إذا قلتم : إن دعاء الله إلى الإيمان هدى للكافرين الذين لم يقبلوا عن الله أمره، فما أنكرتم أن يكون دعاء الله إلى الإيمان نفعاً وصلاحاً وتسديداً للكافرين الذين لم يقبلوا عن الله أمره؟ وما أنكرتم أن يكون عصمة لهم من الكفر، وإن لم يوفقوا للإيمان، وفي هذا ما يجب أن الله سدد الكافرين وأصلحهم وعصمهم ووفقهم للإيمان وإن كانوا كافرين، وهذا مما لا يجوز؛ لأن الكافرين مخذولون، وكيف يكونون موفقين للإيمان وهم مخذولون؟ فإن جاز أن يكون الكافر موفقاً للإيمان، فما أنكرتم أن يكون الإيمان له متفقاً، فإن استحال هذا فما أنكرتم أن يستحيل ما قلتموه.
And it is said to them: If you say that God's call to faith is guidance for the disbelievers who did not accept God's command, then why do you deny that God's call to faith is benefit, reform, and direction for the disbelievers who did not accept God's command? And why do you deny that it is protection for them from disbelief, even if they were not granted success (tawfiq) to faith? And in this is entailed that God directed the disbelievers, reformed them, protected them, and granted them success to faith even though they are disbelievers, and that is not permissible because the disbelievers are forsaken (makhdhulun). How can they be granted success to faith while they are forsaken? If it is permissible that the disbeliever is granted success to faith, then why do you deny that faith befits him? And if this is impossible, then why do you deny that what you have said is impossible?
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is another polemical argument (مسألة) against the Mu'tazilite claim that God's call (دعاء) to faith is guidance (هدى) for disbelievers even if they reject it. Al-Ash'ari draws out the implications of this claim. If it is guidance, then it must also be benefit (نفع), reform (صلاح), direction (تسديد), and protection (عصمة) from disbelief — even without God granting success (توفيق). But this leads to absurdity: it would mean God has directed, reformed, protected, and granted success to disbelievers, yet they remain disbelievers. This contradicts the fact that disbelievers are forsaken (مخذولون), not granted success. Therefore, the original claim is self-contradictory. The argument uses a reductio: if a disbeliever could be 'granted success' (موفق) to faith, then faith would 'befit' him (متفق) — but that is impossible for a disbeliever. Hence the opponents' position is impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that al-Ash'ari denies any benefit in God's call to disbelievers.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari is not denying that the call has any benefit; he is showing that calling it 'guidance' for those who reject it leads to logical contradictions.

Checkpoint

A) That disbelievers are still guided in some sense
B) That disbelievers are reformed and protected even without belief
C) That God's call is meaningless
D) That disbelievers will eventually believe

Key Takeaway
God's call cannot be benefit for those who reject it, as that would entail granting them success while they remain forsaken.

The Meaning of Leading Astray: A Logical Trilemma
Al-Ash'ari examines the meaning of 'leading astray' using a trilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's logical refutation of those who claim God leads disbelievers astray without specifying from what.

Core Idea
Leading astray requires a starting point; it must be from faith.

Al-Ash'ari presents a concise logical trilemma to demonstrate that the only coherent meaning of 'leading astray' is away from faith. By examining the grammar of the Arabic preposition 'عن', he shows that his opponents' position is self-contradictory.

Guided Path
1
Read the trilemma
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the three options al-Ash'ari presents to his opponents.
Notice the precise wording of each option.
2
Analyze each option
For each of the three possible answers, consider why al-Ash'ari finds it absurd or self-defeating.
Focus on the preposition 'عن' (from) — it indicates a starting point.
3
Understand the final analogy
The third option is rebutted by an analogy with guidance: just as guidance must be to something (faith), misguidance must be from something (faith).
This completes the logical refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يقال لهم : أضل الله الكافرين عن الإيمان أو عن الكفر؟ فإن قالوا عن الكفر قيل لهم : فكيف يكونون ضالين عن الكفر ذاهبين عنه وهم كافرون؟ وإن قالوا أضلهم عن الإيمان، تركوا قولهم. وإن قالوا نقول : إن الله أضلهم ولم يضلهم عن شيء . قيل لهم : ما الفرق بينكم وبين من قال : إن الله هدى المؤمنين لا إلى شيء؟ فإن استحال أن يهدي المؤمنين لا إلى الإيمان، فما أنكرتم من أنه محال أن يضل الكافرين لا عن الإيمان .
It is said to them: Did God lead the disbelievers astray (adalla) from faith or from disbelief? If they say from disbelief, it is said to them: How can they be astray from disbelief, going away from it, while they are disbelievers? And if they say He led them astray from faith, they abandon their statement. And if they say: We say that God led them astray and did not lead them astray from anything. It is said to them: What is the difference between you and one who says that God guided the believers not to anything? For if it is impossible that He guides the believers not to faith, then why do you deny that it is impossible that He leads the disbelievers astray not from faith?
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a concise logical argument (مسألة في الضلال) that dissects the meaning of 'leading astray' (إضلال). Al-Ash'ari poses a trilemma to his opponents. First, if they say God led them astray from disbelief, that is absurd because disbelievers are already in disbelief; being 'astray from disbelief' would mean they are leaving disbelief toward faith, which is not the case. Second, if they say God led them astray from faith, that contradicts their own doctrine that God does not lead believers astray. Third, if they say God led them astray without specifying 'from something', that is meaningless — it would be like saying God guided believers to nothing. Just as guidance must be toward something (faith), misguidance must be away from something (faith). Therefore, the only coherent meaning is that God leads people astray from faith, which the opponents reject. Thus their position is logically untenable.

Key Terms
أضل
ضال
إيمان
كفر
هدى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that God can lead disbelievers astray without specifying 'from what' — i.e., misguidance is absolute and not relative.
Correction: As al-Ash'ari shows, the Arabic verb 'أضل' (to lead astray) with the preposition 'عن' requires an object from which one is led astray. Without that, the statement is meaningless, just as guidance requires an object 'to'.

Checkpoint
Why does al-Ash'ari reject the claim that God led disbelievers astray from disbelief?
A) Because disbelief is not a thing one can be led astray from
B) Because disbelievers are already in disbelief, so being 'astray from it' would mean leaving it
C) Because the Qur'an says God leads astray only believers
D) Because the word 'ضلال' never takes the preposition 'عن'

Key Takeaway
The only coherent meaning of leading astray is away from faith, which the opponents deny, making their position logically untenable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself attributing your own spiritual waywardness to God, as if He misled you without cause? How does this argument force you to reconsider that tendency and instead take responsibility for your own departure from faith? What will you do differently when you feel astray?
?
If every instance of misguidance is a departure from faith, then your own moments of doubt or sin are not random—they are a turning away from what you know to be true. Are you willing to admit that your struggles are not God's arbitrary decree but your own choices? What concrete step will you take today to realign yourself with faith?

The Opponents' Interpretation of Allah Leading Astray
Al-Ash'ari asks opponents to explain the verse and presents their reinterpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the opponents reinterpreted the verse 'Allah leads astray the wrongdoers' to avoid attributing the creation of misguidance to Allah.

Core Idea
The opponents turned God's causing astray into a mere naming of astray.

Al-Ash'ari confronts his opponents with a clear Quranic verse that attributes the act of leading astray to Allah. He anticipates their response: they will claim that the verb 'yudillu' does not mean causing misguidance, but rather declaring someone to be astray. This passage sets up the debate on the nature of divine action and human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation

2
Identify the key terms

These terms are central to the discussion.
3
Understand the opponents' interpretation
The opponents say the verse means Allah names them astray and judges them to be in error, not that He causes their misguidance.
This is a declarative interpretation rather than a causative one.
4
Reflect on the theological stakes
Ask yourself: Why would the opponents want to reinterpret this verse? How does it relate to the issue of qadar (predestination)?
This connects to broader debates about divine responsibility for human actions.

Commentary

This interpretation avoids attributing the creation of misguidance to God. The passage ends in the middle of the argument; the author's refutation would follow on the next page, which is not included in this window. Nonetheless, the passage shows the opponents' hermeneutical strategy of reinterpreting verbs of divine action to fit their theology.

Refutation of the Claim that God's Call to Faith is Guidance
Ash'ari refutes Mu'tazila via reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ash'ari uses a reductio ad absurdum to refute the Mu'tazila claim that God's call to faith is guidance for disbelievers.

Core Idea
If God's call were guidance, disbelievers would be both guided and forsaken—a contradiction.

Imam Ash'ari presents a logical argument against the Mu'tazila position that God's call to faith serves as guidance for disbelievers. By showing that this claim leads to impossible consequences, he demonstrates its falsehood. This lesson walks through the reductio ad absurdum and its implications for understanding divine guidance and abandonment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument unfold naturally.
Notice the structure: premise, entailments, contradiction, conclusion.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila premise
The Mu'tazila claim is that God's call to faith (دعاء) is guidance (هدى) for disbelievers who reject it. Underline this premise in the passage.
This is the starting point of the reductio.
3
Trace the logical entailments
Ash'ari asks if the call is guidance, then why not also benefit, rectification, direction, and protection from disbelief? Follow each entailment he lists.
These are attributes that would logically follow if 'guidance' is understood in a strong sense.
4
Recognize the contradiction
If the call grants success (tawfīq) to faith, then disbelievers would be successful (muwaffaqūn) in faith while being forsaken (makhdhūlūn) — an impossibility. Spot this contradiction.
The key term 'خذلان' (forsaken) is opposite to 'توفيق' (success).
5
Conclude the refutation
Since the premise leads to an absurdity, the premise must be false. Understand how this refutes the Mu'tazila position.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum argument in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٣٩ - مسألة أخرى :
ويقال لهم : إذا قلتم : إن دعاء الله إلى الإيمان هدى للكافرين الذين لم يقبلوا عن الله أمره، فما أنكرتم أن يكون دعاء الله إلى الإيمان نفعاً وصلاحاً وتسديداً للكافرين الذين لم يقبلوا عن الله أمره وما أنكرتم أن يكون عصمة لهم من الكفر، وإن لم يوفقوا للإيمان، وفي هذا ما يجب أن الله سدد الكافرين وأصلحهم وعصمهم ووفقهم للإيمان وإن كانوا كافرين، وهذا مما لا يجوز؛ لأن الكافرين مخذولون، وكيف يكونون موفقين للإيمان وهم مخذولون؟ فإن جاز أن يكون الكافر موفقاً للإيمان، فما أنكرتم أن يكون الإيمان له متفقاً، فإن استحال هذا فما أنكرتم أن يستحيل ما قلتموه .
239 - Another question:
And it is said to them: If you say that God's call to faith is guidance for the disbelievers who did not accept God's command, then why do you deny that God's call to faith is benefit, rectification, and direction for the disbelievers who did not accept God's command? And why do you deny that it is a protection for them from disbelief, even if they are not granted success (tawfīq) to faith? And in this is that it would be necessary that God directed (saddada) the disbelievers, rectified them, protected them, and granted them success (waffaqa) to faith, even though they are disbelievers. And this is not permissible, because the disbelievers are forsaken (makhdhūlūn). How can they be granted success (muwaffaqūn) to faith while they are forsaken? If it is permissible that the disbeliever is granted success to faith, then why do you deny that faith would be attained (muttafiqan) by him? And if this is impossible (istaḥāla), then why do you deny that what you have said is impossible?
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer (refutation) against the Mu'tazila position. The author uses a reductio ad absurdum: if God's call to faith is truly guidance (hudā), then it should also be benefit (nafʿ), rectification (ṣalāḥ), direction (tasdīd), and protection (ʿiṣma) from disbelief for the disbelievers, even if they do not actually accept faith. But this would imply that God grants them success (tawfīq) to faith while they remain disbelievers—a contradiction because disbelievers are forsaken (makhdhūlūn), not guided. The argument concludes that since the premise leads to impossibility, the Mu'tazila claim is false. The passage follows a logical chain: premise (call = guidance) → entailments (benefit, protection, success) → contradiction (disbelievers cannot be guided) → rejection of premise.

Key Terms
هدى
دعاء
توفيق
خذلان
متفق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that Ash'ari denies any benefit in God's call to disbelievers. Instead, he denies that it constitutes 'guidance' in the Mu'tazila sense of conveying success (tawfīq).
Correction: Ash'ari does not deny that the call is beneficial in some sense; he argues that if it were guidance (as Mu'tazila define it), it would imply contradictory consequences, thus the Mu'tazila definition is flawed.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari, why is it impossible that God's call to faith is guidance for the disbelievers?
A) Because the disbelievers reject it.
B) Because it would imply that disbelievers are both guided (successed) and forsaken simultaneously.
C) Because guidance only applies to believers.
D) Because God's call is not a benefit.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari refutation shows that attributing guidance to God's call for disbelievers leads to logical impossibility, reinforcing the distinction between divine guidance and abandonment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the call to faith (the Quran, prayer, etc.), do you assume that hearing itself is sufficient guidance? How does Ash'ari's argument force you to examine whether you are truly responding or just presuming guidance?

The Trilemma of Misguidance
Ash'ari presents a trilemma forcing the Mu'tazila to accept that misguidance has an object.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that divine misguidance must have a definite object (from faith or disbelief), and how Ash'ari uses this to critique the Mu'tazila position.

Core Idea
Divine misguidance must be from something, just as guidance must be to something.

Imam Ash'ari engages the Mu'tazila on the meaning of God's misguidance. The Mu'tazila claim God misguides but not from anything. Ash'ari exposes the absurdity of this by drawing a parallel to guidance: if guidance must be to something, then misguidance must be from something. This brief but powerful argument shows the logical necessity of specifying the object of misguidance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the three options
The passage presents three possible answers the Mu'tazila might give about what God misguides from. Find each one and notice how Ash'ari refutes it.
The options are: from disbelief, from faith, or from nothing.
3
Understand the parallel argument
Ash'ari draws a parallel between misguidance and guidance. If guidance must be to something, then misguidance must be from something. This exposes the inconsistency in the Mu'tazila's third option.
4
Reflect on the principle
Consider why this argument matters for theology. It shows that theological statements must be meaningful and consistent. A claim that God misguides 'not from anything' is absurd.
This connects to the broader theme of divine attributes and actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٤٠- مسألة في الضلال :
يقال لهم : أضل الله الكافرين عن الإيمان أو عن الكفر؟
فإن قالوا عن الكفر
قيل لهم : فكيف يكونون ضالين عن الكفر ذاهبين عنه وهم كافرون؟ وإن قالوا أضلهم عن الإيمان، تركوا قولهم .
وإن قالوا نقول : إن الله أضلهم ولم يضلهم عن شيء .
قيل لهم : ما الفرق بينكم وبين من قال : إن الله هدى المؤمنين لا إلى شيء؟ فإن استحال أن يهدي المؤمنين لا إلى الإيمان، فما أنكرتم من أنه
محال أن يضل الكافرين لا عن الإيمان .
240 - A question concerning misguidance (al-ḍalāl):
It is said to them: Did God misguide (aḍalla) the disbelievers from faith or from disbelief?
If they say: from disbelief,
It is said to them: How can they be misguided (ḍāllīn) from disbelief, going away from it, while they are disbelievers? And if they say: He misguided them from faith, they abandon their statement.
And if they say: We say that God misguided them but did not misguide them from anything,
It is said to them: What is the difference between you and one who says: God guided the believers but not to anything? If it is impossible (istaḥāla) that He guides the believers not to faith, then why do you deny that it is impossible that He misguides the disbelievers not from faith?
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical argument (objection-and-answer) that exposes inconsistency in the Mu'tazila position on divine misguidance. The author presents a trilemma: (1) If they say God misguides from disbelief, that is absurd because disbelievers are already in disbelief—they cannot be going away from it. (2) If they say from faith, that contradicts their own doctrine that God does not create faith. (3) If they say He misguides but not from anything, then the same logic would allow saying God guides believers but not to anything, which is also absurd. Thus, the Mu'tazila are forced into contradiction, proving that misguidance must have a definite object (faith or disbelief). The argument uses logical parallel: if guidance must be to something, then misguidance must be from something.

Key Terms

إضلال

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Ash'ari is defending that God misguides from faith, i.e., that He directly causes unbelief.
Correction: Ash'ari is not affirming that God misguides from faith; he is only showing the inconsistency in the Mu'tazila's position. The argument is dialectical, not a positive claim.

Checkpoint

B) God only misguides disbelievers.
C) God guides believers without direction.
D) The Mu'tazila agree with Ash'aris.

Key Takeaway
Misguidance, like guidance, must have a definite object; otherwise theological language becomes meaningless.

Linguistic Refutation: 'Yudillu' Does Not Mean 'Names as Misguided'
Ash'ari linguistically refutes the Mu'tazila interpretation of 'yuḍillu'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic basis for the Ash'ari interpretation of the Quranic verb 'yuḍillu' and why the Mu'tazila interpretation is incompatible with Arabic usage.

Core Idea
Arabic verb forms distinguish between 'making misguided' and 'calling misguided'—the Quran uses the former.

This passage from al-Ash'ari's al-Ibānah presents a concise linguistic argument against the Mu'tazila interpretation of Quranic 'yuḍillu'. The Mu'tazila had claimed that when Allah says 'He misguides the wrongdoers', it merely means He judges them to be misguided. Ash'ari counters by pointing to the structure of Arabic—the verb form used in the Quran does not carry the meaning of 'naming' or 'judging'. He then preempts a possible counterargument by showing that the correct verb for 'naming misguided' is a different form. This lesson unpacks that exchange.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice how the argument is structured as a dialogue: a question, the opponent's claim, and a refutation.
Pay attention to the verb forms أضل and ضلل.
2
Identify the two verb forms
The key linguistic point is the distinction between form IV (أضل) and form II (ضلل). The Mu'tazila interpretation requires the meaning of 'naming as misguided', which belongs to form II, but the Quran uses form IV.
This is the core of the argument.
3
Understand the opponent's claim and Ash'ari's premise
The Mu'tazila claim that 'yuḍillu' means 'He names them misguided'. Ash'ari first establishes that the Quran is in Arabic, then demands evidence that 'aḍalla' ever means 'named as misguided' in Arabic speech.
4
See why Ash'ari's argument is decisive
Ash'ari grants that 'ḍallala' (form II) can mean 'named as misguided', but 'aḍalla' (form IV) does not share that meaning. Therefore, the Quranic usage cannot be interpreted as the Mu'tazila claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٤١ - مسألة أخرى :
ويقال لهم ما معنى قول الله عز وجل: وَيُضِلُّ اللهُ الظَّالِمِينَ ) [إبراهيم: ۲۷] ؟ فإن قالوا : معنى ذلك أنه يسميهم ضالين، ويحكم عليهم بالضلال .
قيل لهم : أليس خاطب الله العرب بلغتهم فقال : بِلِسَانٍ عربي مبين ) [الشعراء: ١٩٥] وقال: ﴿ وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَا مِن رَّسُولٍ إِلَّا بِلِسَانِ قَوْمِهِ ) [إبراهيم: ٤]؟
فلا بد من نعم .
فيقال لهم : فإذا كان الله عز وجل أنزل القرآن بلسان العرب، فمن أين وجدتم في لغة العرب أن يقال: أضل فلان فلاناً، أي سماه ضالاً؟
فإن قالوا: وجدنا القائل يقول : إذا قال رجل لرجل: ضال: قد ضللته قيل لهم : قد وجدنا العرب يقولون : ضلل فلان فلاناً إذا سماه ضالاً، ولم نجدهم يقولون: أضل فلان فلاناً بهذا المعنى، فلما قال الله عز وجل: ﴿وَيُضِلُّ اللَّهُ الظَّالِمِينَ ) لم يجز أن يكون ذلك معنى الاسم والحكم إذا لم يجز في لغة العرب أن يقال : أضل فلان فلاناً، إذا سماه ضالاً، بطل تأويلكم إذا كان خلاف لسان العرب
241 - Another question:
And it is said to them: What is the meaning of the saying of God, Mighty and Majestic: "And God misguides (yuḍillu) the wrongdoers" [Ibrahim 14:27]? If they say: Its meaning is that He names them misguided (ḍāllīn) and judges them with misguidance (bi-al-ḍalāl).
It is said to them: Did not God address the Arabs in their language, saying: "In a clear Arabic tongue" [Ash-Shu'ara 26:195] and "And We did not send any messenger except in the language of his people" [Ibrahim 14:4]? They must say yes.
Then it is said to them: So since God sent down the Quran in the language of the Arabs, where did you find in the language of the Arabs that one says "aḍalla fulānun fulānan" meaning he named him misguided (ḍāllan)?
If they say: We found that a speaker says: if a man says to a man "ḍāll" (misguided), [then] "qad ḍallaltuhu" (I have named him misguided).
It is said to them: We have found that the Arabs say "ḍallala fulānun fulānan" if he named him misguided, but we have not found them saying "aḍalla fulānun fulānan" with this meaning. So when God said "And God misguides (yuḍillu) the wrongdoers", it is not permissible that this be the meaning of noun and judgment (al-ism wa-al-ḥukm) when it is not permissible in the language of the Arabs that one says "aḍalla fulānun fulānan" if he named him misguided. Your interpretation is invalid (baṭala) since it is contrary to the language of the Arabs.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a linguistic refutation. The Mu'tazila interpret 'yuḍillu' as 'He names/judges them as misguided'. The Ash'ari points out that the Quran is in Arabic, and the verb 'aḍalla' (form IV) does not have the meaning of 'naming as misguided'; that meaning is expressed by 'ḍallala' (form II). Since the Quran uses form IV, the interpretation is linguistically invalid. The author also preempts a counterexample: the opponent might cite a usage where 'ḍallala' is used for naming, but that is a different verb. Therefore, the Mu'tazila interpretation contradicts the Arabic language and is thus false.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quranic verb 'yuḍillu' (form IV) can mean 'names as misguided'.
Correction: In Arabic, the meaning 'to name or judge someone as misguided' is expressed by the form II verb 'ḍallala', not by form IV 'aḍalla'. Since the Quran uses form IV, the Mu'tazila interpretation is linguistically invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari linguistic refutation shows that the Mu'tazila interpretation of 'yuḍillu' contradicts the established usage of Arabic, thereby defending the view that Allah actively leads the wrongdoers astray.

The Prophet Cannot Be an Agent of Misguidance
Reductio showing Mu'tazila interpretation implies Prophet misguides.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ash'ari uses a reductio argument to show that the Mu'tazila interpretation of divine misguidance leads to an impossible consequence involving the Prophet.

Core Idea
If naming equals misguiding, the Prophet would be a misguider — impossible.

In this passage, Imam Ash'ari delivers a decisive blow to the Mu'tazila interpretation of God's misguidance. He shows that their linguistic claim leads to a theological absurdity involving the Prophet. By tracing the logical consequence, he demonstrates that their interpretation cannot be correct without compromising the Prophet's sinlessness.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazila claim
According to the Mu'tazila, when God says He misguides the wrongdoers, He merely names them as misguided, not actually leads them astray.
This linguistic interpretation is the target of Ash'ari's argument.
2
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the logical structure: 'If you say... then it would be necessary...'
The argument hinges on applying the same logic to the Prophet.
3
Identify the reductio
See that the passage applies the same principle to the Prophet: if naming equals misguiding, then when the Prophet calls people misguided, he would be misguiding them.
This is impossible because prophets are sinless.
4
Recognize the conclusion
The impossibility means the original interpretation is invalid. The verse cannot mean naming only.
Ash'ari concludes that 'yuḍillu' must mean actual misguidance by God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٤٢ - مسألة أخرى :
ويقال لهم : إذا قلتم : إن الله أضل الكافرين بأن سماهم ضالين، وليس ذلك في اللغة على ما ادعيتموه، فيلزمكم إذا سمى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قوماً ضالين فاسدين بأن يكون قد أضلهم وأفسدهم بأن سماهم ضالين فاسدين، وإذا لم يجز هذا بطل أن يكون معنى : ﴿ وَيُضِلُّ اللَّهُ الظَّالِمِينَ ( الاسم والحكم كما ادعيتم .
242 - Another question:
And it is said to them: If you say that God misguided the disbelievers by naming them misguided, and that is not in the language as you have claimed, then it would be necessary (yalzamu) that if the Prophet, peace be upon him, named a people misguided (ḍāllīn) and corrupt (fāsidīn), then he would have misguided them and corrupted them by naming them misguided and corrupt. And if this is not permissible (lam yajuz), then it is invalid (baṭala) that the meaning of "And God misguides the wrongdoers" is the name and judgment as you have claimed.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is an additional reductio ad absurdum. Building on the previous linguistic refutation, the Ash'ari points out a further consequence: if the Mu'tazila interpretation (that 'yuḍillu' means 'names as misguided') were accepted, then any instance of naming someone as misguided would constitute actual misguidance. This would apply to the Prophet himself when he (in the Quran or hadith) called certain people misguided and corrupt. But it is impossible for the Prophet to be an agent of misguidance; therefore, the interpretation is false. The argument strengthens the previous linguistic point by showing its theological absurdity.

تسمية
إضلال
النبي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Ash'ari is accusing the Prophet of misguiding people.
Correction: Actually, Ash'ari is using a reductio: he assumes the Mu'tazila interpretation and shows it leads to an absurd consequence (Prophet misguiding), which is impossible, hence the interpretation is false.

Checkpoint

A) The Prophet would be a misguider.
B) God would be unjust.
C) The Quran would be contradictory.
D) The disbelievers would be excused.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila interpretation that 'God misguides' means 'names as misguided' is false because it would require the Prophet to be a misguider, which is impossible.

God's Universal Call and Specific Guidance
Ash'ari cites three verses to distinguish universal call from specific guidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ash'ari uses Quranic verses to distinguish between God's general call to all people and His specific guidance to whom He wills.

Core Idea
God calls everyone, but guides only whom He chooses.

In this passage, Imam Ash'ari presents a concise scriptural argument that clarifies a key point in the debate over divine guidance. He cites three verses that distinguish between God's universal invitation to salvation and His selective gift of guidance. This distinction supports the Ash'ari position that guidance is a particular act of God, not a universal offer that humans can accept on their own.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once, noticing the three Quranic verses quoted. Observe how Ash'ari introduces them with the phrase 'a-laysa qad qāla Allāhu taʿālā'.
2
Examine the first two verses
Look at verses 18:17 and 3:86. Notice that both affirm that guidance and misguidance are entirely in God's hands. Reflect on how they establish God's sovereignty over guidance.
These verses are introduced consecutively without separate commentary.
3
Focus on the third verse
Read verse 10:25 and Ash'ari's comment. He explicitly points out that the call (duʿā') is general (ʿāmm) while guidance (hudā) is specific (khāṣṣ). This is the core of the argument.
This verse provides the decisive distinction.
4
Connect to the Ash'ari position
Reflect on how this passage supports the Ash'ari stance: guidance is a divine gift, not a human achievement. The commentary explains this nuance.
Contrast this with the Mu'tazili view that guidance is universal and depends on human choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٤٣- مسألة أخرى :
ويقال لهم : أليس قد قال الله تعالى: ﴿مَن يَهْدِ اللهُ فَهُوَ الْمُهْتَدِ وَمَن يُضْلِلْ فَلَن تجدَ لَهُ وَلِيا تُرْشِدا ﴾ [الكهف : ۱۷] وقال عز وجل: كَيْفَ يَهْدِي اللَّهُ قَوْمَا كَفَرُوا بَعْدَ إيمنيم ) [آل عمران : ٨٦] فذكر أنه لا يهديهم، وقال تعالى: ﴿ وَاللَّهُ يَدْعُوا إِلَى دَارِ السَّلَامِ وَيَهْدِى مَن يَشَاءُ إِلَى صِرَاطٍ مُّسْتَقِيمٍ ﴾ [يونس : ٢٥] فجعل الدعاء عاماً، والهدى خاصاً .
243 - Another question:
And it is said to them: Did not God, Most High, say: "Whom God guides (yahdi) is the guided one, and whom He misguides (yuḍlil) you will not find for him a protecting guide" [Al-Kahf 18:17]? And He, Mighty and Majestic, said: "How shall God guide a people who disbelieved after their belief" [Aal-e-Imran 3:86], and He mentioned that He does not guide them. And He, Most High, said: "And God calls to the abode of peace and guides whom He wills to a straight path" [Yunus 10:25], and He made the call (al-du'ā') general (ʿāmm) and guidance (al-hudā) specific (khāṣṣ).
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a scriptural proof (istidlāl) from three Quranic verses. The first verse (18:17) establishes that both guidance and misguidance are in God's hand. The second verse (3:86) asks how God would guide people who disbelieved after believing, implying that He does not guide them—i.e., guidance is not automatic but is withheld based on divine will. The third verse (10:25) makes a crucial distinction: God's call (da'wa) to paradise is general for all, but His guidance (hudā) to the straight path is specific to whom He wills. This supports the Ash'ari position that guidance is a particular act of God, not a universal offer that creatures can accept or reject on their own. The passage is a concise Quranic argument for divine sovereignty over guidance.

Misconception: Some might think that the Ash'ari denies that God calls all people to guidance, or that guidance is universally available to all.
Correction: The passage clearly affirms that God's call (du'ā') is general for all, but effective guidance (hudā) is specific to whom God wills. The Ash'ari does not deny the universal call; he distinguishes it from the gift of guidance.

Pronoun Reference in the Quran: Answering an Objection
Imam Ashari answers an objection about pronoun reference in the Thamud verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ashari defends the Quranic usage of pronouns referring to different groups within the same verse, using linguistic principles and Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
A single pronoun in the Quran can refer to two different groups.

Imam Ashari continues his refutation of objections against the Ash'ari position on guidance and misguidance. The objector claimed inconsistency in the verse about Thamud, where 'they' seems to refer to both believers and disbelievers. Ashari demonstrates that this is perfectly acceptable in Arabic, citing similar constructions in the Quran itself. This lesson unpacks his argument and its linguistic foundation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Understand the objector's challenge: how can 'guided them' refer to believers and 'loved disbelief' refer to disbelievers when the pronoun 'them' appears in the same context?
The objector assumes uniform reference for a single pronoun.
2
Identify the answer
Ashari states that such usage is permissible in Arabic. He asserts that a pronoun can refer to different groups even within the same passage.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Ashari quotes Surah Al-Anfal 8:33-34, where 'them' refers to disbelievers in one clause and believers in another, proving the pattern.
This shows that the objector's complaint contradicts actual Quranic usage.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Ashari concludes that the objection is invalid and highlights the objector's ignorance of Arabic linguistic norms.
The argument relies on established linguistic conventions, not theological assumption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الآخر : أن الله عز وجل عنى قوماً من ثمود كانوا مؤمنين، ثم ارتدوا، فأخبر أنه هداهم فاستحبوا بعد الهداية الكفر على الإيمان، وكانوا في حال هداهم مؤمنين . فإن قال قائل معترضاً في الجواب الأول: كيف يجوز أن يقول: ما فَهَدَيْتَهُمْ ويعني المؤمنين من ثمود، ويقول: (فَاسْتَحَبُّوا يعني الكافرين منهم وهم غير مؤمنين ؟ يقال له: هذا جائز في اللغة التي ورد بها القرآن أن يقول : فَهَدَيْنَهُمْ ﴾ ويعني المؤمنين من ثمود، ويقال: فَاسْتَحَبُّوا يعني الكافرين منهم، وقد ورد القرآن بمثل هذا قال الله عز وجل: ﴿ وَمَا كَانَ الله لِيُعَذِّبَهُمْ وَأَنتَ فِيهِمْ ﴾ [الأنفال: ۳۳] يعني الكافرين، ثم قال تعالى: ﴿ وَمَا كَانَ اللهُ مُعَذِّبَهُمْ وَهُمْ يَسْتَغْفِرُونَ ﴾ [الأنفال: ۳۳] يعني المؤمنين، ثم قال: ﴿وَمَا لَهُمْ أَلَّا يُعَذِّبَهُمُ اللهُ ﴾ [الأنفال : ٣٤] يعني الكافرين، ولا خلاف عند أهل اللغة في جواز الخطاب بهذا أن يكون ظاهره لجنس والمراد به جنسان، فبطل ما اعترض به المعترض، ودل على جهله .
The second aspect: That Allah, Mighty and Majestic, intended a people from Thamud who were believers, then they apostatized. So He informed that He guided them, then they loved disbelief over faith after guidance, and they were at the time of His guidance believers. If an objector says in objection to the first answer: How is it permissible to say: 'You did not guide them' meaning the believers from Thamud, and say: 'they loved' meaning the disbelievers among them while they are not believers? It is said to him: This is permissible in the language in which the Qur'an came, that He says: 'We guided them' meaning the believers from Thamud, and it is said: 'they loved' meaning the disbelievers among them. The Qur'an has come with such [usage]. Allah, Mighty and Majestic, said: 'And Allah would not punish them while you are among them' [Al-Anfal 8:33] meaning the disbelievers, then He said: 'And Allah would not punish them while they seek forgiveness' [Al-Anfal 8:33] meaning the believers, then He said: 'And why should Allah not punish them' [Al-Anfal 8:34] meaning the disbelievers. There is no disagreement among the people of language regarding the permissibility of address such that its apparent meaning is for one class and what is intended is two classes. Thus what the objector objected to is invalid, and it indicates his ignorance.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The author (Imam Ashari) presents a second aspect (الوجه الآخر) to refute an earlier objection. The context: a group from Thamud initially believed then apostatized. God says He guided them, yet they loved disbelief after guidance. The objector questions how the verb 'guided' (هداهم) can refer to the believers, while the verb 'loved' (استحبوا) refers to the disbelievers, since the pronoun seems to refer to the same group. The answer: This is linguistically permissible in Arabic. The Quran itself uses similar constructions, as in Surah Al-Anfal: 'And Allah would not punish them while you are among them' means the disbelievers, then 'while they seek forgiveness' means the believers, then 'why should Allah not punish them' again means the disbelievers. Thus a single pronoun can refer to two different groups. The author concludes that this invalidates the objection and demonstrates the objector's ignorance.

Key Terms
الهداية
الاستحباب
الجواب
الاعتراض
اللغة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A pronoun in the Quran must refer uniformly to all individuals mentioned in the same context.
Correction: The Quran and Arabic allow a pronoun to refer to a subset of the group or to different groups in different clauses, as demonstrated by the Al-Anfal verses.

Checkpoint
How does Imam Ashari prove that a single pronoun can refer to two different groups in one verse?
A) By citing a verse from Surah Al-Anfal that uses the same pattern.
B) By appealing to the consensus of scholars.
C) By comparing it to poetry.
D) By arguing from logical necessity.

Key Takeaway
Pronoun reference in the Quran is flexible and can refer to different groups within the same context, a known feature of Arabic grammar.

The objector in this passage had a quick objection that showed ignorance. Have you ever dismissed a Quranic verse or a scholarly explanation because it seemed inconsistent to you? How might your own limited understanding have led you astray? Will you now seek deeper knowledge rather than object?
?
This lesson demonstrates that Allah's speech is perfect even when it challenges our expectations. How does your heart respond to the fact that divine wisdom can transcend your logic? Are you ready to submit to that wisdom, even when your mind questions it? What specific step will you take to strengthen your trust in Allah's words?

The Hadith of Creation and the Four Decrees
Imam Ashari narrates a hadith on fetal creation and four decrees.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the content and significance of the hadith on the creation of the fetus and the writing of the four decrees, and its implications for belief in divine decree.

Core Idea
The four decrees written in the womb show Allah's complete sovereignty over each life.

Imam Ashari opens his chapter on Qadar with a powerful hadith from Ibn Mas'ud. This hadith describes how the angel writes four decrees for every person before birth, and then shows that one's final end is determined by Allah's decree, not merely by one's deeds. Let's examine this foundational text.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the full narrative.
Notice the chain of narration and the oath at the end.
2
Identify the four decrees
The angel is commanded to write four things: lifespan, provision, deeds, and whether the person is wretched or blessed. List them and reflect on their scope.
These cover all aspects of life and destiny.
3
Reflect on the decree overtaking deeds
The hadith gives two examples: a person close to Paradise but then does evil deeds due to the prior decree, and vice versa. Consider how this emphasizes Allah's absolute will.
This is a key point in Ash'ari theology.
4
Connect to the broader concept of Qadar
Think about how this hadith supports the belief that all things are predetermined by Allah, and that human actions are created by Allah while humans acquire them.
Imam Ashari uses this hadith as scriptural evidence for divine decree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني عشر ذكر الروايات في القدر ٢٥٠ روی معاوية بن عمرو قال حدثنا زائدة قال: حدثنا سليمان الأعمش، عن زيد بن وهب عن عبد الله بن مسعود قال: أخبرنا رَسُولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم - وَهُوَ الصَّادِقُ الْمَصْدُوقَ - : « إِنَّ أَحَدَكُمْ يُجْمَعُ خَلْقُهُ فِي بَطْنِ أُمِّهِ أَرْبَعِينَ لَيْلَةً، ثُمَّ يَكُونُ عَلَقَةً مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ، ثُمَّ يَكُونُ مُصْعَةٌ مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ ، ثُمَّ يَبْعَثُ الله مَلَكاً، قال: فَيُؤْمَرُ بِأَربع كَلِمَاتٍ، يُقَالُ لَهُ: اكْتُبْ أَجَلَهُ وَرِزْقَهُ وَعَمَلَهُ وَشَقِي أو سَعِيدٌ ، ثُمَّ يُنْفَخُ فِيهِ الرُّوحِ، قَالَ: فَوَالَّذِي لا إِلَهَ غَيْرُهُ! أَحَدَكُمْ لَيَعْمَلُ بِعَمَلِ أَهْلِ الْجَنَّةِ حتى ما يَكُونَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَهَا إِلا ذِرَاعٌ، فَيَسْبَقُ عليه الْكِتَابُ فَيَعْمَلُ بِعَمَلِ أَهْلِ النَّارِ فَيَدْخُلُهَا، وَإِنَّ أَحَدَكُمْ لَيَعْمَلُ بِعَمَلِ أهل النَّارِ حتى ما يَكُونُ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَهَا إِلا ذِرَاعٌ ، فَيَسْبِقُ عليه الْكِتَابُ فَيَعْمَلُ بِعَمَل أَهْلِ الْجَنَّةِ فَيَدْخُلُهَا لا حرمنا الله منها
Chapter Twelve: Mentioning the narrations on Qadar. 250. Mu'awiya ibn 'Amr narrated: Zaidah narrated to us: Sulayman al-A'mash narrated to us, from Zayd ibn Wahb from 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him – and he is the truthful, the believed – informed us: 'Indeed the creation of one of you is gathered in his mother's womb for forty nights, then he becomes a clot for like that, then he becomes a lump of flesh for like that. Then Allah sends an angel, and he is commanded with four words. It is said to him: Write his lifespan, his provision, his deeds, and whether he is wretched or blessed. Then the spirit is breathed into him. By Him besides Whom there is no god! Verily one of you does the deeds of the people of Paradise until there is but a cubit between him and it, then the decree overtakes him and he does the deeds of the people of the Fire and enters it. And verily one of you does the deeds of the people of the Fire until there is but a cubit between him and it, then the decree overtakes him and he does the deeds of the people of Paradise and enters it.' May Allah not deprive us of it.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the twelfth chapter on Qadar (divine decree). It presents a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud. The hadith describes the creation of the human in the womb: first a drop (nutfah) for forty nights, then a clot, then a lump of flesh. Then an angel is sent and commanded to write four things: the person's lifespan (ajal), provision (rizq), deeds (amal), and whether he will be wretched (shaqi) or blessed (sa'id). Then the spirit is breathed. The hadith then emphasizes that regardless of a person's apparent deeds, the prior decree can overtake him. A person may be close to Paradise but then do the deeds of the Fire and enter it, and vice versa. This illustrates the absolute sovereignty of Allah's decree. The supplication at the end 'May Allah not deprive us of it' likely refers to Paradise or the blessing of faith.

خلق
الأجل
الرزق
العمل
الشقاء
السعادة
الملائكة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One's final destiny is solely based on their actions and merits.
Correction: The hadith shows that divine decree can override apparent deeds; a person may be close to Paradise but enter the Fire due to the prior decree, and vice versa.

Checkpoint
What are the four things the angel is commanded to write for the fetus?
A) Lifespan, provision, deeds, and whether he is wretched or blessed.
B) Lifespan, provision, gender, and beauty.
C) Deeds, faith, health, and wealth.
D) Provision, deeds, happiness, and intelligence.

Key Takeaway
The hadith teaches that four decrees are written before birth, and one's final end is determined by Allah's decree, which can override apparent deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The hadith says that your lifespan, provision, deeds, and final destiny were written before you were born. Does this bring you more fear or more hope? How does knowing that your final end is in Allah's hands—not your own—affect your relationship with your daily choices? What will you do today that acknowledges this truth?
?
Imagine you are the person who does deeds of Paradise for a lifetime but then, just a cubit away, the decree overtakes you to the Fire. What would you want to have done differently? Now reflect: are you relying on your deeds or on Allah's mercy? What is one concrete change you need to make in your attitude toward your own righteousness?
?
You do not know what is written for you. But the hadith assures you that the decree is already set. How does this uncertainty challenge your sense of control? What would it mean for you to live with full trust in Allah's decree while still striving in obedience? Name one area of your life where you need to surrender to the decree and stop worrying.

The Hadith of the Fetus's Creation and Divine Decree
Imam Ashari narrates the hadith on the creation of the fetus and the writing of destiny.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the stages of human prenatal development as described in the hadith and the four divine decrees written for every person.

Core Idea
Your destiny is written before you are born.

This lesson examines a key hadith reported by Imam al-Ash'ari in al-Ibānah. The hadith, from Ibn Mas'ud, describes the creation of the fetus in stages and the recording of four essential decrees. It also contains a profound warning about the possibility of a last-minute reversal of deeds, emphasizing that final salvation depends on Allah's decree.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the chain of narration (isnad) and the authority of the Prophet (peace be upon him).
The hadith is considered authentic (muttafaq 'alayh).
2
Identify the stages of creation
The hadith mentions three 40-day periods: first as a drop (nutfah), then as a clinging clot ('alaqah), then as a lump of flesh (mudghah). After that, an angel is sent.
These stages correspond to the embryonic development described in the Qur'an.
3
Understand the four decrees
The angel is commanded to write four things: lifespan, provision, deeds, and whether the person is wretched or blessed. These are pre-ordained by Allah.
This verse shows the comprehensiveness of divine decree.
4
Reflect on the reversal of deeds
The hadith presents a striking scenario: a person is about to enter Paradise, but the decree overtakes him and he does deeds of the Fire and enters it. The opposite also occurs. This teaches that ultimate outcome is by Allah's will, not solely based on apparent deeds.
This does not negate free will; rather, it affirms that Allah's knowledge encompasses the end.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Mu'awiya ibn 'Amr narrated, saying: Zaidah narrated, saying: Sulayman al-A'mash narrated, from Zayd ibn Wahb, from 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, who said: The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace — and he is the truthful, the believed — told us: 'Verily, the creation of each one of you is gathered in the womb of his mother for forty nights, then he becomes a clinging clot for a similar period, then he becomes a lump of flesh for a similar period. Then the spirit is breathed into him. And by Him besides Whom there is no god! One of you will do the deeds of the people of Paradise until there is between him and it only a cubit, then the decree overtakes him and he does the deeds of the people of the Fire and enters it. And one of you will do the deeds of the people of the Fire until there is between him and it only a cubit, then the decree overtakes him and he does the deeds of the people of Paradise and enters it.' May Allah not deprive us of it.

Commentary
This passage is a narration of a well-known hadith from Ibn Mas'ud that details the stages of prenatal development and the divine decree. The hadith begins with the stages: forty days as a drop, then a clot, then a lump of flesh. Then an angel is sent to write four decrees: lifespan, provision, deeds, and final state (wretched or blessed). After that, the spirit is breathed. The hadith then highlights that despite one's apparent deeds, the written decree can overtake a person even at the last moment, causing a reversal of outcome. This emphasizes the overriding power of Allah's pre-eternal decree and the uncertainty of one's ultimate end. The phrase 'May Allah not deprive us of it' is a supplication included in some transmissions.

Correction: The hadith affirms Allah's comprehensive knowledge and decree, but human actions are still chosen by the individual; the decree does not force actions but encompasses what a person will choose.

?

?
Your lifespan, provision, deeds, and final state were written before you were born. How does that truth affect the way you view your current struggles—your worries about money, your plans for the future, your spiritual highs and lows? What would it look like to live today with absolute trust in that decree?
?
The angel writes the decree before the spirit is breathed. You are alive now because that decree was written. If the final outcome is already recorded, what is the point of your efforts? And yet, the hadith does not stop you from acting—it warns that your actions can be overridden. How does that both sober and liberate you as you strive for Paradise?

The Hadith of Adam and Moses: Divine Decree
Narration of the debate between Adam and Moses on predestination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith of Adam and Moses demonstrates that all actions, including sins, occur within Allah's eternal decree.

Core Idea
Even the first sin was decreed by Allah before creation.

This lesson presents a famous prophetic hadith where Adam and Moses debate the nature of predestination. Moses blames Adam for humanity's expulsion from Paradise, but Adam counters that his deed was already written by Allah before the heavens were created. The hadith is a key proof for Ahl al-Sunnah that divine decree encompasses all events.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation once. Notice how the argument unfolds: Moses blames, Adam responds with the decree, and Adam wins.
Pay attention to the phrase 'before He created the heavens'.
2
Identify the key point of contention
Moses blames Adam for misleading people. Adam does not deny the sin but shifts the focus to Allah's pre-eternal decree.
Adam says the deed was 'written' upon him before creation.
3
Understand the implication for qadar
The hadith is used to affirm that all things, including human actions, are part of Allah's decree. However, it does not negate human accountability.
Adam was still responsible despite the decree.
4
Reflect on the chains of transmission
The passage includes two chains: one via Mu'awiya and one via Malik. Both confirm the same hadith.
Multiple chains strengthen authenticity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وروى معاوية بن عمرو قال: حدثنا زائدة، عن الأعمش، عن أبي صالح، عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه، عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: « احْتَجَّ آدَمُ وَمُوسَى، قَالَ مُوسَى : يَا آدَمُ أَنْتَ الَّذِي خَلَقَكَ اللهُ بِيَدِهِ وَنَفَخَ فِيكَ مِنْ رُوحِهِ ، أَغْوَيْتَ النَّاسَ وَأَخْرَجتَهُمْ مِنَ الجنَّةِ، قَالَ: فَقَالَ أَدَمُ : أَنْتَ مُوسَى الَّذِي اصْطَفَاكَ الله بِكَلِمَاتِهِ ، تَلُومُنِي عَلَى عَمَلٍ كَتَبَهُ اللهُ عَلَيَّ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَخْلُقَ الله السَّمواتِ، قَالَ: فَحَجَّ آدَمُ مُوسَى وروى حديث ( حَجَّ آدَمُ مُوسَى : مالك، عن أبي الزناد، عـن الأعرج، عن أبي هريرة، عن النبي
And Mu'awiya ibn 'Amr narrated, saying: Zaidah narrated, from al-A'mash, from Abu Salih, from Abu Hurairah, may Allah be pleased with him, from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, who said: 'Adam and Moses argued. Moses said: O Adam, you are the one whom Allah created with His hand and breathed into you of His spirit; you misled people and brought them out of Paradise. Adam said: You are Moses, whom Allah chose with His speech; do you blame me for a deed that Allah wrote upon me before He created the heavens?' So Adam overcame Moses in argument.' And he narrated the hadith: 'Adam overcame Moses' — Malik, from Abu al-Zinad, from al-A'raj, from Abu Hurairah, from the Prophet.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage presents the famous hadith of the debate between Adam and Moses. Moses blames Adam for causing humanity's expulsion from Paradise, but Adam counters by pointing out that his sin was already decreed by Allah before creation. The phrase 'before He created the heavens' emphasizes the primacy of divine predestination. The narration concludes that Adam won the argument (حج آدم موسى). The passage also mentions an alternative chain of transmission for the same hadith, from Malik. This hadith is often cited by Ahl al-Sunnah to affirm that all actions, including sins, are by Allah's decree.

Key Terms

الحجاج
الكتاب
السموات
اصطفاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this hadith proves humans have no free will and are not accountable for sins.
Correction: The hadith does not negate accountability; Adam did not deny his sin but affirmed that it occurred within Allah's decree. Humans are still responsible for their choices.

Checkpoint

B) He argued that the sin was not his fault
C) He said the deed was written by Allah before the heavens were created
D) He asked Moses to intercede for him

Key Takeaway
Adam's victory in the argument shows that Allah's eternal decree encompasses all events, even sins, but does not remove human accountability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you secretly feel that 'it was destined' and that absolves you from feeling guilty? How does Adam's willingness to take ownership of the deed ('a deed that Allah wrote upon me') challenge your tendency to hide behind fate?
?

?
Adam's victory was not in denying his sin but in affirming Allah's eternal decree. Is your heart truly at peace with Allah's decree—both for sins you've committed and trials you've faced—or do you wrestle against it? What one step can you take today to surrender to His decree like Adam?

Divine Decree

Two Hadiths on the Writing of Destiny Before Birth
Imam Ash'ari reports two hadiths proving that Allah writes the creature's destiny (ajal, rizq, etc.) before birth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that, according to these hadiths, Allah decrees every aspect of a person's life and fate before they are born, including their term, provision, deeds, effect, character, and whether they are wretched or blessed.

Core Idea
Destiny is written before birth, while the embryo is still in the womb.

Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari presents two prophetic hadiths that firmly establish the Islamic belief in pre-natal destiny. These narrations show that Allah sends an angel to write the creature's entire life course while still in the embryonic stages. Understanding these hadiths is crucial for grasping the early Sunni position on qadar (divine decree).

Guided Path
1
Read the two hadiths
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Notice the chain of narration and the key details.
2
Identify the stages of the embryo
In the first hadith, 'Abdullah describes the drop, blood, blood-clot, and chewed lump stages, each lasting forty days.
This matches embryonic development as known in modern science.
3
List what the angel writes
The angel is commanded to write the person's term, deed, provision, effect, character, and state (wretched or blessed). Memorize these six items.
These cover all major aspects of destiny.
4
Understand the unchangeability of character
The hadith concludes that you cannot change his character unless you change his creation, implying that the decreed character is fixed.
This refutes those who think humans can completely alter their innate disposition.
5
Reflect on the second hadith
The Prophet (peace be upon him) states that every soul's place in Paradise is already written. This complements the first hadith about writing destiny.
Note the hadith is incomplete; it likely also mentioned Hell.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٥١ - وَرَوَى مُعَاوِيَةُ بْنُ عَمْرٍو قَالَ حَدَّثَنَا زَائِدَةُ، عَنْ سُلَيْمَانَ الْأَعْمَشِ، عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ مُرَّةَ عَنْ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ أَبِي لَيْلَى، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللهِ ابْنِ رَبِيعَةَ قَالَ كُنَّا عِنْدَ عَبْدِ اللهِ قَالَ فَذَكَرُوا رَجُلاً فَذَكَرُوا مِنْ أَمْرِهِ فَقَالَ الْقَوْمُ أَمَا لَهُ مَنْ يَأْخُذُ عَلَى يَدَيْهِ قَالَ عَبْدُ اللهِ أَرَأَيْتُمْ لَوْ قُطِعَ رَأْسُهُ كُنْتُمْ تَسْتَطِيعُونَ أَنْ تَجْعَلُوا لَهُ يَداً قَالُوا لَا قَالَ عَبْدُ اللهِ إِنَّ النُّطْفَةَ إِذَا وَقَعَتْ فِي الْمَرْأَةِ مَكَثَتْ أَرْبَعِينَ يَوْماً ثُمَّ انْحَدَرَتْ دَماً ثُمَّ تَكُونُ عَلَقَةً مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ ثُمَّ تَكُونُ مُضْغَةً مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ ثُمَّ يَبْعَثُ اللهُ مَلَكاً فَيَقُولُ اكْتُبْ أَجَلَهُ وَعَمَلَهُ وَرِزْقَهُ وَأَثَرَهُ وَخُلُقَهُ وَشَقِيَ أَوْ سَعِيدٌ وَإِنَّكُمْ لَنْ تَسْتَطِيعُوا أَنْ تُغَيِّرُوا خُلُقَهُ حَتَّى تُغَيِّرُوا خَلْقَهُ. ٢٥٢ - وَرَوَى مُعَاوِيَةُ بْنُ عَمْرٍو قَالَ حَدَّثَنَا زَائِدَةُ عَنْ مَنْصُورٍ عَنْ سَعْدِ بْنِ عُبَيْدَةَ عَنْ أَبِي عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ عَنْ عَلِيٍّ قَالَ كُنَّا فِي جَنَازَةٍ فِي بَقِيعِ الْغَرْقَدِ فَأَتَى النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَعَدَ وَنَحْنُ حَوْلَهُ وَمَعَهُ مِخْصَرَةٌ لَهُ فَنَكَتَ بِهَا وَرَفَعَ رَأْسَهُ فَقَالَ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مَا مِنْكُمْ مِنْ نَفْسٍ مَنْفُوسَةٍ إِلَّا قَدْ كُتِبَ مَكَانُهَا مِنَ الْجَنَّةِ
251 - Mu'awiyah ibn 'Amr narrated, he said: Zaidah narrated to us, from Sulayman al-A'mash, from 'Amr ibn Murrah, from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla, from 'Abdullah ibn Rabi'ah, he said: We were with 'Abdullah, he said: They mentioned a man, and they mentioned about his affair. Then the people said: Does he not have someone to take him by the hand? 'Abdullah said: Do you see? If his head were cut off, would you be able to give him a hand? They said: No. 'Abdullah said: Indeed, when the drop (of semen) falls into the woman, it remains for forty days, then it descends as blood, then it becomes a blood-clot for a similar period, then it becomes a chewed lump for a similar period, then Allah sends an angel, and he says: Write his term, his deed, his provision, his effect, his character, and whether he is wretched or blessed. And indeed you will not be able to change his character until you change his creation. 252 - Mu'awiyah ibn 'Amr narrated, he said: Zaidah narrated to us, from Mansur, from Sa'd ibn 'Ubaydah, from Abu 'Abd al-Rahman, from 'Ali, he said: We were at a funeral in Baqi' al-Gharqad, then the Prophet (peace be upon him) came and sat, and we were around him, and he had a stick with him. He poked the ground with it and raised his head and said, peace be upon him: There is no soul that is breathed except that its place from Paradise has been written.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage reports two hadiths about the writing of destiny before birth. The first hadith is from 'Abdullah ibn Rabi'ah from 'Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud). He gives an analogy: if a man's head is cut off, can you give him a hand? They say no. Then he describes the stages of the embryo: the drop remains in the woman for forty days, then becomes a blood clot, then a chewed lump, each for a similar period. Then Allah sends an angel who is commanded to write the person's term of life, deeds, provision, effect (legacy), character, and whether they are wretched or blessed. The hadith concludes with the statement that you cannot change his character unless you change his creation, implying that the decreed character is fixed. The second hadith is from 'Ali. He describes that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was at a funeral in Baqi' al-Gharqad. He had a stick with him, poked the ground, and raised his head, then said: There is no soul that is breathed except that its place from Paradise has been written. The hadith is incomplete in the text, but the intended meaning is that everyone's destiny regarding Paradise or Hell is already written. Together, these hadiths affirm that Allah decrees every aspect of a person's life and fate before they are born, and that this decree is unalterable.

Stages of the Embryo and Predestination
Hadith about the stages of creation and predestination of the embryo

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the stages of embryonic development as described in the hadith and the predetermined nature of life's key aspects according to Sunni belief.

Core Idea
The embryo's destiny is written by Allah at an early stage, and character is as fixed as creation.

This lesson presents a hadith from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that describes the physical stages of the embryo and the moment when an angel writes the person's entire destiny. The hadith also includes a striking analogy about the impossibility of changing one's inherent nature, reinforcing the doctrine of predestination (qadar). As you read the passage, notice how the stages are linked to the writing of destiny.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its context
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the opening discussion about a man who needs restraint and the analogy about the severed head.
The analogy sets the stage for the doctrine of fixed character.
2
Identify the four stages of the embryo
Find where the stages are mentioned: the drop stays forty days, then becomes blood, then a clot, then a lump of flesh.
Each stage is equal in duration (forty days).
3
Understand what the angel writes
After the lump stage, Allah sends an angel to write specific aspects: lifespan, deeds, provision, impact, character, and final state.
This writing occurs before birth and is unchangeable.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The hadith ends by linking character to creation: you cannot change character unless you change the physical creation.
This emphasizes that destiny is fixed by Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٥١ - وروى معاوية بن عمرو قال حدثنا زائدة، عن سليمان الأعمش، عن عمرو بن مرة عن عبد الرحمن بن أبي ليلى، عن عبد الله ابن ربيعة :قال كنا عند عبد الله قال فذكروا رجلا فذكروا من فقال القوم : أما له من يأخذ على يديه؟ قال عبد الله : أرأيتم لو قطع رأسه كنتم تستطيعون أن تجعلوا له يداً؟ قالوا: لا . قال عبد الله : إِنَّ النُّطْفَةَ إذا وَقَعَتْ في الْمَرْأَةِ مَكَثَتْ أَرْبَعِينَ يَوْماً ، ثُمَّ انْحَدَرَتْ دَماً ، ثُمَّ تَكُونُ عَلَقَةً مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ، ثُمَّ تَكُونُ مُضْغَةً مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ، ثُمَّ يَبْعَثُ الله مَلَكَاً فَيَقُولُ: اكْتُبْ أَجَلَهُ وَعَمَلَهُ وَرِزْقَهُ وَأَثَرَهُ وَخُلُقَهُ وَشَقِيٌّ أَوْ سَعِيدٌ، وَإِنَّكُمْ لَنْ تَسْتَطِيعُوا أَنْ تُغَيِّرُوا خُلُقَهُ حَتَّى تُغَيِّرُوا خَلْقَهُ
251 – And Mu'awiya ibn 'Amr narrated, saying: Zaidah narrated to us, from Sulaiman al-A'mash, from 'Amr ibn Murrah, from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla, from 'Abdullah ibn Rabi'ah, who said: We were with 'Abdullah, and they mentioned a man and mentioned about him, so the people said: Does he not have someone to restrain him? 'Abdullah said: Do you think that if his head were cut off, you could make him a hand? They said: No. 'Abdullah said: Verily, when the drop (of semen) falls in the woman, it stays for forty days, then it descends as blood, then it becomes a clot for like that, then it becomes a lump of flesh for like that, then Allah sends an angel who says: Write his lifespan, his deeds, his provision, his impact, his character, and whether he is wretched or blessed. And you will not be able to change his character until you change his creation.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage contains a hadith narrated by 'Abdullah ibn Rabi'ah from 'Abdullah (likely Ibn Mas'ud). It begins with a discussion about a man who is not being restrained from evil. 'Abdullah uses an analogy: if a man's head is cut off, you cannot give him a hand, implying that changing a person's inherent nature is as impossible as restoring a severed head. He then describes the stages of embryonic development: the drop stays forty days, then becomes blood, then a clot, then a lump of flesh. At that point, Allah sends an angel to write the person's lifespan, deeds, provision, impact, character, and final state (wretched or blessed). The hadith concludes that one cannot change a person's character (khuluq) unless one changes his physical creation (khalq), emphasizing the fixed nature of predestination.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This hadith is sometimes misinterpreted to mean that human effort is futile, since everything is already written.
Correction: The hadith teaches that Allah's knowledge is fixed and that the decree is unchangeable, but it does not negate free will or responsibility. The angel writes what will occur, but the actions themselves are still performed by the individual.

Key Takeaway
The hadith teaches that from the moment the embryo forms, Allah determines every aspect of the person's life, including character, and no one can alter that decree.

Predestination and the Command to Work
Prophet's refutation of fatalism by linking predestination to facilitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet reconciled predestination with human action, emphasizing that divine facilitation aligns with one's choices.

Core Idea
Predestination includes the means; work is part of the decree.

This hadith presents a classic challenge to predestinarian belief: if everything is written, why bother striving? The Prophet's response clarifies that divine predestination does not negate effort; rather, Allah facilitates each person towards the deeds that lead to their destined outcome. Understanding this balance is essential for a sound Islamic theology of qadar.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith narrative
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the setting: a funeral, the Prophet's declaration about every soul's place being written.
Pay attention to the precise wording: 'written as wretched or blessed.'
2
Identify the objection
A listener asks: if everything is pre-written, why not abandon work? This is a common fatalistic misunderstanding of predestination.
3
Analyze the Prophet's response
The Prophet commands: 'Work, for each is facilitated.' He does not deny predestination but redefines it as facilitation towards deeds aligned with one's destiny.
Note the word 'taysir' (facilitation) which becomes a key concept.
4
Examine the Quranic proof
The Prophet recites verses 92:5-10 which describe two types of people and how Allah eases them toward ease or difficulty. This shows that predestination involves facilitating one's chosen path.
5
Connect to broader kalam
Reflect on how this hadith addresses the tension between divine decree and human responsibility. It affirms both: destiny is fixed, but effort is part of that destiny.
This is a key argument in Sunni qadar theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٥٢ - وروى معاوية بن عمرو قال: حدثنا زائدة عن منصور عن سعد بن عبيدة، عن أبي عبد الرحمن، عن علي ، قال : كنا في جنازة في بقيع الغرقد فأتى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقعد ونحن حوله، ومعه مخصرة له فنكت بها ورفع رأسه، فقال صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَا مِنْكُمْ مِنْ نَفْسٍ مَنْفُوسَة إلا قَدْ كُتبَ مَكَانَها مِنَ الجَنَّةِ وَالنَّارِ، وَإِلا قَدْ كُتِبَتْ شَقِيَّةٌ أَو سَعِيْدَةٌ ». فقال رجل من القوم: يـا رسـول الله ! أفلا نمكث على كتابنا وندع العمل؟ فمن كان من أهل السعادة يصير إلى السعادة ومن كان من أهل الشقاوة فيصير إلى الشقاوة، فقال: « اعْمَلُوا فَكُلَّ مُيَسَّر، أمَّا أَهْلُ الشَّقَاوَةِ فَمُيَسَّرُونَ لِعَمَلِ الشَّقَاوَةِ، وأَمَّا أَهْلُ السَّعَادَةِ فَمُيَسَّرُونَ لِعَمَلِ السَّعَادَةِ »، ثم قرأ ( فَأَمَّا مَنْ أَعْطَى وَاتَّقَى * وَصَدَقَ بِالْحُسْنَى * فَسَنُيَسِرُهُ لِلْيُسْرَى * وَأَمَّا مَنْ بَخِلَ وَاسْتَغْنَى * وَكَذَبَ بِالْحُسْنَى * فَسَنُيَسِرُهُ لِلْعُسْرَى ) [الليل: ٥-١٠]
252 – And Mu'awiya ibn 'Amr narrated, saying: Zaidah narrated to us from Mansur, from Sa'd ibn 'Ubaidah, from Abu 'Abd al-Rahman, from 'Ali, who said: We were at a funeral in Baqi' al-Gharqad, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) came, sat down, and we were around him. He had a stick with him, and he poked the ground with it and raised his head, then said: 'There is not a single soul that is created except that its place in Paradise or Hell has been written, and except that it has been written as wretched or blessed.' A man from the people said: O Messenger of Allah, should we not then rely on our book and abandon work? For whoever is among the people of happiness will attain happiness, and whoever is among the people of wretchedness will attain wretchedness. He said: 'Work, for each is facilitated. As for the people of wretchedness, they are facilitated for the deeds of wretchedness, and as for the people of happiness, they are facilitated for the deeds of happiness.' Then he recited: 'As for he who gives and fears Allah, and believes in the best [reward], We will ease him toward ease. But as for he who withholds and considers himself self-sufficient, and denies the best [reward], We will ease him toward difficulty.' [Al-Layl 92:5-10]
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This hadith, narrated by 'Ali ibn Abi Talib, recounts an incident at a funeral in Baqi' al-Gharqad. The Prophet declared that every soul's place in Paradise or Hell and its state (wretched or blessed) is already written. A listener then raised a common objection: if everything is predetermined, why not stop working and simply rely on what is written? The Prophet's answer is crucial: 'Work, for each is facilitated.' He explains that the people of wretchedness are facilitated for the deeds of wretchedness, and the people of happiness are facilitated for the deeds of happiness. He then recited the Quranic verses from Surat al-Layl, which describe how Allah eases each person toward the path that matches their inclination. Thus, predestination does not negate human action; rather, divine facilitation aligns with one's choices.

العمل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Predestination makes human effort pointless, so we should rely on the decree and not work.
Correction: The hadith shows that predestination includes the means (effort) and that Allah facilitates each person towards the deeds of their destiny. Therefore, effort is part of the decree and must be undertaken.

C) He said 'Work, for each is facilitated' and recited Quran
D) He remained silent

Key Takeaway
Predestination does not negate effort; rather, Allah facilitates each person towards the deeds that lead to their destined outcome.
