The Change of Final Deeds Before Death
Hadith about a man who works like people of Paradise but ends in Hell, and vice versa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that a person's final actions before death determine their eternal outcome, in accordance with divine decree.

Core Idea
Your final state is known only to Allah.

This hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) illustrates a profound aspect of divine predestination: a person may appear righteous or wicked throughout life, but their ultimate destination depends on their actions just before death. It teaches us not to judge based on appearances and to never despair of Allah's mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the Prophet's words sink in.
Notice the parallel structure of the two scenarios.
2
Identify the two scenarios
The hadith presents two opposite cases. Identify each and note how they mirror each other.
One case: good deeds then change to bad. Other: bad deeds then change to good.
3
Reflect on 'written in the Book'
Consider what it means that the person's fate is already written. How does this reconcile with the change of deeds?
This shows divine knowledge and predestination.
4
Apply the lesson
Think about the implications: not to be complacent in good deeds, nor to despair of Allah's mercy.
The final state is hidden; we must strive until death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٥٣ وروى موسى بن إسماعيل قال : حدثنا حماد، قال: أنا هشام ابن عروة، عن عروة، عن عائشة رضي الله عنها أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «إِنَّ الرَّجُلَ لَيَعْمَلُ بِعَمَلِ أَهْلِ الْجَنَّةِ ، وَإِنَّهُ مَكْتُوبٌ فِي الْكِتَابِ مِنْ أَهْلِ النَّارِ، فَإِذَا كَانَ قَبْلَ مَوْتِهِ تَحَوَّلَ فَعَمِلَ بِعَمَلِ أَهْلِ النَّارِ، فَمَاتَ فَدَخَلَ النَّارَ ، وَإِنَّ الرَّجُلَ لَيَعْمَلُ بِعَمَلِ أَهْلِ النَّارِ، وَإِنَّهُ مَكْتُوبٌ فِي الْكِتَابِ أَنَّهُ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْجَنَّةِ، فَإِذَا كَانَ قَبْلَ مَوْتِهِ تَحَوَّلَ فَعَمِلَ بِعَمَلِ أَهْلِ الْجَنَّةِ ، فَدَخَلَ الجنة»
253 – And Musa ibn Isma'il narrated, saying: Hammad narrated to us, saying: Hisham ibn 'Urwah informed us, from 'Urwah, from 'A'ishah (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed, a man may perform the deeds of the people of Paradise, while he is written in the Book as one of the people of Hell; then just before his death, he changes and performs the deeds of the people of Hell, so he dies and enters Hell. And indeed, a man may perform the deeds of the people of Hell, while he is written in the Book as one of the people of Paradise; then just before his death, he changes and performs the deeds of the people of Paradise, so he enters Paradise.'
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This hadith from 'A'ishah addresses the nature of divine predestination and the importance of one's final state. It describes two scenarios: a person who consistently does good deeds like the people of Paradise, yet is written in the Book as destined for Hell; but before death, he changes and does evil deeds, thus entering Hell. Conversely, a person who does evil deeds like the people of Hell, but is written as destined for Paradise, changes before death and does good deeds, entering Paradise. The hadith emphasizes that the final actions before death determine the ultimate outcome, and this is consistent with what was written in the Book. It underscores the mystery of predestination: people may appear righteous or wicked, but their end is known only to Allah and aligns with His decree.

Misconception & Correction

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Reflect on your own consistency: Do you take your faith for granted? This hadith strips away all security. What concrete step will you take today to guard against a bad end, knowing that the final decision is out of your hands yet your actions matter?

Hadith as Proof of Allah's Foreknowledge and Predestination
Summarizing hadith proofs for predestination

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith collectively establish Allah's foreknowledge, predestined writing, and the division of humanity into two groups.

Core Idea
The hadith prove Allah knew, wrote, and created two groups: Paradise and Hell.

The author concludes the discussion of predestination by summarizing how the hadith support core Islamic beliefs. This passage ties together divine knowledge, divine decree, and the two destinies of humanity, quoting Quranic verses to reinforce the point.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the flow. Notice how each claim is supported by scripture.
The passage ends abruptly; the conclusion is implicit.
2
Identify the four claims
Look for: Allah knew what would be, He wrote it, He wrote the people of Paradise and Hell, and He created them as two groups.
These are the key points from the hadith summary.
3
Connect with the Quranic quotes
The author cites three verses to corroborate the hadith. Note how each verse reinforces the division into groups.
These verses are from Al-A'raf, Ash-Shura, and Hud.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why this summary is placed at the end. It brings together revelation-based proofs (hadith and Quran) for the doctrine of predestination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذه الأحاديث تدل على أن الله عز وجل علم ما يكون أنه يكون وكتبه، وأنه قد كتب أهل الجنة وأهل النار ، وخلقهم فريقين: فريقاً في الجنة وفريقاً في السعير، وبذلك نطق كتابه العزيز إذ يقول : ( فَرِيقًا هَدَى وَفَرِيقًا حَقَّ عَلَيْهِمُ الضَّلَالَةُ ) [الأعراف:٣٠] وقال تعالى: ( فَرِيقٌ فِي الْجَنَّةِ وَفَرِيقٌ فِي السَّعِيرِ ) [الشورى: ٧] وقال تعالى: ( فَمِنْهُمْ شَقِيٌّ وَسَعِيدٌ ) [هود: ١٠٥] فخلق الله
And these hadith indicate that Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, knew what would be that it would be, and wrote it, and that He wrote the people of Paradise and the people of Hell, and created them as two groups: a group in Paradise and a group in the Blazing Fire. And with that speaks His Mighty Book, when He says: 'A group He guided, and a group deserved error' [Al-A'raf 7:30], and He said: 'A group in Paradise and a group in the Blazing Fire' [Ash-Shura 42:7], and He said: 'Among them are wretched and blessed' [Hud 11:105]. So Allah created...
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This concluding passage summarizes the preceding hadith, affirming that they collectively establish key points of Islamic creed regarding predestination. First, Allah knew everything that would come to pass before it occurred. Second, He wrote that knowledge in the Preserved Tablet. Third, He specifically wrote the names of the people of Paradise and the people of Hell. Fourth, He created humanity as two distinct groups destined for either Paradise or Hellfire. The author then supports this with three Quranic verses: from Al-A'raf (7:30) stating that some are guided and others deserve error; from Ash-Shura (42:7) explicitly dividing people into two groups; and from Hud (11:105) stating that among them are wretched and blessed. The passage ends abruptly with 'so Allah created...', but the intended meaning is clear that Allah created these groups according to His foreknowledge and decree.

Correction: The author shows predestination is a core belief supported by revelation, not conflicting with responsibility.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The hadith and Quran divide humanity into two groups. Which group do you honestly expect to be in if you were to die tonight? What is stopping you from truly living as if that expectation compels you to change?
?
Do you use the belief in predestination as an excuse to delay repentance or action? Ponder: if Allah knows all, but you still have free will, what will you do this week to ensure your name is in the book of the people of Paradise?

Hadith and Verse on Predestination of Felicity and Misery
Al-Ash'ari quotes a hadith and verse affirming predestination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari uses a Quranic verse and a hadith to affirm Allah's predestination of people for Paradise or Hell.

Core Idea
Allah has predetermined who will be wretched and who will be happy.

Al-Ash'ari opens this section with a bold declaration about predestination, then immediately supports it with divine revelation. The verse from Surat al-A'raf and the prophetic hadith both reinforce the same point: ultimate destinies are in Allah's hands. In this lesson, you will examine these textual proofs and consider their implications.

The verse is from Surah al-A'raf, verse 179.

It shows humility and recognition of the gravity of the topic.

The author does not discuss free will here, but the broader Islamic teaching holds both predestination and accountability.

The Covenant as Proof Against Qadariyya
Al-Ash'ari presents the verse of the covenant and the hadith of Adam's progeny as proof against Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ash'ari uses the verse of the covenant and the hadith of Adam's progeny as a proof against the Qadariyya doctrine of complete free will.

Core Idea
The primordial covenant is Allah's enduring proof against human denial of His lordship.

Al-Ash'ari introduces a foundational proof from the Qur'an and Sunnah against those who deny predestination. The verse of the covenant (al-A'raf 172) and the prophetic hadith about the extraction of Adam's descendants establish that all humanity acknowledged Allah's lordship in the primordial realm. This pre-creation acknowledgment serves as an irrevocable witness against any later denial.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the flow: verse, hadith, then explanation of the proof.
The footnote marker (۲) is part of the original text.
2
Identify the two sources of proof
The author uses the Qur'anic verse (al-A'raf 172) and a hadith about Allah extracting Adam's progeny. Locate each.
3
Understand the logical structure
The verse describes the covenant; the hadith adds the extraction context. Together they show that Allah made humans testify to His lordship, creating an undeniable proof.
The proof hinges on this primordial testimony.
4
Reflect on the refutation of Qadariyya
The Qadariyya deny that Allah has decreed actions. But the covenant shows that humans have innate knowledge of Allah, and rejecting it is willful denial, not ignorance.
This supports the Ash'ari position on predestination.
5
Connect to broader doctrine
Consider how this proof fits into the overall argument for divine decree. It establishes that humans are accountable from the very beginning.

Source Text

دليل في القدر :
ومما يدل على بطلان قول القدرية قول الله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذْ أَخَذَ رَبُّكَ مِنْ
بَنِي ءَادَمَ مِن ظُهُورِهِمْ ذُرِّيَّتَهُمْ ) الآية [الأعراف: ۱۷۲] .

Proof on Predestination: Among what indicates the invalidity of the Qadariyya's statement is the saying of Allah, Exalted: 'And when your Lord took from the children of Adam, from their loins, their descendants...' the verse [al-A'raf: 172]. And the narration has come from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him: 'Allah, Exalted and Majestic, wiped Adam's back and brought forth his descendants from his back like small ants, then He made them affirm His oneness, and He established (2) the proof against them' because He, Exalted, said: 'And He made them testify against themselves, "Am I not your Lord?" They said, "Yes, we testify."' Allah, Exalted and Majestic, said: 'Lest you say on the Day of Resurrection, "Indeed we were unaware of this."' [al-A'raf: 172] Thus He made their affirmation of His oneness, when He brought them out of Adam's back, a proof against them if they deny in this world what they had known in the first realm, then after acknowledgment they reject it.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This is a proof against the Qadariyya (those who deny predestination). It uses the verse of the covenant (al-A'raf 172) and the prophetic hadith about the extraction of souls from Adam. The argument is that Allah made humanity testify to His lordship in the primordial state, establishing a proof so that on Judgment Day they cannot claim ignorance. This testifies that knowledge of Allah is inherent, and denying it is a rejection of that initial acknowledgment. The author emphasizes that this covenant serves as a divine proof against those who later disbelieve.

Correction: The covenant is a metaphysical reality signifying the innate human knowledge of God, not a temporal event.

Key Takeaway
The primordial covenant is a decisive proof that all humans have innate knowledge of God and cannot plead ignorance on Judgment Day.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Hadith of Two Handfuls: Predestination of Happiness and Misery
Al-Ash'ari quotes a hadith about two handfuls and a verse showing predestination of happiness and misery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a prophetic hadith and a Quranic verse together demonstrate that happiness and misery are predetermined by Allah's prior knowledge and will.

Core Idea
In the end, happiness or misery is decreed by Allah from the beginning.

This passage from Al-Ash'ari presents a hadith in which Allah takes two handfuls, one for Paradise and one for Hell, showing that the final outcome is divinely decided. He then quotes the verse where the people of Hell admit that their wretchedness overcame them. This lesson explores how these texts establish the doctrine of predestination in Sunni theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the prophetic narration describing Allah's two handfuls and the prevailing of wretchedness and happiness. Notice the imagery of divine selection.
2
Study the Quranic confirmation
Read the verse from Surah al-Mu'minun where the damned confess that their wretchedness overcame them. Reflect on how it echoes the hadith.
3
Understand the theological conclusion
Observe how Al-Ash'ari concludes that all of this occurs by Allah's prior knowledge, will, and desire. This grounds the doctrine of qadar.

Source Text

Allah, Exalted and Majestic, reported about the people of the Fire that they said: 'Our Lord, our wretchedness prevailed over us, and we were a people astray.' [al-Mu'minun: 106] And all of that is by a command that preceded in the knowledge of Allah, Exalted and Majestic, and His will was executed in it, and His desire preceded it.

Commentary
This passage presents a prophetic hadith describing Allah taking two handfuls, one for Paradise and one for Hell, indicating that the division is predetermined. The hadith says that wretchedness or happiness prevails over the respective groups. Then a Quranic verse (al-Mu'minun 106) is quoted where the people of Hell confess that their wretchedness overcame them. The author concludes that all of this occurs according to Allah's prior knowledge, will, and desire, reinforcing the doctrine of predestination.

?

The Child's Funeral and Predestination of Felicity
Al-Ash'ari recounts a hadith illustrating predestination of felicity and misery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine of predestination as illustrated by the Prophet's correction of Aisha's assumption about a child's guaranteed Paradise.

Core Idea
Allah's decree precedes birth — every soul is already assigned its destiny.

This lesson presents a famous hadith where the Prophet gently corrects Aisha's assumption that a child who died before sinning was guaranteed Paradise. Through this incident, we learn a foundational principle of Islamic theology: Allah has decreed for each person their ultimate happiness or wretchedness from before their creation. The lesson also introduces the complementary principle that human effort is still required.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the dialogue between Aisha and the Prophet, and the author's concluding remark.
The hadith is from Aisha, the Mother of the Believers.
2
Identify Aisha's assumption and the Prophet's correction
Aisha thought the child was happy because he died sinless. The Prophet corrected her by stating that Allah has already designated people for Paradise or Fire while they are still in their fathers' loins.
This emphasizes that predestination is not based solely on actions but on Allah's eternal decree.
3
Understand the theological implications
The author comments that this shows happiness and wretchedness have already preceded for their people. Then the Prophet adds that everyone should act, for each is facilitated towards what they were created for. This balances predestination with human responsibility.
Both divine decree and human action are affirmed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٥٧ - وروى معاوية بن عمرو قال حدثنا ،زائدة قال : حدثنا طلحة بن يحيى القرشي، قال: حدثتني عائشة بنت طلحة عن عائشة أم المؤمنين رضي الله عنها أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم دُعِيَ إلى جنازة غلام من الأنصار ليـصـلـي عليـه، فقالــت عائشة : طوبى لهذا يا رسول الله ! عصفور من عصافير الجنة لم يعمل سوءاً ولم يدركه ، قال : ( أَوَ غَيْرَ ذَلِكَ يَا عَائِشَةُ إِنَّ الله عَزَّ وَجَلَّ قَدْ جَعَلَ الجَنَّةِ أَهْلاً وَهُمْ في أصلاب آبَائِهِم، وللنَّارِ أَهْلاً جَعَلَهُم لَهَا وَهُمْ فِي أَصْلابِ آبَائِهِم»(۱) أن السعادة قد سبقت لأهلها، والشقاء قد سبق لأهـلـه. وقال النبي : ( اعْمَلُوا فَكُلِّ مُيَسَّرْ لِمَا خُلِقَ لَهُ ، (٢). وهذا يبين
257 - And Mu'awiya ibn 'Amr narrated, he said: Zaidah narrated to us, he said: Talha ibn Yahya al-Qurashi narrated to us, he said: 'A'isha bint Talha narrated to me from 'A'isha, the Mother of the Believers, may Allah be pleased with her, that the Prophet, peace be upon him, was invited to the funeral of a boy from the Ansar to pray over him. 'A'isha said: 'Happy is this one, O Messenger of Allah! A sparrow of the sparrows of Paradise, he did no evil and did not reach it?' He said: 'Or other than that, O 'A'isha? Indeed Allah, Exalted and Majestic, has made people for Paradise while they are in the loins of their fathers, and made people for the Fire while they are in the loins of their fathers.' This shows that happiness has preceded for its people, and wretchedness has preceded for its people. And the Prophet said: 'Act, for each is made easy for that for which he was created.' This makes clear
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage narrates an incident where a young boy from the Ansar died, and Aisha thought he was guaranteed Paradise because he died before committing sins. The Prophet corrected her by stating that Allah has predestined people for Paradise or Fire even while they are in the loins of their fathers. The author then comments that this shows happiness and wretchedness have already preceded for their respective people. The Prophet then adds that everyone should act, but each person is facilitated towards what they were created for. This combines predestination with human action, indicating that divine decree does not negate effort.

الشقاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Children who die before sinning are guaranteed Paradise.
Correction: The hadith teaches that Allah's decree applies to all, including children, but does not specify the fate of specific children; rather, it emphasizes that predestination is from before birth and that final outcomes are known only to Allah.

Checkpoint
Why did the Prophet correct Aisha's assumption about the child?
A) Because the child had sinned.
B) Because Allah's predestination applies to all, even before birth.
C) Because the child was not from the Ansar.
D) Because Aisha was not present at the funeral.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet taught that Allah's decree of happiness or misery precedes birth, yet humans are to act according to their created purpose.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you read that Allah has made people for Paradise and for Fire before birth, does it trouble your heart? How will you live today differently, knowing that your actions are not irrelevant but are facilitated by His decree? Write down one fear you have about predestination and bring it before Allah in your next prayer.
?
Aisha assumed the child was saved because of his innocence. What assumptions do you make about your own salvation? How can you replace complacency with the urgency of 'Act'? Name one area in your life where you have been passive, trusting merely in your circumstances, and commit to a concrete change starting now.

Another Proof: Allah Creates All Actions, Including Unbelief
Al-Ash'ari cites Quranic verses to prove Allah creates all actions, including unbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ash'ari uses Quranic verses to prove that Allah is the creator of all actions, including misguidance and unbelief, refuting the Qadariyya.

Core Idea
Every action, even unbelief, is created by Allah alone.

In this passage, Al-Ash'ari presents a second proof from the Quran demonstrating that Allah is the creator of all human actions, including disbelief. He cites several verses that attribute guidance and misguidance directly to Allah, concluding that unbelief, since it occurs by Allah's will, must be created by Him. This argument directly challenges the Qadariyya who claim humans independently create their deeds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice how Al-Ash'ari moves from verse to verse, building his case.
2
Identify each Quranic verse
Find each verse cited and note what it says about Allah's actions: guidance, misguidance, doing what He wills, creating your works.
There are four verses quoted.
3
Follow the logical deduction
The author argues: if unbelief is something Allah intended, then He must have done it, decreed it, and created it. See how the verses support that.
4
Reflect on the implication for Qadariyya
Consider how this argument refutes the view that humans create their own actions independently. The passage directly attributes all actions to Allah.

Source Text

٢٥٨- دليل آخر :
وقد قال الله عز وجل: (مَن يَهْدِ اللهُ فَهُوَ الْمُهْتَدِ وَمَن يُضْلِلْ فَلَن تَجِدَ لَهُ وَلِيًّا ترشدا ﴾ [الكهف: ١٧] وقال تعالى: ﴿يُضِلُّ بِهِ كَثِيرًا وَيَهْدِي بِهِ كَثِيرًا ) [البقرة: ٢٦] فأخبر تعالى أنه يضل ويهدي، وقال: (وَيُضِلُّ اللَّهُ الظَّالِمِينَ وَيَفْعَلُ اللَّهُ مَا يَشَاءُ) [إبراهيم: ۲۷] فأخبرنا أنه ﴿ فَعَالٌ لِمَا يُرِيدُ ) [البروج: ١٦] وإذا كان الكفــر ممـا أراده فقد فعله وقدره وأحدثه وأنشأه واخترعه وقد بيّن ذلك بقوله : أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ * وَاللهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الصافات: ٩٥-٩٦] .
258 - Another proof: And Allah, Exalted and Majestic, said: 'Whomever Allah guides, he is the guided one, and whomever He leads astray, you will not find for him a protecting guide.' [al-Kahf: 17] And He, Exalted, said: 'He leads astray many thereby and guides many thereby.' [al-Baqara: 26] Thus He informed that He leads astray and guides. And He said: 'And Allah leads astray the wrongdoers, and Allah does what He wills.' [Ibrahim: 27] Thus He informed us that He is the 'Doer of what He intends.' [al-Buruj: 16] And if unbelief is something He intended, then He did it, decreed it, brought it about, originated it, and created it. And He clarified that by His saying: 'Do you worship what you carve, while Allah created you and what you do?' [al-Saffat: 95-96].

Commentary
This is another proof from the Quran demonstrating that Allah is the creator of all actions, including misguidance and unbelief. The author cites several verses: al-Kahf 17 states that whoever Allah leads astray has no guide; al-Baqara 26 says that Allah leads astray many and guides many; Ibrahim 27 says that Allah leads astray the wrongdoers and does what He wills; al-Buruj 16 says Allah is the Doer of what He intends. From these, the author deduces that if unbelief is something Allah intended, then He must have done it, decreed it, and created it. This is further supported by al-Saffat 95-96, which states that Allah created both humans and their actions. This refutes the Qadariyya who claim humans create their own deeds independently.

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The passage does not deny human choice and responsibility; it affirms that Allah's creation encompasses all actions, but humans still have free will and are accountable.

Key Takeaway
Allah is the creator of all human actions, including disbelief, as affirmed by multiple Quranic verses, refuting the idea that humans independently create their deeds.

?
When you see someone in disbelief, do you attribute their state to Allah's creation and still feel compassion? Or do you judge them as if they created their own unbelief? How can you align your heart with the reality that Allah is the creator of all actions, including that person's rejection?

Hadith on Predestination of People for Paradise or Hell
Imam Ash'ari quotes a hadith to prove predestination of happiness and misery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran and hadith affirm that Allah's knowledge and will predetermine every person's ultimate happiness or misery, while still commanding action.

Core Idea
Our ultimate destiny is known to Allah before we are born.

Imam Ash'ari presents two scriptural proofs for the doctrine of predestination (qadar). First, a Quranic verse where the people of Hell admit their misery overcame them, and second, a hadith where the Prophet corrects Aisha's assumption about a child's guaranteed Paradise. These texts establish that Allah's foreknowledge and will encompass everyone's final end, yet humans are still commanded to act.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once without analysis. Let the words of the Quran and the Prophet sink in.
2
Understand the correction of Aisha
Notice that Aisha thought the child was guaranteed Paradise because he had not sinned. The Prophet corrected her, explaining that Allah appoints people for Paradise or Fire even before they are born.
This shows that destiny is not based solely on actions but on Allah's eternal decree.
3
Grasp the balance between decree and action
The Prophet also said, 'Act, for each is facilitated for what he was created for.' This shows that divine decree does not negate human effort; rather, actions are enabled according to one's created purpose.
This refutes the misconception that predestination means fatalism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الله عز وجل مخبراً عن أهل النار أنهم قالوا: ﴿رَبَّنَا غَلَبَتْ عَلَيْنَا شِقْوَتُنَا وَكُنَّا قَوْمًا ضَالِينَ ﴾ [المؤمنون: ١٠٦] وكل ذلك بأمر قد سبق في علم الله عز وجل، ونفذت فيه إرادته وتقدمت فيه مشيئته. ٢٥٧ - وروى معاوية بن عمرو قال حدثنا زائدة قال : حدثنا طلحة بن يحيى القرشي، قال: حدثتني عائشة بنت طلحة عن عائشة أم المؤمنين رضي الله عنها أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم دُعِيَ إلى جنازة غلام من الأنصار ليـصـلـي عليـه، فقالــت عائشة : طوبى لهذا يا رسول الله ! عصفور من عصافير الجنة لم يعمل سوءاً ولم يدركه ، قال : ( أَوَ غَيْرَ ذَلِكَ يَا عَائِشَةُ إِنَّ الله عَزَّ وَجَلَّ قَدْ جَعَلَ الجَنَّةِ أَهْلاً وَهُمْ في أصلاب آبَائِهِم، وللنَّارِ أَهْلاً جَعَلَهُم لَهَا وَهُمْ فِي أَصْلابِ آبَائِهِم»(١) أن السعادة قد سبقت لأهلها، والشقاء قد سبق لأهـلـه. وقال النبي : ( اعْمَلُوا فَكُلِّ مُيَسَّرْ لِمَا خُلِقَ لَهُ ، (٢).
Allah Almighty said, informing about the people of the Fire that they said: "Our Lord, our misery overcame us, and we were a people astray" [Al-Mu'minun: 106]. And all of that is by a command that had preceded in the knowledge of Allah Almighty, and His will was executed in it and His volition preceded in it. 257 - And Mu'awiyah ibn 'Amr narrated, he said: Zaidah narrated to us, he said: Talhah ibn Yahya al-Qurashi narrated to us, he said: 'A'ishah bint Talhah narrated to me from 'A'ishah, the Mother of the Believers, may Allah be pleased with her, that the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, was invited to the funeral of a young boy from the Ansar to pray over him. 'A'ishah said: "Glad tidings for this one, O Messenger of Allah! A sparrow of the sparrows of Paradise, he did not do evil and did not attain it." He said: "Or other than that, O 'A'ishah? Verily Allah, Mighty and Majestic, has made people for Paradise while they are in the loins of their fathers, and made people for the Fire while they are in the loins of their fathers" — that happiness has preceded for its people, and misery has preceded for its people. And the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, said: "Act, for each is facilitated for what he was created for."
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the predestination of happiness and misery, combining a Quranic verse and a prophetic hadith. The author begins by quoting Allah's statement from Surat al-Mu'minun, in which the people of Hell acknowledge that their misery overwhelmed them and they were astray. The author then comments that all of this occurs by a command that had already preceded in Allah's knowledge, and that His will and volition were executed in it. This establishes that misery and happiness are decreed from eternity. Then the author brings a narration from 'A'ishah: when the Prophet was called to pray over a deceased child, 'A'ishah expressed that the child, having not committed sin, is a sparrow of Paradise. The Prophet corrected her, explaining that Allah has appointed people for Paradise and for the Fire while they are still in the loins of their fathers, implying that their ultimate destiny is predetermined. The author draws the conclusion: 'that happiness has preceded for its people, and misery has preceded for its people.' Finally, the author quotes another saying of the Prophet: 'Act, for each is facilitated for what he was created for,' indicating that divine decree does not negate human action but rather that actions are enabled according to one's created purpose. The passage thus affirms that ultimate felicity or damnation is known to Allah from eternity and that His will encompasses all.

Key Takeaway
Allah's knowledge and will determine every person's final destination, yet humans are commanded to act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah has already written who is destined for Paradise and who for Hell, does that make your daily choices feel heavy or light? Will you use the decree as an excuse to stop striving, or as a reason to ask Allah for steadfastness in His decree?
?
The Prophet said, 'Act, for each is facilitated for what he was created for.' Think of a time you felt your efforts were wasted. In light of this hadith, can you trust that even your struggles are enabled by Allah for your predetermined end? Will you commit to acting, not because you control the outcome, but because Allah facilitates your deeds for your fate?
?
Aisha assumed the child was guaranteed Paradise because of his innocence. When you judge others' religious states—whether their piety or their sin—are you relying on outward appearance, or do you submit to Allah's hidden knowledge? Will you repent from assuming you know who is saved and who is damned, and instead focus on your own actions?

Objection Answered: Why the Disbeliever Cannot Create His Own Disbelief
Ash'ari argues that the corrupt nature of disbelief must be created by Allah, not by the disbeliever.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari argues that the corrupt nature of disbelief is created by Allah, not by the disbeliever, based on the principle that an agent must know an action's true reality to be its author.

Core Idea
Disbelievers cannot create their own disbelief because they do not know its true corrupt reality.

This passage presents a powerful objection-and-answer argument. Imam al-Ash'ari poses a dilemma to those who claim that disbelievers create their own disbelief. He shows that if the disbeliever's act is corrupt, the disbeliever cannot be its author, because he believes it to be good. Therefore, the corruption must be created by Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Then read the literal translation. Notice how the argument progresses from a question to a conclusion.
2
Identify the objection and the answer
The passage begins with a question. Identify who is being addressed and what the question is. Then see how the author refutes the opponent's possible answer.
3
Understand the key principle
The author uses a principle: an act is only an act in its reality if the agent knows it as it is. Ponder why this principle is used and how it supports the conclusion.
4
Trace the conclusion
The conclusion is that Allah decrees and creates disbelief as corrupt. See how the reasoning leads to this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٥٩- مسألة : ويقال لهم : هل فعل الكافر الكفر فاسداً باطلاً متناقضاً؟ فإن قالوا: نعم . قيل لهم : وكيف يفعله فاسداً متناقضاً قبيحاً، وهو يعتقده حسناً صحيحاً أفضل الأديان؟ وإذا لم يجز ذلك ؛ لأن الفعل لا يكون فعلاً على حقيقته إلا ممن علمه على ما هو عليه من حقيقته، كما لا يجوز أن يكون فعلاً ممن لم يعلمه فعلاً، فقد وجب أن الله عز وجل هو الذي قدر الكفر وخلقه كفراً فاسداً باطلاً متناقضاً، خلافاً للحق والسداد .
259 - Issue: And it is said to them: Is the disbeliever's disbelief an act that is corrupt, invalid, and contradictory? If they say: Yes. It is said to them: How can he do it as corrupt, contradictory, and ugly while he believes it to be good, correct, and the best of religions? And if that is not permissible — because an act is not an act in its true reality except from one who knows it as it is in its reality, just as it is not permissible for it to be an act from one who does not know it as an act — then it is established that Allah Almighty is the One who decreed disbelief and created it as disbelief corrupt, invalid, and contradictory, contrary to truth and rightness.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer argument against those who claim that disbelievers create their own disbelief. The author poses a dilemma: 'Is the disbeliever's disbelief an act that is corrupt, invalid, and contradictory?' If the opponent answers 'yes,' then the author asks: how can the disbeliever perform it as corrupt, contradictory, and ugly while he himself believes it to be good, correct, and the best of religions? This is impossible because an action is only truly an action (in its reality) if the agent knows it exactly as it is. For example, one cannot intentionally perform an act of disbelief while believing it is true faith. Therefore, since the disbeliever does not know his disbelief to be corrupt (he thinks it is good), he cannot be the one who made it corrupt. Hence, it must be Allah who decreed and created disbelief as corrupt, invalid, and contradictory. The argument reaffirms that the creation of disbelief in all its essential qualities belongs to Allah alone.

Key Terms

فاسد
باطل
متناقض
حقيقة الفعل
قدر الكفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the disbeliever is excused because he believes his disbelief is true.
Correction: The author does not excuse him; rather, he argues that the quality of corruption comes from Allah's creation, not from the disbeliever's intention.

Checkpoint

A) Because the disbeliever is ignorant of its corrupt nature.
B) Because an agent must know an action's true reality to be its author.

D) Because disbelief is inherently good.

Key Takeaway
Allah alone creates the corrupt nature of disbelief; the disbeliever cannot create it because he is unaware of its true reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you ever quietly credit yourself for its goodness? This lesson shows even the quality of belief and disbelief comes from Allah. Before your next prayer, pause and ask Allah to create sincerity in your heart—do you trust that only He can make your worship true?
?
The disbeliever could not change the corrupt nature of his disbelief because he did not know its reality. What sin in your life do you still rationalize as 'not that bad'? Could it be that you, like the disbeliever, are blind to its true corruption? Will you ask Allah today to show you your faults as they really are, so you can repent from them?

The Analogy of Knowledge and Power
Ash'ari refutes independent human action via analogy with knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ash'ari uses an analogy between knowledge and power to refute the claim that humans have independent ability to act.

Core Idea
Claiming independent human power is like claiming independent knowledge — both make us equals to Allah.

Ash'ari presents a powerful analogy to counter the idea that human actions are not created by Allah. He begins with a Quranic reference and then draws a parallel between knowledge and power. The argument is simple yet profound: if humans could do something Allah did not decree, they would have a power Allah does not, which is impossible. Let's read the passage carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the literal translation. Pay attention to the logical flow from deeds to the analogy.
Notice the repeated structure: 'Whoever claims... has given them...'
2
Identify the analogy between knowledge and power
Ash'ari argues that just as claiming humans know what Allah does not know makes them equal to Allah in knowledge, claiming they have independent power makes them equal in power.
This is the core refutation: both claims lead to shirk in attributes.
3
Understand the theological conclusion
The passage ends with an exaltation of Allah above such falsehood. Understand that the argument does not deny human responsibility but refutes independent power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو كانت عبادتهم للأصنام من أعمالهم كان ذلك مخلوقاً لله، وقد قال الله تعالى: جَزَاء بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الأحقاف : ١٤] يريد أنه تعالى يجازيهم على أعمالهم، كذلك إذا ذكر عبادتهم للأصنام وكفرهم بالرحمن، ولو كان مما قدروه وفعلوه لأنفسهم لكانوا قد فعلوا وقدروا ما خرج عن تقدير ربهم وفعله، وكيف يجوز أن يكون لهم من التقدير والفعل والقدرة ما ليس لربهم؟ فمن زعم ذلك فقد عجز الله عز وجل، تعالى الله عن قول المعجزين له علواً كبيراً . ألا ترى أن من زعم أن العباد يعلمون مالا يعلمه الله عز وجل، لكان قد أعطاهم من العلم ما لم يدخل في علم الله، وجعلهم الله نظراء، فكذلك من زعم أن العباد يفعلون ويُقَدِّرُوْنَ مَا لَم يُقَدِّرْهُ، وَيَقْدِرُونَ على ما لم يقدر عليه، فقد جعل لهم من السلطان والقدرة والتمكن ما لم يجعله للرحمن، تعالى الله عن قول أهل الزور والبهتان والإفك والطغيان علواً كبيراً .
If their worship of idols was from their deeds, that would be created for Allah, and Allah Almighty said: 'A reward for what they used to do' [Ahqaf:14] meaning that He rewards them for their deeds. Likewise, when He mentions their worship of idols and their disbelief in the Most Merciful, and if it was from what they decreed and did for themselves, they would have done and decreed what is beyond the decree of their Lord and His action. How can it be permissible for them to have from decree, action, and power what their Lord does not have? Whoever claims that has rendered Allah incapable, exalted is Allah above the words of those who render Him incapable, a great exaltation. Do you not see that whoever claims that the servants know what Allah Almighty does not know, he would have given them knowledge that did not enter into Allah's knowledge, and made them equals to Allah? Similarly, whoever claims that the servants do and decree what He has not decreed, and have power over what He has no power over, has given them authority, power, and ability that He did not give to the Most Merciful. Exalted is Allah above the words of the people of falsehood, slander, fabrication, and transgression, a great exaltation.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a proof by analogy refuting the view that human actions are not created by Allah. The author begins by referencing Quranic verse (Ahqaf:14) which speaks of rewarding deeds, showing that deeds are attributed to humans. However, if humans truly performed those deeds independently, they would be decreeing and acting beyond what Allah decreed and did. That would imply they have a power and decree that Allah does not possess, which is impossible. The author then draws an analogy with knowledge: claiming that humans know what Allah does not know would make them equal to Allah in knowledge. Similarly, claiming they have independent power over actions makes them equal to Allah in power. The conclusion is that such claims are tantamount to rendering Allah incapable and ascribing partners to Him. The passage ends with an exaltation of Allah above such falsehood.

التقدير
الفعل
القدرة

السلطان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument denies that humans have any role in their actions, thus negating moral responsibility.
Correction: The argument does not deny human responsibility; it refutes the idea that humans have independent power to act without Allah's creation. Moral accountability remains because actions are still attributed to humans as their acquisitions.

Checkpoint
What analogy does Ash'ari use to refute independent human power?
A) The analogy of creation
B) The analogy of knowledge
C) The analogy of reward
D) The analogy of speech

Key Takeaway
Claiming that humans have independent power over their actions implies they are equals to Allah, which is impossible and refuted by the analogy with knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever act as if you have control over outcomes that only Allah should decree? Consider a time you felt proud of your own planning. How does this passage expose that pride as a form of claiming power that belongs only to Allah?
?
If you truly believed that every action you do is under Allah's decree and not independent, how would your fear of Him change? Would you still sin casually knowing He is the one who decrees and has power over all? What does your current behavior reveal about your belief?
?
The analogy with knowledge is striking: claiming to know something Allah doesn't know is clearly shirk. But claiming power over your own actions might be more subtle. Ask yourself: In what area of your life do you feel you have 'done it yourself' without relying on Allah? Repent from that subtle idolatry.

The Kafir's Disbelief as Created Evil: Ash'ari's Dialectical Argument
Ash'ari argues that the kafir's act of disbelief is created by Allah as corrupt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ash'ari's argument that the kafir's disbelief is created by Allah as corrupt, based on the principle that an action's true agent must know its true nature.

Core Idea
Only Allah can create disbelief because the kafir does not know its evil.

In this passage, Imam Ash'ari employs a dialectical question to challenge those who claim humans create their own actions. He asks whether the kafir's act of disbelief is corrupt and contradictory. When the opponent agrees, Ash'ari exposes a logical inconsistency: the kafir himself believes his disbelief is good. From this, he derives a powerful principle that leads to the conclusion that Allah alone is the creator of disbelief as evil.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Notice the question-and-answer format.
This is a typical Ash'ari dialectical style.
2
Understand the initial question
Ash'ari asks: Is the kafir's act of disbelief corrupt, invalid, contradictory? The opponent must agree if they accept the obvious reality.
3
Identify the contradiction
If the act is corrupt, how can the kafir believe it is good? Ash'ari points out the inconsistency between the act's true nature and the agent's belief.
4
Grasp the principle
Ash'ari states that an action is truly an action only from one who knows its true reality. This is a key epistemological principle.
5
Draw the conclusion
Since the kafir does not know the true evil of his disbelief, he cannot be its real agent. Therefore, Allah must be the one who created disbelief as it truly is—corrupt and invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٥٩- مسألة : ويقال لهم : هل فعل الكافر الكفر فاسداً باطلاً متناقضاً؟ فإن قالوا: نعم . قيل لهم : وكيف يفعله فاسداً متناقضاً قبيحاً، وهو يعتقده حسناً صحيحاً أفضل الأديان؟ وإذا لم يجز ذلك ؛ لأن الفعل لا يكون فعلاً على حقيقته إلا ممن علمه على ما هو عليه من حقيقته، كما لا يجوز أن يكون فعلاً ممن لم يعلمه فعلاً، فقد وجب أن الله عز وجل هو الذي قدر الكفر وخلقه كفراً فاسداً باطلاً متناقضاً، خلافاً للحق والسداد .
Question 259: And it is said to them: Is the act of the disbeliever in disbelief corrupt, invalid, and contradictory? If they say: Yes. It is said to them: How does he do it as corrupt, contradictory, and ugly while he believes it to be good, correct, and the best of religions? And if that is not possible, because an action is not an action in its true reality except from one who knows it as it truly is, just as it is not possible for it to be an action from one who does not know it as an action, then it is necessarily the case that Allah Almighty is the One who decreed disbelief and created it as disbelief, corrupt, invalid, contradictory, contrary to truth and rectitude.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical argument (مسألة) in which Ash'ari questions the opponent about the nature of the kafir's act of disbelief. First, he asks whether the kafir's act of disbelief is corrupt, invalid, and contradictory. If the opponent agrees, Ash'ari then points out the inconsistency: the kafir himself believes his disbelief to be good, correct, and the best of religions. How could he perform an action as corrupt and ugly while holding such a belief? Then Ash'ari lays down a principle: an action can only truly be performed by someone who knows its true reality. Since the kafir does not know the true evil of his disbelief (he thinks it is good), he cannot be the real agent. Therefore, Allah must be the one who decreed and created that disbelief as it truly is—corrupt, invalid, and contradictory. This refutes the view that humans create their own actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That this argument means the kafir is not responsible for his disbelief.
Correction: Ash'ari does not negate human responsibility; he affirms that Allah creates all actions, but humans acquire (kash) them and are accountable.

Checkpoint
What principle about actions does Ash'ari use to argue that Allah creates disbelief?
A) Actions are created by their doer
B) An action can only be done by one who knows its true nature
C) Actions are good or evil by nature
D) The kafir acts out of ignorance

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari's dialectical argument demonstrates that only Allah can be the true creator of disbelief because the kafir lacks knowledge of its true evil nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time you persisted in a sin because you convinced yourself it was permissible or even good. How does Ash'ari's argument strip away that self-deception and force you to see the act as it truly is before Allah?
?
If only Allah truly knows the reality of your actions, how does that transform the way you evaluate your own deeds? Are you more concerned with how others see you or how Allah sees you?
?
Ash'ari says the kafir cannot be the true agent of disbelief because he doesn't know its evil. What does this mean for your own negligence in seeking knowledge? Are you acting as a true agent in your obedience, or are you blindly assuming your actions are good?
